O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	 O you, very dear son, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine along with its completion, and I have made the end through its explanations and by its clarifications.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	 And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	 And because the work of hands is lacking in our region and is foreign from beginning to end, the knowledge has perished and decayed, and nothing remains of it except for small descriptions in the books of the ancients which have been changed by hand.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	 And from this come errors and vanities, and intentions are closed off, and knowledge is distanced.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	 Or it seems to me that I wish to bring life together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of explanation, declaration, and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	 And I will bring together the forms of the fire tongs for cautery, and of the other instruments of the work with the arrangement of the declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	 And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	 And it is necessary for those who undertake this to be proficient in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that they know the arrangement of the members, and their shapes and connections and separations, and have knowledge of the bones and nerves and muscles and the number of holes, and the movement and rest of the veins, and the place of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	 And therefore Hippocrates said that the name with the name is very much, but with the work it is little;
et meismement en l’art de main.	 and likewise in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	 In the beginning of this book we tell you that if one is not knowledgeable about the aforementioned things, let him beware lest he fall into error and harm men;
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	 So I have seen many times that some who engage in this science abandon their knowledge and judgment through experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	 For I saw a foolish physician who cut an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and also cut the arteries of the neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	 causing so much blood to come out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	 And I saw another physician who removed a stone from an old man, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	 and he carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	 And I had already been called to remove it, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well if one cut it off he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	 And I saw another physician who took into his care a duke of our land whose leg was broken and had an open wound; ‌
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	 and the ignorant physician, using strong force, sets the fracture on the wound of the stars, leaving no trace of flesh on the wound, and leaves it thus unfinished.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	 and he ordered that she not be released at all;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	 and so it remained until the leg was completely swollen, along with the foot, which became gangrenous.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	 I was called to come to him, and I hurried to go and release the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	 and when I had released it, she found peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	 But still, corruption was already established in the limb, and it could not be healed.
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	 and the corruption did not stop spreading through the limb until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	 And I saw another physician who pierced an abscess and then ignited it due to the wickedness of his practice.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	 Because when a cancer is purged of black bile, it should not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place that all the corruption can be completely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	 Et pour cela, très cher fils, il vous est nécessaire de savoir que l'œuvre des mains est divisée en deux parties :
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	 et oevre ou n'est pas de peril, ne de danger.
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	 Et ou il n'a mie paor ne peril, mais ou il est biaus et saluables.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	 car mult es garceus qui n'ont pas l'art, mais se font savoir, et font plusors mauvaises oevres, einsi comme il n’i aient mie, por ceu que il n'entendent mie les choses.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	 et li pueples vous aimera por vos bons fais, si que nus ne puet faire mesque bonnes oevres.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	 And let the frightening diseases go away from serious illness;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	 And remove your weapons from those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	 Galen says in some of his warnings:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	 “Do not take on the care of serious illnesses, lest you be called a foolish physician.”
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	 The first chapter is about fire cautery and hot medicinal cautery, and this chapter is arranged from the head to the feet;
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	 And of the shapes of the instruments, and the handling of the cautery, and of all that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	 The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cups [for bloodletting], and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things. ️
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	 And this chapter is organized and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	 The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	 And it is organized from the head down to the feet, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	 Thus, as we remember the work, it is necessary for me to speak of the quality of the help and of the harmfulness of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	 I say that the qualities of aid, and of harm, is the longest speech and the most subtle science and secret response;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	 And on this many of the wise have spoken, and they agreed upon it.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	 And I am ashamed of my words, for I fear length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	 I say that cautery universally helps all complexions where there is matter, except two complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	 That is to say, hot complexion without matter, and dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	 In a hot and dry constitution together with matter, some have said that fire cautery is of great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	 And others say the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	 That fire cautery does not benefit diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	 For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to treat hot diseases by heat, nor dryness.
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	 And those who say the opposite claim that fire cautery greatly helps hot and dry diseases that occur in the human body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	 For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	 And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	 For I have found it true by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	 Nevertheless, no one should interfere with it except for those who have experienced it, and know through long practice the chapter on fire cautery, and the diversity of human constitutions, and the predispositions and causes of their diseases, and the occurrences and the passage of time;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	 des autres complexions n’avons nous point peur, principalement en maladies froides et humides.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	 And all the doctors gathered and agreed on the use of cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	 And know, son, that cautery with fire is one of the secrets of healing, and more beneficial than cautery with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	 For fire is simple, and does not spread to any other member except the one that is burned, unless it can.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	 The hot medicines spread from one member to another and cause serious illness in the affected member;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	 And perhaps kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	 The fire, due to its power and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	 And this I have found through experience and the length of my service and study in the art, which is based on the truth of things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	 And for this reason I apologize for the length of my speech, because it is not pleasing to me that I should reveal the secret which lies in fire and the quality of the work, how it removes diseases from the body, as the philosophers say when they demonstrate.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	 Or receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	 Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prietens.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	 And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because the harm that occurs is suppressed by the help of cautery;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	 and especially if the cautery is necessary to alleviate pain quickly, before the time when greater harm may come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	 And never think of it like this, dear son, as foolish doctors do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	 because the disease that is healed by cautery does not recur;
et il le dient ensi;	 and they say it like this;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	 but it is not as they think, because cautery is only a medicine that changes the temperament, and dries up the humors which cause pain, and is more effective than medicine for its quick action, and for the power of its work and its dominance.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	 And it is possible that the illness may come sometimes according to the temperament of the patient and the place of the disease and its power.
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	 And the superfluous substances are gathered in him by the consumption of food and similar things, unless there are cauteries administered in places where there is little superfluity and moisture, such as dental cauteries for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	 but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	 And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the last resort of medicine, and that is true.
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	 but they do not believe that cauteries are worthwhile after medication, but their intentions are false; and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of cures in some illnesses and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	 Then it is clear that cautery is the last resort in medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	 The ancients said that cauteries of gold instruments are more beneficial than those of iron, and they only said this because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	 and they said that the place of cautery does not cause putrefaction, but this is not true because I have tested it and found that it is true in some men;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	 and gold cauteries are more beneficial than iron ones, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	 And yet when you heat a gold instrument, you cannot tell when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools down quickly;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	 and if one heats it too much;
si font au feu;	 it melts in the fire.
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	 And thus there are many hindrances.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	 And for this reason, we use fire cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	 I have arranged this chapter from the head to the feet so that it may be easier to find the path.
dou cautere olivaire	 of olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	 This cautery is used for moisture and coldness of the brain, and there are two types done for this reason: one caused by an illness called "soda," and another caused by many humors descending from the head to the eyes, ears, and due to excessive dreaming, toothache, sore throat, and especially all illnesses that come from coldness such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	 The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged with a solvent medicine, cleansing three or four times, according to what the patient's strength, age, and habit allow.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	 And then make the patient’s head bald.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	 And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on his knees;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	 after that, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes.
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	 And there, where your fingers will be, cause the blood to flow first; then heat the cautery which is called "olivare," and this is its form.
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	 And place it on the designated spot with ink, and make descending and constricting your hand little by little while turning;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	 then lift your hand immediately, and return to the spot if you see the bone move slightly;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	 and if you do not see it, then begin the cautery again until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	 after that take a little bit of silk, and put inside soft cotton, and place it on the spot, and let it remain for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	 then apply a moistened cloth in butter;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	 and leave it until the burn is healed;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmacon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	 And it was said by the ancients, that when the wound remains open longer, it drains more.
et por ce si aide mues.	 and therefore such movements are helpful.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	 And some of them said that one should let the cautery burn until part of the bone is burned, and then scrape off what has been burned from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	 And others say that one should let the cautery stay so long, and push it in so hard that one digs into the bone as wide as a spindle that women put in their distaffs, so that the humors may be moved out.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	 and one should let the wound remain open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	 afterwards, one should cure and sew it up.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	 And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in every way, except for certain people where there is fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	 and it seems to me that I should leave it alone.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	 car the head is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we have seen in other members;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	 and likewise when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more safe and beneficial for me, I use this work together with healing.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	 of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	 When chronic pain comes to the whole head and lasts a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie", and of purging the head and oils and plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	 and if one makes the cautery that we have said before, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	 Take care if the head of the patient is very strong by nature, and if it is too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	 Then cauterize under that cautery with a little bit that we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	 Then make a cautery on top of each horn of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery in the place that is called "vessels".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	 And this is the place where one applies cupping glasses.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	 And lift your hand so that you do not see the bone at all:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	 The patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere.
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	 And the cauteries of the horns should be more subtle than those used to cauterize the middle of the head, and this is its form:
dou cautere dou chief	 of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	 When a sudden pain comes in one part of the head and the illness extends to the eye, and the eye is purged by purging medicines, and other cures that I have mentioned in the division of illnesses are done, and none of this helps:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	 then he makes cauterizations according to two methods, that is to say with liquid medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	 The cautery with liquid medicine is done by taking a cup of aloes, removing the bark and pouring the cup into two cups of water. Then make an incision in the place where the pain is such that you can respond to the aloe juice under the skin;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	 and when it has been applied, then bind it well and leave it thus for twelve hours.
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	 And then unbind it and draw out the aloe juice, and leave the wound thus for two days or three.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	 Then apply a cloth soaked in butter on top until the pustule emerges.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	 After the treatment of swelling until it is healed;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	 and if you see this, make some of the burning medicines that I have written in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	 The iron cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Heat the cautery of whatever shape it has.
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	 And it is called "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a nail with a hole for a pin, and in the middle there is a small opening.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	 and place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand and turn the iron a little lightly, until half the thickness of the cure is burnt.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	 and lift your hand so that the part outside does not burn, and let there be an abundance of blood flow out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	 Afterwards, place cotton in vinegar, and put it on the spot for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then I place moistened cotton in butter, and then cure the swollen area until it is healed.
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	 and if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery that is called "cutting," do so at the tip, and be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	 of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	 When you cure a migraine as we have said before in the division of diseases, and it does not benefit, and you see that the previously mentioned cautery of medicine and iron does not suffice, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery called "cutting" until it is white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	 and thus on the painful place a line of half two in length, and remove your hand once, and hold it so that you do not cut the artery and do not come to the bone.
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	 And guard against the jawbone that moves when eating, and the nerve should not be regarded so that it does not move or cause spasm in the patient, and guard against bleeding from the artery when it is cut, where there is great fear in the cutting, and likewise for those who are unfamiliar with it and are not students or experienced.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	 And leave the work halfway;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	 But I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it belongs in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 And if you see that this cautery is not sufficient for the illness, and the patient can endure it, cauterize in the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	 And if you see, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on artery extraction, along with a cautery that has two knives.
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	 And this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	 of the earache from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	 When there is ear pain from cold, and one has tried medicinal solutions and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery which is called "puncture", of which here is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	 Then prick all around the sick ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move a little above the root of the ear after you have marked the place.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	 And let there be ten pricks around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterwards, treat the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	 Of the mouth's torment
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	 The torture that must be cured by cautery comes only from those caused by phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases.
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	 And do not perform cautery on similar ones that come from drying out or numbness of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	 When you cure this kind of torture that comes from fever of the liver and purgings of the head and gargling, and it is not effective, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three cauteries:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	 one at the root of the ear, and another a little below the temple, and the third between the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	 and place the cautery in the part that appears healthy, and have him cauterized at the top of the ear above a little below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as a finger.
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	 and let the cautery remain until half of the head is burnt;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	 And it resembles the knife that we have placed before, but it is a little more subtle and it is necessary for the knife to be a little larger;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 after curing the place as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	 When the apoplexy is old and you cure it as we have said, and it does not help, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	 Two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one in the place called "vessels" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	 And let it be treated as we have said before.
de litargie	 of lead
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	 For this disease, one must give the patient large doses of purgative pills to cleanse the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	 then wash the patient's head thoroughly, and place on the back of his neck a mustard plaster as described in the treatise on plasters;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	 and this is the way to apply the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	 If you do so as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	 If he is healed in this way, it is good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	 and if he is not, let him make three cauteries on the head, descending to the neck, with two fingers' width between each cautery;
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	 and treat it as the others, and if you see a swelling, and the patient is tolerant, make one cautery in the middle;
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if necessary, two more on the two horns, and care for it until it is healed.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	 And let the cautery be called an "olivare," as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	 of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	 It is necessary that the head be cleansed of hair and what we have said before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	 after shaving the patient's head, then make a cautery in the middle of the head and on each horn, one behind and three on the spine of the neck.
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	 And if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is able to endure it, and the disease is severe, then make four cauteries on the spine of the back.
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	 And let it burn until the most of the heart (wound) is burnt, and then lift your hand.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	 Aprés le cure tant qu'il soit sanéz, et soit li cautères qui est apelez "olivare" que nos avons devant dit.
de l’epilempsie	 of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	 The epileptics should not use the cautery except those who are phlegmatic, and it is first necessary to purify the brain with years and other cures that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is great and willing to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	 Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	 aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	 If the patient is a child, perform the subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	 When due to melancholy the superfluities or corrupt moisture and thick phlegm are present, then use the cautery of hot irons as we have said for those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	 And if due to melancholy the superfluities are inclined towards melancholy and the body of the patient is moist, then give him something to drink that will cleanse his brain according to what was previously mentioned in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	 After lifting the head of the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	 then make a good linen tourniquet, like a circle, and place it on the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	 and let the patient sit cross-legged, and be well held from all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	 then bring the linen cloth, and use old sheep butter for it; ›
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	 and heat with gentle fire, so that the two may be poured into it without harming.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	 then empty the circle inside the head, and let it cool down;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and do this to the patient once every week with other good treatment until he is cured.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	 In performing cautery, make several incisions throughout the entire cautery process.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	 This method of moist heat balances the brain equally; › ›
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	 And then apply cotton soaked in butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	 from the fear of pain
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	 When fear first comes to the eyes due to the signs I mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something that cleanses the head, and guard it from all moisture, and make them sweat in a bath several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	 After that, instruct him to turn his head back, and make a cautery in the middle of his head, and make two cauteries on both temples if the descent is in both eyes together, or one if it is in one.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	 and cut all the veins and arteries that are beneath the skull, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temples.
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	 And beware of excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, staunch it with such power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	 And I will teach you in the extraction of the artery and at the incision, the precaution with which you will staunch it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	 And sometimes one performs cautery or hot iron underneath the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	 from the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	 When tears from the eyes are old and habitual and are on the veins, or near the arteries that appear on the outside of the head;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	 And if it is seen that this is from cold phlegmatic excesses, then make the cautery that I have mentioned at the beginning of the eye, descending to the eyes.
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	 I make a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two hot iron cauteries underneath the two bones.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	 And if more is needed, then cauterize it wisely above the eyebrows with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	 from the body tears inside the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	 When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and he does not benefit from it at all, then give the patient three nights of cooked barley.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	 And after the king, the head, and he performs a cautery in the middle of the olive-shaped burn.
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	 And makes two cauteries of the type called "clavilis" on the two sore spots, a little below the eyebrows.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	 And beware of the artery so that you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	 And this is the form of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	 When the eyelid of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery which is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	 To what form here is this?
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	 And if you see this, make two cauteries on the two sore spots as long as the sore spots are.
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And do not leave your hand there except until a third of the skin is burnt, as I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	 The hair that stings the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	 Sometimes it happens that the hair of the eye is turned toward the eyelid and pricks the eye, and in this case one makes cauteries in two ways:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	 This is to say by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	 Or instruct the patient that he should let the hairs grow long and even.
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	 And if they prick at their base, let him hold his eyes still so that they do not move until they are born.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	 When they are born and are even, then put the patient in your health.
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	 After that, on the skin of the eyes place a figure that is like the leaves of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs. PERTY
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Then put a piece of cotton soaked in egg white and powdered pepper on the eye, then heat the cauterizer which has this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	 After you have cauterized on the face where you have punctured a little at a time many times, let the heart be burned in that spot.
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	 and the sign of the health of the work is that you see the skin drawn back, and the hairs raised to the height of the eye.
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	 then lift your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then put cotton soaked in butter until the burn is gone.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 after the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	 And if after this the hairs come back and the skin is softened then begin the cautery on that same spot again, just as you did before.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	 and if the hairs are lacking, then cauterize until the skin is raised to its natural place, and is even, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	 The burning medical cautery is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow large and even. Then make a form of paper in the shape of the myrtle leaf.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	 then take French soap and alive coal, each one third, and grind them together well;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	 and do it quickly so that it does not cool, then spread it over the form you have made like the myrtle leaf, and place it on the eyelids.
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	 And if the disease is in one eye only, then one should work on that one, and if in both, likewise.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	 and place cotton soaked in egg white under the eye.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	 and the patient's eye should be in your healthy hand, and place your finger on top of the medication, and press one time and lift all the times that the patient feels burning from the medication, for they feel burning as if by fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	 When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine with your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	 And when the biting is over, then lift the skin with a needle, and look to see if the skin is raised as it would be by the constriction of fire or by an incision.
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	 And if it is so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	 If not, then apply more medicine to the place until your workings are equal and your eyes focused.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then place a piece of butter-soaked cotton on the burned area until the heart of the burn is cooled; afterwards, treat the wound with ointments called "diaphenes" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	 And if you need to be very careful with your work so that not even a little bit of the medicine gets into your eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	 And if the skin becomes soft afterwards and the hair pricks inwards, then begin the treatment again on that place which is softened by the skin, just as you did before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 After the treatment until he is healed;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	 and this is the shape of the leaf of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	 And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and in smallness, according to this should be your constraints;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	 and may not be answered the right way to him who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	 of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	 When you cure a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your cures do not benefit, then it is necessary that you make a cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	 Instruct the patient to place his head in your hand;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	 and let the assistant hold the patient's head between his hands in such a way that it does not move, nor remove his head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	 then place moist cotton soaked in egg white or juice of parsley on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	 then heat the cautery which is such:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	 and it is carved at the tip like the shape of a peacock feather, along with the handle being the cautery;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	 If you see it, let it be pointed from one end to the other, and if you see it, let it be like a tent.
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	 But nonetheless, this one that is chosen is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	 After pressing the fistula if it is open, extract the pus and dry it out;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	 And if it is closed, then incise it, and draw outwards from below.
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	 Then place a very hot cauterizer on top, and hold your hand on the cauterizer near the nose below the eye, so that your hand does not slip.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	 And put the cauterizer in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	 If you proceed with the cautery to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	 If not, then begin the cautery again once more, or another one if you need to, and leave it for three days.
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	 after which he puts on a moistened cotton swab with butter, and the care of the drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass without healing, then he puts on a corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	 and the king according to what he would find in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	 And there is a manner of cautery for fistulas that some of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	 Cut into an abscess, and open the place;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	 then put into the slit one subtle mixture of this form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	 and make it in the quantity of one third of a pound;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	 and hold your hand firmly on the mixture, and let the patient not move at all, until the melted lead runs to his eye.
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	 and it is necessary that one puts on the patient's eye a cotton swab moistened in egg white or water.
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	 The arrow sinks so deep into the place of the fistula, and the vein by a marvelous healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	 And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	 If not, then one must administer a piercing to the nose, and return the fistula to the body of the nose according to what is proper in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	 from cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	 Much often happen crevices in lips called "hair", and likewise in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	 When you treat these crevices as we have said in the divisions, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cautery knife according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	 And quickly put it in those crevices until it reaches the bottom.
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After curing the place of the wound until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	 Of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	 When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the mouth, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, afterwards it causes putrefaction and rot and becomes inflamed and turns into a fistula.
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	 and you cure it as we have said in sections, and it does not help at all:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	 then it is necessary that you have the cautery according to the size of the fistula.
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	 after the opening or hole of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the iron goes to the bottom of it, and in the rear place.
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And do this once or twice after the treatment of what we have said for treatment, until it is healed.
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	 and if it is treated thus, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	 and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the rotten bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	 from the movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	 When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and that does not work, then place the patient's head in your lap; ︎
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	 after heat the cautery whose form will come here next in such a way that you place a reed on the tooth; ︎ ︎
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	 and put inside the hot cautery quickly, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	 After, lift your hand and renew the cautery according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	 After, let the patient fill his mouth with salted water, and hold it for an hour until it is rich in juices.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	 And in this manner the tooth that was moving is thus made firm, and the softened gum is restricted, and the moisture that was corrupting it dries up.
de la dolor des dens	 of tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	 When toothache comes from coldness, whether it is true or imagined, and medical treatments are not effective, then there is need for cautery in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	 And cautery with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	 Cautery with butter is such that you take butter from a cow, and put the tip on an iron or copper spoon;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	 After take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a tent (i.e., a needle or similar instrument), and moisten it with boiled butter, and place it quickly on the aching tooth, and hold it until it is cooled down;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	 And thus it often happens that its virtue reaches the root of the tooth; and if you see it so wet, put cold butter on wool and cotton, and place it on the aching tooth, and apply hot iron until the fire reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	 The cautery with fire is such that you should take an iron or copper rod, and let it be thick enough so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	 After heating the cautery, from which the form will come later, place it on the tooth and hold your hand there until the cautery is cooled.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	 Do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	 And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter during this cautery, and then rinse strongly;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 and it is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	 And make a cautery with whatever head you want, according to what you have power [to do];
et c’est li forme de la caine:	 and this is the form of the caustic [substance]:
des scrophules	 of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	 When the scrofulae are of cold and moist phlegm, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the caustic made from what follows is the form, and let it have two openings for the fumes to escape from the other side of the cautery; 》
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	 and place the hot caustic on the abscess once, or twice as needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	 And if the abscess is small, apply a cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it there for three days.
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	 And place a damp cloth soaked in butter over it until the burn is gone;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 afterwards, treat the area with onion and honey until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	 The shape of the dog:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	 When moisture prevails over the channels of the brain, and especially when this comes from a cold constitution, then it is necessary that the patient be first purged by purgative medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	 afterwards, make a cautery at the root of the throat, and be careful not to go as far as the throat, but only a little way.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	 Afterwards, make another cautery at the junction of the neck with the top of the spine, and let this cautery be called "clavicle," from which we have the form before;
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And treat the place as we have said before, until it is healed.
de la toust	 of the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	 When all and the disease of the stomach are from cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or heat, and the disease is chronic, then make two cauteries on the stomach in nearby places.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	 And another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	 And let the cautery which is called "clavicle" be according to the shape that was said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	 And if you see fit, make a cautery by pricking the entire cautery which is called "point" in the form that is shown here before for the disease of the ears.
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 And let there be as many as thirty points, or however many are needed.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	 After curing the area according to what has been said before, and let the cautery be at three times according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	 And because these cauteries are lighter, therefore you make them in three doses.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	 of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	 When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	 Afterwards, instruct the patient to lie on his back and on his side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	 afterwards lift up the heart which is inside with your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	 and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery that has two nerves where it looks like this:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	 and cauterize the heart until you pierce it to the side, and there will be four cauteries together with the figure of the cautery;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	 and because of this, the cautery is made with the three-nerved cautery, so that the figures of the cauterization are six cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	 and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the form of the three-nerved cautery:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	 And sometimes it is placed on this one nerve, for which there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	 Afterward, place the cautery on the surface and grind it with silk.
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	 Afterward, make the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 And if it is dislocated on top, which happens rarely, then make a cautery on the thick part of the cautery, or make many cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 Because the joint is healed and the moisture is removed and the patient is cured.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When in the stomach come coldness and much moisture to the point that it draws from his complexion, and he has many catarrhs, and in the usual manners of treatment he does not improve at all, then it is necessary for the patient to be turned on his back, and extend his legs and his hands. xspace
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	 After this, make three cauteries: one under the heel of the foot by the quantity of a thumb, making the entire cautery flat, and two cauteries on each side such that the shape of the cauteries forms three angles, with enough space between them that they do not touch each other when they drip pus.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 and the cauteries should be so deep that they pierce the two parts of the heart, and the shape of the cauteries should be according to this form without touching each other.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	 And if you see someone cauterized with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	 and he who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and pressing on the stomach at this point according to the quantity that you see of it;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 then cauterize with all the cautery which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Après le cure de la cure que nous avons eue devant, tant qu'il soit sané.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	 When it comes to the liver, pain comes from cold and moisture and great flatulence, so much so that it is removed from its natural complexion by excesses; xspace
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	 and the patient is cured of that which we have said in sections, and it does not benefit him at all, then the patient must be purged on his liver;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	 And make a sign of three cauteries in this form and shape and quantity on the liver, outside the hypochondrium, where the ribs of the man come.
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	 And let there be between each cautery the thickness of a finger;
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	 And let the cauteries be as long as the body, and do not press your hand too much on all the cautery;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	 And only burn half of the cautery, and let the patient stand on his feet.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	 And if he cannot, then let him be lying down, extending his legs and raising his arms;
et c’est li forme:	 And this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	 And if you wish, then cauterize these cauteries with a surgical instrument, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and be careful not to burn all the way through, for you would dry out the entire body.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And let it not reach boiling point, for the heart is very delicate in that spot, and you should know this well.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	 When there is an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	 If it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain, but not too intense;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 And if it is in the membrane, the pain is madness-inducing.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	 And then, when this treatment should be performed by physicians, the patient must lie on their back.
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 And then sign the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a grape, as shown in this figure:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	 And he cauterizes with a cautery until the heart is burnt, and it reaches up to the spleen, so that all the flesh is burnt out.
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	 after the treatment according to the treatment of wounds until he is healed;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 and it is not fitting that anyone use this cautery except one who has studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and through whom many of these diseases have been cured at some point.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Then he can boldly work, yet it seems to me that it is better to leave him alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	 of the fire brand for treating wounds
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	 The ancients said that one must make plasters with cauteries of the roots of aristolochia, and in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	 take a long root of aristolochia, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and let it be as thick and as long as your thumb.
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	 And the wetness with oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize the cautery between the collarbone and the neck, and two small cauteries a little below in the part that is under the beard;
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	 And two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, leaning slightly behind;
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	 And one cautery in the chest, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two at the ribs of the chest opposite the cautery that is between the shoulders;
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	 And do not press with your hand, but make it openly as if smelling.
