Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	 And some ancients said that some people use a fire-cautery resembling a razor, and heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches that abscess;
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	 And suddenly, a pain outside, as we have said concerning the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	 But in this work there is fear that the patient dies immediately or a fistula develops which cannot be healed.
de la mice	 of the bladder
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	 When you treat the bladder disease as we have said in the division of treatments, and it does not benefit at all, then there are three types of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	 Of which there is a manner such that you should make three or four cauterizations, in rows according to the length of the vein, following the pattern of the liver cautery that we have mentioned before;
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	 and do not press your hand over the entire cauterization, and let the patient be lying on his back;

et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	 and lift the skin that is above the vein, or let the patient's hand come towards the left, and let the elevation of the skin be according to the size of the body, and the cauterizations should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	 After that, he pushes in the two burning nerves so that the heart is pierced from the other side, and then draws them out through the cautery, and thus there will be four.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	 And if you see it, cauterize the entire cautery with three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	 Après le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens,
de ydropisie	 Of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	 Fire cautery is not suitable for a patient with dropsy, except in the manner known as "ascytis".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	 When you cure according to the methods we have described in divisions, and your cure does not benefit, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the navel, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the bladder, and two behind the back on the spine, and one in the chest;
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	 And let the cautery be very close to the heart's tip.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	 After that, leave the cautery open to release pus for a long time, and do not neglect the patient's care after the cautery;
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	 And healing would hasten, and the two intentions will be together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	 The shape of the cautery for the belly should be like the one we previously showed;
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	 And the one for the back should be olive-shaped, as shown before.
de l’enfleure des piez	 for the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	 When the feet are swollen in someone who is dropsical, and they are full of yellowish water, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring finger;
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	 And lift your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	 And do not enter too deeply, so as to draw out the watery fluid, and let the cautery be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	 Then do two cauteries on each leg at the little-toe joint;
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	 And the longer cautery should be one under the knee in front and the other behind it, in the middle of the leg;
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	 And leave the burns open for a long time without treating them, until they heal on their own.
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	 after the treatment of other treatments that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	 of the injury
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	 When intestinal problems come from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive virtues in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be treated by conventional means;
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	 and you see the patient suffering greatly and has strong virtue, then make a large burn on the stomach according to what has been said before in the section on stomach burns, in the circular burn.
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	 and four subtle burns around the navel, at each one-sixteenth of an inch, and two burns on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	 And if you see that the moisture is abundant and the patient enduring, then make a cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each eye, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	 of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	 When hemorrhoids are in the anus, one or more, and they are old and from thick, cold, and moist corrupt humors, and they are treated as we have said by division, but it does not help, then perform cautery:
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	 Three on the spine of the back, placed one after another in a triangle, and one cautery below the anus, two fingers.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	 And if you think that his stomach is cold, and the food does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then on the face make one large cautery on the stomach as mentioned before, and another on the liver, and another on the bladder with all the cauteries closed.
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	 And leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Aprés cure, wait until the place is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	 of the skin condition called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	 When you cut a furuncle, heat the cautery that resembles a razor, and then place it all ablaze on the furuncle that has been cut.
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	 And leave your hand there until the cautery comes to the base of the vein from which the blood flows;
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	 Do this once or twice, and if there is much furuncle, then cauterize each one as we have said.
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	 After the curing of the furuncles is beneficial until they are healed.
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	 And if you cauterize with a large cautery on furuncle, it will have greater help.
de plaie mal curee	 of a poorly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	 Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nous raconterons en son leu, si vient tel maladie que ne puet estre sanee fors que par cautere.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	 Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tout une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tout la tente combien elle a de parfont.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	 After heating the cautery that resembles a razor, insert it into the fistula according to the quantity in which the tent is inserted, and start again with the cautery until that rotten and corrupted flesh is burnt, once, or twice, or three times, according to how much is needed;
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	 And guard against stretching the nerves within, and from large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	 if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestines, guard against these places, and do not perform this procedure except on flesh, and know that it is not persistent;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	 after curing the place until it is healed, and if the place is healed, and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the place is completely healed;
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	 and if the matter is not removed, know that the place is torn, and the bone corrupts at the base.
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	 and similarly as one of those which we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	 of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	 When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and from great flatulence, and a woman does not desire intercourse, then you must make a cautery on the kidneys from one side and another with the cautery we have previously mentioned. 
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	 And if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a row, and they will provide greater assistance.
de la vessie	 of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	 When the bladder is soft and weak due to cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then make a cautery on the part above the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, one on the right and one on the left, and let each cautery be as long as a thumb's length;
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	 And make one cautery on the back, or two if you need to;
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	 and let the cautery be cleaved according to the shape mentioned before.
de la marris	 of the chest
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	 When the womb is cold and moist, preventing conception, and the menstrual flow is corrupt and delayed;
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	 And when they come, there is great pain:
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	 Then it is necessary to make three cauterizations around the shoulder, as we have said in the bladder cautery, and two cauterizations on the back;
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	 And let the cautery be made carefully, as we have said.
de la hainche	 of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	 When the mucus descends to the hip joint, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that one thigh is longer than the other when measured together;
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	 and the place of separation is found, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient on the hip joint with one cautery resembling a circle, and sign before the place around the joint as it turns, so that the joint is inside the circle;
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	 And so let the cautery be such as that which has been used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	 And if this cautery is not available, make three cauteries from a large olive, and let the cautery be as deep as all the fingers.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and heal it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	 de la douleur de la hanche
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	 When pain comes to the hip joint due to cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division, but the cure does not work, and the illness is old:
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	 then you must purge the patient of thick humors with stinking pills, or other good similar pills.
Aprés li fai cautere;	 After that, make a cautery;
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	 and the manner of the cautery is according to two methods:
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	 This is to know together with burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	 Fire cautery is done in many ways, one of which is as follows:
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	 that you cauterize on the hipbone three triangular cauteries according to this shape, and make them deep and large, and let there be between each cautery a space the thickness of a finger, and let the cautery be olive-sized;
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	 sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on top of the hipbone, for which there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	 And if you see it, then cauterize with the circle cautery that we have previously mentioned for the hip dislocation.
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	 but do it in such a way that the circle includes the entire hip, and all the bone's surface is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	 And this is the manner in which one proceeds with sciatica, when the pain is located in the hip and does not extend to the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	 And if it reaches the thigh and the leg, make two cauteries where the patient says the pain is located, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers' width, on the left side a little.
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	 And let the cautery be cupped, and let the thickness of the scar be burned;
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if the patient feels that the pain extends to two fingers from the foot or close to it, make three or four cauteries where he feels the pain in the cautery which is called "finger".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	 And if necessary, do more of them.
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	 And if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a cupped or circular cautery, and take care in all your cauteries not to leave such a large scar that you burn the nerves and major arteries, so as not to cause greater harm and constriction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	 And I myself have seen many who have made a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left it so that the leg was completely swollen, and the foot as well, and the entire foot became perforated and corrupt.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	 After a belly ache from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	 And if the pain is in two parts together, make a cautery on one and on the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	 And the wise say in the cautery of the hip, this is the manner: make such an iron and let it be at the end as thick as a penny, or a little less, and let it be between the teeth and from one tooth to the other, the length should be the size of a hazelnut.
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	 And let the teeth be set in two parts, and also like nuts, and there should be a good handle of iron.
et c’est li forme:	 And this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	 And it should be heated until it is all red and glowing, and then put it on the hip of the sick person, and turn it on the healthy side.
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	 And after cauterizing once, cauterize again, and leave it for three days.
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	 And then make a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 after the treatment with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	 Albucasis says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its appearance, and we see few who use it;
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	 And yet this is one of the good cauteries, which can be tolerated where it is needed.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	 The cautery of burning medicine is such that you should make an instrument with teeth in which the margin of the door descends, and it should be made of bronze or iron, one side long, and in the height there should be two noses, and between each should be the width of a finger. etti de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	 And let them be open from within and without, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	 Then place the box of the hip on the patient lying on his sound side, and then press your hand very much on the box of the hip;
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	 Then put between the two circles of hot iron that have been heated in the fire, and leave it there for an hour, allowing the patient to bear the heat and burn of it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	 For it works as if by fire;
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	 and when the burning sensation has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and lift the hip from the soft iron, and leave it thus for three days, and apply butter until that which is blackened by the burn is removed;
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	 And let it remain for three days until the pus exits.
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And this would be the last aid after the treatment of wounds, until he is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	 And if the pain has spread to the thigh or to the leg, make one instrument that will fit according to what you have done in the hip equally;
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	 and this is the way of the hot water, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	 Take quicklime and live coal, an equal amount of each, grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	 where there should be one small hole outside so that the point of a razor can enter;
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	 and place on top of that pot another well-lidded pot, and put alkaline and hot and sweet water on top, until there are two fingers' worth of liquid above the powders, so that you have it well in your hand.
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	 and let it sit until it descends with water and dregs into the pot, then take all that water, and throw it onto hot coals and lime as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	 And then it will be very useful and is administered in many medical works and in the cauterization of other limbs.
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	 For it does the same work as fire, and there are other medicines with which one can well cauterize the hip thus as sesame and honey from anacardium and hot coals with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	 And Galen tells us of a treatment by which a man was healed from the pain in his hip and the sciatic vein, and he praises it greatly, saying that no other treatment was done, and that he was cured after one treatment, and then he bathed as he teaches hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	 And it is said in such a way that you take fresh and dry green vitriol and grind it very finely with a little fat, and put it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is located, and let it sit;
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	 And he lets it [be] for three hours, and by that amount that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	 And then have him enter the bath so that his body becomes slightly warm, and put him to bed, and all the pain will leave, and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	 And know that no one should use such a cautery, except after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	 And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with sheep's wool, it helps greatly.
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	 and the cautery should be done in such a manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	 Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the depression that is between the big toe of the foot and the other one called phalanx.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	 Afterwards, take dry sheep's wool and put it to the fire until it becomes coal, and place it on the fleece, and let it stay until it is stained.
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	 And do so again, and do not cease to do so until you feel by sense that it reaches the hip, and that the pain is relieved.
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	 and this manner of cautery is called "sheep's wool cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	 de la dolor dou dos
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	 Of back pain, whether it comes from falling, or from a blow, or from excessive evacuation, or from something like cold spread matter, none of these is suitable for cautery, except that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	 It is necessary that, after the patient has been purged with foul-smelling pills or other similar things, three lines of incisions are made on the back where the pain is located, each line being nine inches long, and in each line five cauteries or more, according to the strength and quantity that the patient can bear.
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	 And let the cautery be made according to the method called "point";
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	 And if you wish, make three or four cauteries in a medium-sized "clavicle" cautery in this manner.
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	 This illness often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow forehead when they wake up, and fear.
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	 And you will find at the back of the spine, and with us, the appearance that comes over the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	 When you see this, and you want to cure it, then cauterize it with the cautery of that type according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	 So that the cautery burns each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	 And if you wish, then cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery two or three lines wide, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	 After curing the place until it is healed as we have said, beware that you do not administer cautery in a nervous area.
de la dolor des jointes	 Of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	 When pain in the joints is from moisture that has spread to each member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which doctors call "gout" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and cures by medicines cannot heal it, it is healed by cautery in this manner:
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	 make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-sized according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	 And if it is necessary that you make an incision on the sole of the foot, then make a cautery over the entire area called "punctum".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	 And if the pains reach up to the knees and other joints, as often happens, then make three or four cauteries on each knee, in total three or four olive-sized cauteries on each side;
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	 and if you need more, then do more, but do not hold your hand outside for longer than it takes to burn the length of the heart.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	 And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	 And if the pain is in the hands, then make two incisions around the wrist.
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	 and if there remains no pain in the fingers, then make an incision above each joint and on the back of the hand.
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	 and if the pain reaches up to the ribs or the shoulders, then cauterize each part, and take good care of the patient and give them medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	 For if you give him good care and purge the phlegm, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	 de la rupture du sinus
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	 When diarrhea comes suddenly and the bowels descend to the kidneys and this is recent, then it should be that when you see him being treated, he should not eat anything that day.
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	 And that he uses things which loosen the belly, so that the excrement descends from his belly;
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	 after that, make him sit on his back between your hands, and instruct him to hold his arm until the bubbles are healed, and bring them to your fingers, and sign from underneath the flesh onto the bone of the wrist, and all in one sign that is similar to half a circle above the body;
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 then heat the cautery which has this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	 Till he is white and has his hair cut off.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	 Then reset the bubbles in their place;
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	 and the minister should hold his hand until they do not return again.
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	 and work well on the thighs of the patient, and place a pillow and a sheet under the thighs, and another one on the foot which holds his hands.
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	 Then place the cautery on the sign as long as your hand can reach, and hold it straight and steady until you touch the bone. And if you do not reach the bone on the first try, then repeat it again until you reach the bone.
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	 And be careful that the boiling does not overflow when you apply the cautery.
que tu ne le brulasses;	 So that you do not burn yourself.
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	 And so that by this the patient is not burned or any other harm comes to him.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	 And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	 And it is necessary that the cautery for children be subtle according to their size, and also large enough for adults according to their size.
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	 After three days, cure the place of the burn with butter until the scalding is gone.
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	 After the treatment of other wounds until they are healed, and the patient lies on his back for forty days until the wound is well closed.
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	 And it is necessary that his nursing be done for a long time, so that the blisters do not burst when he tries to get up and walk around.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	 And after forty days, when he wants to get up, let him be given a well-made brace and wear it for another forty days.
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	 And let him have good rest, that he works little and guards against overindulgence in drinking and eating, and against too much laughter.
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	 And when he follows this advice, then he is completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	 And I will say hereafter the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	 about the opening of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	 When ulcers appear in other places and are painful, and you see that they no longer grow, do one cautery after another according to its size, and burn the third part of the heart.
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	 According to what we have said;
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	 and any of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-pronged cautery like this:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	 but first mark the place of entry and make a line across the width above the opening, and another one below it, and then keep your hand steady throughout the entire cauterization.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	 But the first cautery is lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	 of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	 When pain comes in any limb, from falling or striking, and this pain lasts a long time, and medical treatment does not help, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery called "poins," and let the cautery be according to the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and its strength and location of twisting and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	 if it is healed from the first cautery, it is good;
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	 if this is not the case, repeat another cautery on top of it, for such is the custom that it must move to the nearby member; therefore, you must perform the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	 of mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	 The humors are sometimes aided by cautery with great help, and likewise the diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	 Cannot you see it being cauterized? Take care if the disease is at its beginning; and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and neither diminishes nor stays, and you doubt that the corruption may spread throughout the patient, then make five cauteries on the head:
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	 I enter the head at the nape, and the other towards the forehead at the hairline.
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	 And two on the two horns, and one behind on the occiput.
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	 And leave your hand in such a way that the cautery reaches the bone, and as much that scabs come out of it so that the fumes of the gross humors can exit from there.
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	 And cauterize on the nose according to what is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	 And if the mixture is spread all over;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	 and it clearly spreads, then you must cauterize with the cauteries that we have mentioned on the head, one cautery on the nose, two on the spine of the neck, six on the spine of the back, one large on the buttock and another nearby, and two on each shoulder.
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	 And two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands.
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	 And beware of the nerves that are beneath the heel, lest you burn them.
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	 And sometimes someone performs cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one on the stomach bone, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	 And know that when you do more cauterizations, the more help you give, and the more it benefits him.
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	 And know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as much as the healthy person feels it, because his body is already completely corrupt.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	 And it is necessary that the cautery be great or small according to the members and the joints, as you will find them in various shapes of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Afterwards, care for the place with flour made from vetches mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	 When swelling comes to any limb and is treated with medicines and oils and poultices, and it does not heal, then make cauteries on the limb according to its size and smallness.
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	 And let the cautery be a little deep into the thickness of the heart.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then continue with the treatment until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	 And sometimes one does cautery both on the hand and on the foot and on the back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed.
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	 nevertheless let no one interfere with it unless he is knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves that move the body.
de albaras	 from the bladder
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	 When the disease called "albaras" is inflamed and medical treatments are of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the thickness of the heart, so that the whiteness is removed and its color changes.
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	 Then take flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of a pigeon and blood of an almond, each one part;
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And let it all be mixed together, and bound with a cloth, and placed in the spot until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	 The cure of cancer by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When cancer begins at the start, and you see it stop, then cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the circumference of the cancer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	 Nevertheless, the wise say that one should also make a cautery in the middle of the ulcer;
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	 nevertheless this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupt, and I have seen it happen sometimes.
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 and a more appropriate thing is that it be cauterized around it, with the cautery called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	 from the swelling that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	 When someone has a disease called "adubelati," and it takes too long to die because of the excess or the old age of the patient when he is feeble (that is, too old) and has little blood, or because of the time;
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	 and you want to hasten his death:
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	 then cauterize him with many small cauteries by pricking.
aprés le laisse ensi.	 after that, leave him thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 For she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 And if you see her pierce through the entire cautery, then heat the cautery with this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 And place your hand in the middle of this disease that is called «adubelati» until the cautery has pierced through to the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it outside in such a way that the course of the corruption is relieved.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the treatment until he is perfectly cured.
li cure dou feu par fer	 The fire cure by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 There is another type of disease called "corrodens," and it is nothing other than a consumption of the limbs, for it consumes the limbs as fire does dry logs.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	 If you see this disease in a place that can bear cautery with fire, then heat the cauteries very hot and large, according to what is needed for the place where the disease is;
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 afterwards, cauterize all around until you burn away all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupt is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then leave it for III days, and place on the cauterized places soft bread with oil until the burns of the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After the cure of injuries producing flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	 And if you see after three days that a scar does not form, it is good;
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 and if not, then begin the cautery again on the place where the flesh has become corrupt.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	 And this disease has sometimes been cured with cold medicine instead of fire cautery;
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	 but nevertheless fire cautery is more helpful, and I have already spoken about the treatment with cold medicine in the division.
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 take what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	 of parsley that grows at the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 Often it happens that on the soles of the feet grows a disease called "closed" according to our intention, and it is a large warty thing that wounds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the cautery for this disease is in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	 Fire cautery is that you heat one cautery as if it were a feather of an owl, and let it be made of good iron so that it can hold the nail on all sides, and that there are subtle edges;
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	 after placing it all hot on the nail, turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the head of the nail;
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	 and leave it thus for three days until it begins to exude pus;
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 then make an emplaster of crushed wild mallows with salt, and leave the emplaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal the place of burning by applying a plaster until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	 And if they are turned outward on the body, and this often happens in hands and feet, then you must apply a hot water cautery.
et est en teil maniere:	 and it is done in this manner:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	 take a reed of bronze or iron, or a quill of goose feather, and place it on the nail and the wart, that is to say, on the pustules and warts.
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	 And place the chain above so that it presses all around, then put a pouch of hot water on it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the chain comes to the root of the nail, and let the hot water find its way deeply to the root;
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	 And let the patient endure the scalding of the hot water for an hour;
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 Then leave it thus, and it will completely remove all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 In this manner, do one after another, until you have treated all those that are in the body, then heal the burns that produce flesh.
li cure dou trembler	 Heal the shivering
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	 When someone trembles from cold of the nerves or from quartan fever or others, it is necessary that you make four cauteries or five on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra;
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	 And in the cautery of the foot, and above the stomach at the umbilical cautery;
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	 it will cause shivering, and will hasten the health from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	 of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 Sometimes appear on the outside of the body, as stinking pustules, which come from large corrupted matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	 if it is necessary at first when they appear to make a cautery above each head of the pustule:
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 a subtle cautery of boxwood, of which the tip is gripped in the fire, or of long root of Aristolochia, or the lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	 And sometimes they cauterize at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow from then on, but the excess which comes from them is destroyed, and they are healed;
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 but this must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	 when the vessel is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	 Often there is a great flow of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or in the incision of the abscess, or in the cauterization of the limb, and similar things;
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	 and it is a very serious matter to stop it.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	 And yet when this happens to someone, then hasten to put your finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it very tightly until the blood is still under your finger, and no drop comes out anymore;
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	 then heat several small and large olive-shaped cauteries in the fire until they are all red.
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	 Then take I, whether large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is cut, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	 And if it spurts when you lift your finger from the vein and the iron is extinguished, then take another hastily from those that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	 And do not stop doing this one after another until the blood is stopped;
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	 and be careful not to burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other evil comes upon the patient;
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	 and know that when blood flows from the artery, one cannot stop it well, even if the artery is large, except by one of the four ways that we have said:
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	 either by cautery, or by extraction when it has not been treated, or by tightly binding with thread, or by medicines placed on that have the power to stop blood;
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	 And let it be tied and bound securely.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	 Whoever will administer clotting by tightly binding with cloths or by placing burning objects on top, or other similar things, it will not benefit if possible.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	 And if this happens to someone and he does not have a mirror or medicine nearby, then he should put his finger on the vein's wound as we have said, and stretch it well until it is sealed above the wound and above the vein;
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	 And do not move the finger, but pour cold water over it often until it is very cold, so that the blood is frozen and swollen and sealed;
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	 and then make inquiries ahead for those who need cautery and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	 Here begins the second book on the cure of incisions
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	 We have told you in the first chapter about every disease in which it is necessary to use fire or burning medicine, and the instruments and causes and shapes of cauteries;
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	 And I have placed this chapter from the head to the feet, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same path so that one finds more easily what one wishes.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	 And before I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for this reason greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	 For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things;
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	 where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	 if they are of such a nature that they become so distressed with their illness that they die easily due to the insanity they experience from their illness, and the severity of their affliction;
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 And one must have fear of these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	 And there are those who give you their mind, and say:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	 “wait, I am cured”;
et li maladie est despitouse.	 and the disease is stubborn.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	 It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put greater consideration on your honor than on your covetousness, and do not act foolishly but wisely concerning those of whom you are certain, and from whom you can take and gain.
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	 and use prognosis and diagnosis in the treatment of your patients so that health may be restored;
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 and this will help you acquire a good reputation, glory, and praiseworthy memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	 Very dear son, may our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to breathe in the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	 Now I have arranged this chapter for you by sections, in the same way as in the previous chapter on cautery, which I have described to you from the head to the feet, so that you may find more easily what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	 full of water from the head
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	 You should know that this illness often comes to children at birth, when the midwife pulls too hard on the child's head.
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	 And sometimes it happens for unknown reasons, so we do not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	 And I have never seen this illness except in children, and all those whom I have seen were hurried to death.
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	 And therefore it seems to me that I should leave the treatment of such cases.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	 And I saw an infant whose head was full of water, and the head swelled each day so that it could not support itself.
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	 And the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture is gathered beneath the bone on the forehead, between the brain and the bone.
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	 And the procedure is such that if the moisture is between the skin and the bone, and the abscess is small, you should make a wide incision in the head.
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	 And it should be as long as two fingers, until the moisture flows out.
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	 And see here the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	 If the moisture is greater, and the abscess is larger, make two cuts in the shape of a cross, like this:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	 And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see the seams of the head open on each side, and the water jumps out strongly when you press it with your hand inside, and this does not return to its place:
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	 then you must make three incisions in the head like this:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 And after the incision, draw out all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	 After closing the incisions with bandages and powder, apply wine and oil, and leave it like this until the fifth day.
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 Then dislocate it, and heal the wound with compresses and dressings, and allow the head to be steadily held, and give the patient dry food of little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	 And another way to incise is that you look at where the pus of the abscess appears, and the gathering of water;
car aucune fois est elle devant;	 for sometimes it is in front;
aucune fois derrier;	 sometimes behind; 914
aucune fois en destre;	 sometimes on the right;
et aucune fois en senestre.	 and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	 Therefore cut where the abscess opens, and the gathering of water, and make an incision according to your ability;
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	 and be careful not to cut the artery;
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	 And let there be a flow of blood, so that the patient dies from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	 with a knife
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	 When someone has a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or the bladder, and the illness is longstanding, and medical treatment does not help, then the last resort is to use cautery by cutting the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	 Therefore, when you see them open, the patient must turn his head backward;
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	 then rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, and then let the patient stretch his neck with all his might against the cloth.
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	 Then look for the vein where the blood beats, and the place of one is behind the ears and is not far away.
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	 Then mark the places on each side, then open one and the other with a sharp spatula of two parts, so that the incision reaches to the bone, and let this be wide at the top.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	 And if you see, insert the spatula underneath the artery and cut above it, cutting also as two must cross each other.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	 And when the vein is cut, then the blood jumps up continuously outward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	 And if the surgeon does not open to the touch, then you must measure the space of three fingers, then sign the cross and cut down to the bone;
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	 and it is necessary to let out blood outside, and this should be six parts, or perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the fullness of the artery;
puis regarde la plaie:	 then examine the wound:
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 if there remains a point on the bone of pus, then cut away so that such abscesses do not form, then apply pressure to the wound and bind it, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	 Of headache
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	 When a chronic headache comes and an acute catarrh due to the moisture of tears, heat in the temples, and old insanity, and similar things, and he is treated by various methods of medicine, and none of this helps him, then we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	 And the manner of their extraction is that the patient makes his hair grow long on his temples, and he attends to the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well with its beating, and it protrudes little outside except in some men who are too cold;
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	 And if it is swollen, let the patient strain his neck with some cloths, then rub the area with some rough cloth, and wash the area with hot water until the blood vessel appears clearly.
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 Then take the spatula of which there is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	 Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then draw it up with tweezers, and separate it well from the tissues that are beneath each part.
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	 And if the artery is subtle, then turn it with the point of the hook, and cut that part according to the quantity of two fingers' width.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	 For if it is not cut, then the blood will not flow at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	 And draw out blood for six times, up to three.
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	 And if the artery is large, then you must tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread to prevent decay before healing the wound, and let the blood flow out gradually.
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	 Then cut the excess that is between the two ligaments at that same hour, and then, if you see, use the cautery blade to cauterize down to the bone until the head is cut.
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	 And this is the mild work, if the patient does not have a fever and has a warm temperament.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	 For the cautery is used to remove moisture:
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	 because it is of greater help against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	 In order to extract the artery, one must fill the place with old cotton and put a well-made compress on top.
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And when they are unwrapped, they should be treated with dry medicines that promote the growth of flesh, and with compresses, until they are healed.
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	 And if without the cutting of an artery as long as you work there, then hasten with the copper through cautery, where you apply the vitriol and hold it in your hand until the blood is stanched.
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	 And if you do not have this [vitriol] present, then place your finger on the spot until the blood is frozen, and wash the spot with cold water until the bleeding stops, and hold it as needed.
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	 And it is better and more suitable for the extraction of an artery that you cauterize the vein with this cutting cautery, in two parts, but let the cuts be well-spaced to retain their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	 When the instrument is too blunt, it retains less of its heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	 And there should be one finger's width of space between the two knives, and then when you have brought the two irons together, and placed the hot iron on top until it reaches the bone, cut the vein in two places.
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	 And let there be a space between the two heads, for it is not completely healed by this cautery.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	 tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	 When tears from the eyes descend into the veins that are on the head of fire, and medical treatment does not help at all, and you see the patient's face turn red, and there is a sensation of cold in the forehead as if shivering;
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.
