And if the eyes are dark and moist to the point that the hair of the eyelids falls out, and the eyelids are heated and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	 And the ancients called it "treatment for contusions", and it is that you make behind the patient who has this disease, the hairs that he has on his forehead, then make three cuts in the forehead equally according to the length of the forehead;
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	 And let one of the incisions be like two fingers' width in the middle of the forehead, descending down to the nose, and the other two on either side of the ribs above the nipples, and be careful not to cut into the arteries that are on the sides above the nipples.
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	 And keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound be three fingers' width across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 And have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping the blood, then apply the sharp instrument from two sides like this form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	 From the incision that is in front of the temple to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	 And peel off all the skin that is between the two incisions along with the fat that is on top of the bone, then do likewise from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove this instrument forcefully.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	 Place in the first cut the instrument that is called "scalpel," which is very sharp on one side and soft, not sharp, on the other; this is its form.
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And place the sharp side towards the flesh of the heart, and the soft side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	 And cut all the vessels descending from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous until it reaches the heart, and then make another cut in the middle slit up to the other side.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	 And then bleed equally, and press the place for the blood taken out.
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	 Then put in each slit a tent of old cotton, and place on it moistened cloths with wine and oil and vinegar, and ensure that no abscess comes there.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And on the third day untie the bandage, and apply a large amount of warm water, then perform the dressing with a basilicum ointment mixed with rose oil, and other dressings used for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	 Of the inflammation of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	 When people commonly come down with an acute catarrh, and you see the eyes dim and small, and the sight weakened, and the lids burnt
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	 and the hair falls out, and there is sharp pain in the head, and the patient sneezes;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	 then know by these signs that this condition and this catarrh come from many veins, and the remedy for it is as follows:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And do this: instruct the patient to shave his forehead, then make a large cut in the middle of the forehead, and another one from ear to ear.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	 And begin with an incision from the left temple to the right, extending to the bone.
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	 and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that control eating.
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	 and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then dry between the two lips of the incision and place old cotton and linen bandages there.
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	 Then lay over it moistened cloths in wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess.
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 When it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until flesh begins to grow there, then treat it with drying agents that cause the flesh to heal.
En teil maniere:	 In this manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	 Take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of resin, and make a poultice with them.
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	 And apply it to these wounds in order to heal the flesh completely.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 Of ear stoppage
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	 Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	 Or seeds, or a creature, or a stone from a mine, or similar things such as iron.
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	 Or seed, like peas, beans;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	 If something is flowing out like water, and similarly things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 Quand quelque chose comme une pierre ou une autre chose qui n'est pas appropriée pour l'oreille tombe dans l'oreille et ne pousse pas à l'intérieur de l'oreille, alors exposez l'oreille au soleil.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	 If you see the stone, if any little drop of violet oil or sesame oil drips from it, then initiate extraction.
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	 and make him sneeze with condiments, and plug his nostrils when he is about to sneeze, and place around the ear pieces of cloth or wool.
et estent l’oreille au desus.	 And stretch the ear outwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	 Often there comes pus through this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 and if it does not come out, then initiate extraction with fine tweezers, of which the shape is described here:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	 If it comes out with the tweezers, that is good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	 if not, then initiate extraction with a fine probe of small diameter; iento 12.
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	 And if it does not drain through the ear, make a tube of bronze and insert the end of the tube into the ear hole firmly. And stop up the ear around the tube with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the tube;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	 then draw strongly, for often a strong force comes as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	 and if it does not come strongly in this manner, then take some birdlime and put it into some pointed instrument, and put a little cotton around it.
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	 then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and draw strongly.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	 And if it does not drain strongly from any of these things that we have said, then hasten to split the ear before a hot abscess and spasm come there.
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	 And the manner of the cut is such that you should first cauterize the patient with the cephalic, and draw blood according to the measure of its virtue. Then make the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fatty place or dependent area;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	 And let the cut be like a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then remove it as best you can, and suck it quickly to your mouth.
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And tend to it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	 And if there are seeds inside and they swell, then administer an extraction.
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	 And if it cannot come out, then apply a thin subtle poultice according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	 But do not do this when you think that the grain is wet due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces.
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 then extract it with fine tweezers and place it in a press, as we have said, so that the extraction may be delicate.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 In the case where water falls into the ear, it is necessary that the patient first uses sneezing-inducing substances, and fills the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And let him lie on his side, on the same ear where the water has entered.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it jumps out due to this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	 if not, then take several stones according to the length of your thumb, light and soft, and heat them a little in the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	 and place one of them into the opening of the patient's ear, and make him sit on his feet from another side, and strike with another stone on top of the stone that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	 and do not stop doing this until all the water has come out, and so it will all come out.
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	 And if you see, take a reed, and put one of the heads in the ear, and hold the other head with fire until the longer part of the reed is burned.
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 then repeat with another reed until all the water has come out, as we have said regarding stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	 In extracting an insect, if it is of small body, such as a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	 but if it is of large body that can be felt, then perform an extraction with tweezers;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	 and this is the lightest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	 In extracting worms infested in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the treatment does not benefit, then you must look at the ear in the sunlight:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	 If there are any openings, draw them out with fine forceps. If none are found, take the cane whose form is here:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	 And insert the thinnest end into the ear according to the intensity of the patient's suffering, then draw out all the cane.
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 Do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	 And if they do not obey and come out, then stop up around the cane with cotton as I have said in the stone.
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	 And if they do not come out strongly as we have said, then administer the distillations that the ancients have proved in the killing of worms, and you will find them in treating distillations.
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And thus drip your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, whose form you see here.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	 And whether it is made of silver or brass, it should have one small hole at the bottom and an opening on top for dripping.
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	 And to press in the distillation, use an iron instrument well-suited for this purpose. If you wish, take a razor and wrap around its point some cotton suitable for this task;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	 then cast your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you wish, into the funnel, with the funnel in the ear.
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	 then insert the razor with all the cotton into it and press your hand gently until the oil is completely dripped into the ear.
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	 And let the patient feel warmth inside, and let the distillation be in a pot heated over the fire before it is distilled into the ear;
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	 and ensure that it is not too cold, for then the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 Of ear stoppage
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	 No child is born without a hole in their ear;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	 and the same thing happens to adults due to clogging of a wound or flesh born inside the ear, and this clogging sometimes goes deep into the ear, so that it cannot be seen;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	 and sometimes it happens that the pot is empty of the hole, which one can see well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	 Therefore, those that go deep and cannot be seen are of serious illness in many ways, and as for the ones that can be seen, it is necessary that you put the patient's ear in the sun;
et regarde dedens:	 and look inside
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 if you see the depilation obvious, then work all this spatula of which is the form here
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	 And let it be sharp and cutting both front and back completely, so that it does not wound the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	 if the depilation is of flesh born or of the body of the ear, then hold it with subtle tongs, and cut gently, so that all that flesh may be removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the incision is deep in the ear, take a fine, light razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	 If you feel the depilation from which the patient feels itching at hearing, prick gently, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 then put in the ear a plug according to the width of the hole, and wet it with Egyptian oil.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	 Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a cloth and soak it in red wine, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on it.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	 And if you see the ear swelling, then remove the cloth and use another cloth soaked in ointment made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	 And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge in cold water and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding, which are discussed in the section on distillations.
de la char des papieres	 of paper flesh
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	 This ail that comes in paper on the eyes when they are wet and then dry, you should remove them with tweezers and scissors, and cut off their root with a small spoon.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	 Then put powdered vitriol on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	 And if it comes off, then cauterize with a fine lancet, and afterwards cauterize the incision well. embre li cauterizeir la place ou il fu remes.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	 And many times they return, when something remains of their roots.
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	 And when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	 et maintes fois repairent,
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	 Many times in the eyes there come things that seem like hailstones in shape and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hailstone," and it is a collection of moisture thick in the eye both above and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	 The operations are as follows:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	 Take care if the hailstone moves from one side to another, and this is easy to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Then make an incision on the surface, then lightly scrape each part, then take it with tweezers and cut it off.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	 If you cannot cover it without piercing the skin slightly, it will not harm the patient.
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 And if the split is large, sew it up with a stitch and treat until it heals;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 And if it is small, do not use any force, for the unguent will restore it quickly and generate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	 And if the stone is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, invert the skin, and stretch the stone with tweezers, and cover and press on one side and then the other;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	 And if the skin is separated by the incision, it does not matter.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	 And when the stone is covered, remove the eye of salted water, and treat the place with that which generates flesh until the patient heals.
de la graisse des eulz	 of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	 Exinach is a grease that forms on the skin of infants more than in adults, and it greatly troubles their eyes. In the mornings, they develop catarrh, and cannot look at the sunlight because tears quickly form in their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 And because of this, they lie on their faces and sleep with their eyelids closed, and the skin under their eyebrows is moistened by the swelling and appearance covered in exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press on the place with your fingers, you feel the bone move between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	 And the manner of working is for the patient to put his head into clean water.
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	 Then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach from each part, then place it on him.
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	 And press with your thumbs on either side, so that the ends of the bones come together in a circle.
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	 Then make in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a cut not more than half an inch wide, like the one made when bleeding a vein.
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	 And cut the skin through until you reach the bone.
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	 And in many cases, bone fragments come out of the cut, resembling a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	 Then extract it all in one piece with a cloth between your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is scattered.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	 And be careful not to push into the cut, so that you do not reach all the way with the spatula to the bone, and injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	 And if the vein does not open at the beginning of the cut, then slightly widen the cut until it opens.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	 Then extract it as we have said, then wet rags in vinegar and water, and place on the spot, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And there are such men who break stones and place them to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal the wound until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it comes to the place of a hot abscess, then treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	 of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	 When hairs grow on the eyelids other than the natural ones and become mature, they harm the eyes and bring about various diseases such as frequent tearing and softening of the eyelids and cataracts, to the point that it leads to the loss of sight;
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	 And the treatment is according to four methods:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	 Either by fire cautery, or by medicinal water according to what is said in the previous chapter on cauterization, and it can also be done by incision and suture, or by hooks, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	 It is necessary that you place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye to your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	 if it is torn, that is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	 if not, then insert a needle with all the thread on top;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	 and let it be at the edge of the paper where the hairs grow near those hairs, and draw the thread over all the paper, and turn it to the razor;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	 then make an incision in the part under the paper, under the hairs, touching the whole spatula, from the large tear duct to the small one;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	 then remove the thread, and place under the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then sign on the paper the shape of a hook, like a myrtle leaf, and nevertheless it is necessary that the shape be according to the quantity that you wish to raise the paper which is divided into all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	 And for such a person who needs it, one should cut a large quantity of the paper according to how the paper is softened.
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	 Then make the entire sputum into two lines that you have drawn, and begin from the large cheekbone down to the small one.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	 And let one of the cracks be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the ointment into one of the two corners of the heart, then peel it all off.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	 Then assemble the two lips with a seam of one needle along one thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and make the excess of the threads on the two eyebrows adhere to each other with some sticky substance, if you know how to do this.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	 And if not, then do not worry about it; leave the stitching and threads for III days or IV.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	 Then cure the wound without stitching with dry and constricting things, for the skin recovers by the closing of the wound and the coming together of it, but stitching is harmful (as the ancients said), and this is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	 And there is another method:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 It is that you trace the skin with a design that resembles the leaves of myrtle, as we have described, in three places that are exposed according to the form that follows:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	 Then cut those who rise to small equal forces according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	 And if you cannot hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with one thread in it, and insert it into the design;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	 And insert another thread next to the large tear, and the second thread next to the small one, and gather the threads evenly between your fingers.
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the leather over which you have placed a patch, as we have said, then gather the two lips of the wound by stitching, and heal it until it is healthy.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	 And if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar comforting ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	 And sometimes it happens that the hair of the skin is turned:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	 then you must use what we have said about the incision.
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 But stitching in one place and another is more skillful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	 The treatment of dogs is as follows:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	 and it is that you convert the paper into a cone and place it inside as I have said, then make two dogs by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatula is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	 and cut off the two ends where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	 then assemble one to the other delicately on top of the paper around the eye, and hold the two dogs firmly from both sides;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	 and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is held will die and become black and rotten, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 If it delays, then cut it with scissors, then treat it until it is healed;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	 And when the wound has healed, and the scab has fallen off, and the hairs will no longer hurt.
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 And this is the shape of the two cannulas that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity in length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	 The work is such that you take a fine needle, and you put a thread of soft and fine silk through it.
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	 Then assemble the heads and tie them together finely, and let the length of the thread be one palm long.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	 Then arrange in the quiver another fine silk thread quickly, and tie the ends of the thread together.
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	 Then let the patient put his head on your shoulder;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	 And it should be in the sunlight so that the work is visible, for this is a fine and small work. Then put the needle all the way into the quiver at the root of the hair, and make it pierce the skin quickly until you draw it out over the natural hair.
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	 Then pull out the hair until it reaches the base, and push into the base that hair, if there is one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	 Then pull out your hand so that the hair comes out completely from the base to the skin with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	 And if the base is pulled and the hair does not come out with it, then you will pull the base from below along the entire thread that you have ordered, until the base comes out of the hole above and you can see it with the eye's vision;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	 then you will pull out the base and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair hardens in its place and the flesh grows back;
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	 And if the hair is small, then take a long hair from the horse's mane, and raise it with that one you leave, until it is lengthened, and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	 of the eye's decay
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	 When this disease called "alecrati" or the purulence comes in the eye, there are two types of it.
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 one is natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it occurs suddenly from a wound, or from cutting or burning, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 And the way to work on it is that you cut through that adhesion, and sever its lips, and put inside linen tenths, and leave it until it heals.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 And it is not appropriate to use in the treatment of it things that dry and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	 For if you do this, then the disease returns worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	 but in the work of softening things, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 and the root of water lily or flax seed should be cooked, and diachylon melted in some of the oils, and wrap it in a bandage, and treat this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	 And the treasure of your treatment is that you take care that it does not heal according to the shape it was before;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	 and this work that we have spoken of is not outside of remedies for this illness, so that it does not return according to the shape it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	 Et la chair qui vient dans l'œil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 Cette maladie, qui est en dessous, s'appelle véritablement «axacrati», et elle est à la fois naturelle et accidentelle.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	 The accident comes from a wound and a tear and a burn and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	 and the way of working it is that you take a needle with two threads attached, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left side to the right, so that the thread comes out in two places on the flesh.
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 Then press the flesh above all the needle, and cut it to a broad spatula shape.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	 And if the appearance of the stone returns as it should be, this is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	 if not, then take a razor and place it in the cleft, and turn the stone, and make two clefts on the side inside the stone;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	 and let the ends of the two clefts be at the two corners of the incision that you have cut, and let them be made in such a way that when they are assembled, the appearance is like the shape of a letter called "Greek";
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	 then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its edges are sharp underneath, following the stone, then join the two freed parts, and sew them together with a woolen thread;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then, regarding the treatment of those we have spoken about concerning softening medicines and tents, until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	 And if the disease comes from a laceration or incision or cautery, then it is necessary that you make a clean incision under the hairs of the skin, according to what has been said before;
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	 then drain between the two lips of an ulcer, as I have said.
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	 and the work should be done according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares an engine with all his power to bring back the shape to its natural form.
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	 and the patient himself, according to what is necessary in terms of treatment and instruments, in various situations.
dou soudement de la papiere	 of the suddenness of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	 When this healing occurs in such a way that the skin above is adhered to the white of the eye, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the tip of a razor underneath the skin, and lift it up;
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	 and use tweezers to hold it, until you cut that which is exposed to the fine spatula, which should not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient cannot tolerate the spatula being too sharp and damaging the eye;
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	 and let your cut, with which you peel off that adhesion, be light, so that the skin returns to its natural shape;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	 and all that adhesion is healed, and sometimes there is salty water in the eye, and it is lifted with fresh water, and with chamomile;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	 Then place between the paper and the eye a linen tent, and put on the eye abundant wool soaked in egg.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And after the third day, use collyrium and suturing instruments until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	 of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	 Know that the nail grows in two ways:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	 one is nervous and similar to hard silk, and the other which is not nervous but is like white frozen moisture, that when touched with iron and tried to clip with tweezers, no one can.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	 And both likenesses begin towards the large tear duct and grow little by little until they cover the entire eye and all its light and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	 And the manner of incision is such that the patient places his head on your shoulder, then closes his eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	 and holds the paper in your hand, then winds the fingernail around small pincers, and stretches it upwards;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	 then takes a needle, and inserts into it the hair of a horse, or cow, or ox, and makes the thread strong;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	 and slightly doubles the tip of the needle and pierces it into the nail, and pushes the needle all the way through, and binds the nail with a thread and stretches it upwards, and completely removes the skin along the side of the nail that follows the vein and the silk from the hair to the root, then cuts off the remaining part at the root of the tear duct with all the subtle spatula and small forces, and leaves the natural flesh in the tear duct, so that through the incision does not come the body's usual tears;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	 And sometimes the nail stretches to the quick, and to the thread, as we have said.
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	 then scrape off all the soft tissue, of which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	 And ensure that the soft tissue does not touch the flesh and break it, and that the tendon is not torn;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	 and after the incision, put in the eye a little of burned silk, and made from lead oxide, and leave it until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then treat him so that he is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	 And if the nail is not prominent and you cannot insert the needle, and the quick cannot enter, often this appearance of a nail is cured with medicines;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	 and they are born as I have described in the section on childbirth. And if you see that it has been covered, then work on the eye of the patient, and take a small sharp spoon according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	 and raise the eyelid gently. And if you see that it does not diminish and the reason presses on, then apply to the eye a collyrium made of lead and red chalk and sal ammoniac, ground together, and bandage the eye until the next day;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	 then begin again with the other eye according to this same procedure, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If there is nothing contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then let it be, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then begin again with the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	 And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid appears in the eye to a great extent, then suspend it with the onion, and cut off a part of it but not all, so that a body of tears does not come there;
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	 Then drip into the eye an angry red liquid made from quicksilver.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	 Of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	 In the eyes of some men there appears sometimes a red flesh, covering the pupil and extending onto the eyelids, turning them outward, and resembling a balsam apple.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	 and the procedure is such that the patient puts his head in your lap, then you work on the eyes, and collect all that flesh into suitable tweezers for this purpose, and hold it with force;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	 then cut off the first piece of flesh, and continue cutting until you have finished, being careful not to harm the eye during the procedure;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	 and let the cut of the spatula be such as we have said in the cutting of the nail and small nails from which one removes a splinter, as is shown in the form following this chapter;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	 and when the incision is complete and all the flesh removed, then fill the opening with oil of celery seed where you drip red colocynth or similar corrosive medicines, and place over it a piece of cotton soaked in egg white, so that it is assured to be warm against an abscess;
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	 and if anything remains there, and the pus begins to increase, and you suspect an abscess is forming, then leave the opening and treat the abscess with soothing remedies for a warm abscess;
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do when flesh is joined in the opening by this means.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	 But nevertheless you must moderate the treatment of each weak opening according to the natural way;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	 And from the way of accident, in ironwork.
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	 and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member can withstand the work.
des voines des eulz	 of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 If they are red veins that cover the eye, they hinder sight and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	 Therefore, first you should look to see if the eye, into which the arrow has entered, is sound, and there is no other disease besides the arrow.
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	 then take the coal in this manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 instruct the patient to place his head in your lap, then raise those veins as far back as possible according to his knowledge, and let the incision be subtle, double, like this shape: ️
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	 Et soit deux fois onze degrés dans le corps, selon cette forme :
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	 then, with the coal, incise those veins subtly and wipe away the blood hour after hour, until you see those veins moving out of the eye;
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	 And take care not to wound the eye with the points of the spatula, and perform this work at noon before the sun, and be very careful in your work so that you do not cut more than those veins.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	 And when you have done this, instill in the eye green and red choler to corrupt what remains of the scab.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if you do not have the power to remove all of it in that hour, then make a poultice on the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is soothed and assured of heat from an abscess, then begin again according to this manner which was before, until it is healed;
et c’est li forme des forces:	 And this is the form of the strengths:
de la fistule de l’oil	 of the eye's fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	 The healer calls "arissati" fistulae:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	 when you treat it by cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it does not heal, then there is pus in it that you must open above the abscess, where it should be removed, and drain all the moisture from there until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	 And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, then clean it with all the instruments whose form I have described here.
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	 and it is called "sharp hook", and it should be made of iron, with a round head, and it should be pointed like a file as it is in the following form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	 And place on top of it the spot of the rotten bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	 And do this several times, then restore the place with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	 If the place is healed and flesh grows, and the body of the wound is healed, and it remains thus for forty days, and it does not reopen and is not suppurating, and no evil incident occurs, know that it is healed.
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	 If not, then there is no other trick than to bring the fistula back through the nasal passage in this manner:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 And it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take a drill in this manner, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and let the shaft be tapered to the end as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	 Then place it on the bone near the eye socket, then move your hand away from the eye into a pouch, then turn the whole forest until it penetrates the bone and the patient feels it because the wind comes out if he holds his hand to his nose.
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	 And then apply dry medicine to the place as I have shown you, and when the flesh grows and the place hardens, the matter goes to the nose.
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 This is a lighter procedure for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	 Of the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	 When the eye is completely open and there is no obstruction or narrowing of the nose, you must bind the patient.
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	 Then heal it, then apply cupping glasses to the temples without pricking to draw out [humors], then place on the eye a poultice made of alum and aloe and incense and frankincense, then press the eye, and bandage with strips of cloth.
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	 And the manner of applying bandages is such that you take bandages soft enough, and fold each one into fourths, then place one on top of the other according to the amount the eye needs.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	 Then hold it in place with a very hard bandage, and resume using cupping glasses to suck without cutting;
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	 Then remove the cupping glasses and keep the eye bound day and night, and if the ligature weakens, it is necessary to bind it tightly.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	 Then remove the bandage after a day and night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good;
se ce non;	 If not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then resume applying poultices and bandages and the ligature and cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	 of the breakage of a vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	 When discharging comes into the soft cloth, it opens, and comes out of the papers like a drop of resin, and it is astonishing to see.
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	 Then if you see it covered, the work is such that you insert a needle into the root of the lower part up to the upper part, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the eyelid;
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	 and let it pierce through, and leave the first needle according to the arrangement.
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	 then cover the place of the double thread and wrap part of the soft cloth around it, and secure it well, then remove the needle and put a damp cloth soaked in plenty of egg on the eye.
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	 And leave it there until the thread and the soft cloth fall off, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed.
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And sometimes the wound is bound with a piece of cloth from each side of a circle until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	 And if the eye gives a great appearance of it, pierce it with a subtle surgical instrument through to the depth of the eye, and let out the cloudy moisture and descend the eye, and insert it immediately.
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then keep it thus until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	 of the white of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	 This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing other than a bubble that forms in the eye, appearing like descending water, but it is not water;
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	 and the manner of performing the work is such that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands on both sides, and move it until you see the bubble rise to your eyes;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	 then it should be pierced through, and not descend, and let the light be extinguished, and may the patient see things as he did before;
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 and if it does not descend below, know that it is acute, and if the descending of the bow is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	 then make the patient sit between your hands, then take a fine spatula and cut into the hard skin at the junction with the hard skin and the horn, until the bow comes out.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 and when it has come out, then drip into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or hot water in which fenugreek has been boiled and honey, then it should be treated with another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	 of the eye's waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	 We have knowledge of the similarities of waters in their division, and those which are necessary for piercing.
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 Perform it according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, out of the light from the sun, and tie the healthy eye shut tightly.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	 Then place the eyelid of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	 Then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right.
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	 Then place the tip of the instrument near the cornea by the thickness of a ray on that white part of the eye at the minor lacrimal duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" vigorously, and turn your hand until it pierces the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty place.
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	 And it is necessary that the measure of the almagda route be at the depth of the measure from the plummet to the end of the nostril.
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	 And this is the crown of the eye.
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 Then you will see the bone in that paper through the clarity of the horny skin, and then place the instrument to where the water is, then press it under one vein after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 If water enters now, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	 After resting a little, and if the water rises up the second vein, place the finger with the instrument, and when it is stuck in and does not rise, then draw out the almagda gently turning your hand a little at a time.
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 And then put in a drop of pure oil, and lift this eye up.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then place outside the eye cotton or wet wool in rose oil and plenty of egg, and bind with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those who are of our time, apply comfrey with plenty of egg on top.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	 And if almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are such men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit," of which here is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	 And pierce therefore only the membrane, and do not go too deep, but make the place subtle, then put there aloes, as we have said.
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	 and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a warm sleeping place, where he sleeps on his back in a dark place.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	 and let him be free from all movements, and take light food, and not move his head to the right or left, and let him lie according to his condition until the third day.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	 then unbind him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and show him some things, and then rebind him until the seventh day.
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 and it is not necessary that you do this in the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you elevate him, because the waters rise quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	 If abscesses come, you should open the eye before the seventh day, and apply that which soothes abscesses.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 And when it is healed, open the eye and place on its face a border to cover for some days, and always keep it in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	 Then leave the house gradually, and turn back to his habits;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	 And one came to us who was from the Yirach, who told us that in their land they do almagda surgery, where water is sucked out, but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients.
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	 And perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	 And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagda, so that he who does not know them may see;
et soient d’arain proprement:	 and they should be of pure copper.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	 And their tops should be of this same subtlety, and the lower part in three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	 Of the flesh above the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	 Sometimes there are born in them various shapes of snakes, so that some appear to have many legs like scorpions.
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 And if there are such [snakes], they may be charmed with the color of fire, and some have a gentle nature of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	 Therefore, for the snake that is gentle and not charmed, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	 and open his nostrils, and throw the onion to those snakes, and drive them away.
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 Pour extrêmement fines et aiguës, et ensuite soutiens la spatule
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	 And if there remains anything that cannot be cut, then open it with very fine instruments lightly, so that nothing remains.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	 And if the abscess swells or bursts before you have completed the operation, then support it as needed;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	 And if it is a malignant abscess, then hasten and cauterize until the pus is dried up and all the flesh removed; then throw it into a well-sealed vessel filled with vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	 If the vessel works, and moisture reaches the mouth, know that he is cured;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	 And if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is flesh born on the bone above, which prevents the instrument from cutting.
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	 Then you should place there a little thick linen thread, and tie it with your hand, and each knot should have between them a finger width or less.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	 And the patient should put the head of the thread into his nose as strongly as he can, and pull it until it comes out through the mouth.
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	 And often children do this in schools, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it.
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 Then hold the head that comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other by feeling the thread as we have described.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	 Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted that flesh, then draw out the thread, wipe off the blood, and dip the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before.
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	 Do this for three days or more, until the ointment has corroded all that remains of flesh;
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	 And then put in the nose some lead for a few days until it is healed, and if there is need for dry medications, then use them.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 And this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, in which one distills the oils and medications into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	 And let it be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and the passage also.
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	 And if you see, make a closed reed, and let the instrument be full to cleanse the head.
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	 And have a handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	 Of the flesh above the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	 Often there arises in the head of the nose a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes very large, so much that it is a visible thing to behold.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	 And for this reason, you must cut it off at the beginning and remove all of its strength, then apply the cautery or burning medicine on top.
