et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	 And if it is delayed in being cut until it is large, then take care if it is hard, of dark color, and poor sensation.
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	 Do not touch it with iron, for it is an inflamed abscess, for when one cuts into it sometimes, great harm comes to the patient.
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	 and if the abscess is of soft touch, not at all of red color, and you see that it can be completely covered, then let the patient bleed and the incision without fear, and treat the place with dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	 When the nose is struck and wounded
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when a solution for continence comes to one of these cartilage works, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	 It is necessary then, when this happens to someone, to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and then join the two lips together in one stitch, then treat it until it is healed.
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	 and if the lips are already separated on both sides, then it is necessary that you burn all their interior parts until they heal, then join the two lips together in one stitch, and bandage it, and powder with dragon's blood and ground incense.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And place on top of the powders a piece of strong or other suture plaster, and let it remain until it falls off by itself, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	 The method of stitching is to bring the wound together:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	 or with needles, as we have said in the case of the belly stitching;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	 or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	 of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	 In the hands of some men, there occurs within the lips a hard abscess, resembling barleycorns, smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	 then you must turn the lips, and cut into each knot, and take it with tweezers and cut it in each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 then fill the place after the incision of vitriol with grease, so that the wound may be stained;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and then apply a plaster of linen, and dress the place with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	 of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	 Often occurs on the gums joined flesh, which the ancients called "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	 so you should hold it with tweezers, and cut it at its root, and let the wound bleed out.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	 then apply on the place vitriol ointment, or other restraining and drying powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	 and if that flesh returns after being cut, which often happens, then cut it the second time, and cauterize it: ︎
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	 If it does not return after cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	 and these are the forms of the instruments to cover (the wound).
des sordens	 of the sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	 Sometimes they are gathered at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough.
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	 And sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish and rotten, to the point where decay reaches the gum, and the teeth become putrid.
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	 then you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head should be in your lap, and pull out the teeth or scabs until nothing remains.
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	 And thus do with blackness and greenness, and with jaundice and other stains, until they are cleaned.
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	 And if one removes what is there at the first reason, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	 If not, then begin again on the second day and the third, until you have everything reset.
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	 And know that the teeth need various shapes of instruments for setting, according to what the work shows, because the file used for filing the teeth has different forms than those used between the teeth.
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	 And these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	 It is necessary that when you cure the tooth of its pain, you delay drawing it out as long as possible, for this should not be done. hline
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	 Because it is a very high substance until one has no excuse to draw it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Therefore, when the patient is forced to have the tooth pulled, you must be certain of the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	 Often pain afflicts the patient, thinking it is a toothache, and he has the good tooth pulled.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	 Yet the pain does not leave because of this, until the bad tooth is removed, for we have already seen this happen with these lords.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	 And when you are certain about the aching tooth, it is necessary that you cauterize all around the tooth as far as possible to protect the gum from all sides;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	 Then move it with your fingers or fine pliers, little by little, until it is well loosened, then secure the pliers firmly.
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 And let the patient's head be between your knees, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, if it does not come out forcefully, then take one of these instruments and push it gently into each side, and remove it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	 And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, then you must fill it with rags, where the holes are.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	 and if you tighten it gently with pliers, so that it does not break when tightening;
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 and you must very skillfully work around the gum to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And take great care not to break it, and leave a part behind, and the patient will suffer greater pain than before due to the evil of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	 And take care not to act as the ignorant healers do, who in their haste and boldness sometimes break the tooth, and do not bring about what we have described.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	 but sometimes they cause great illness due to the roots that remain or because of the tooth they break, as we have often seen.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	 And when the tooth is pulled out, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	 And if blood comes from it, as often happens, then fill the place with crushed vitriol.
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And if this does not work, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	 The forms of the instruments that one uses to pull teeth first should be with long points and thick handles, so they do not bend when you pull out the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	 And these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	 And they should be of thick iron that does not bend when pulling, and they should be well-made and toothed to hold well.
de la racine des dens	 from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	 When the root remains after pulling out, it is necessary that you place moistened cotton in butter on the place for one or two days, until the place is softened, then insert the tweezers called "algefri", so that the tooth appears to be a bird's beak.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 And let them be made inside like a file, and this is the shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, then you must uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and place the instrument called "althali", that is, pincers, into it.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	 And let it be outside and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out from this, it is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	 If not, then help yourself with all the instruments which are used in the forms that follow hereafter.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	 And so one helps oneself with this instrument that has two teeth, of which here is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	 and other iron tools that are at the front in the manner of teeth, and with this instrument that looks like large pliers, whose form is here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	 And let this instrument be outside so that it cannot break, and know that there are many instruments of teeth.
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	 and also other instruments, which are not counted.
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	 and the wise master finds his instrument by himself according to what his work and the illness shows him, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of their diversity and if one breaks the cartilage or other bones, where it can, then he seeks the instruments that are needed, which I have told you about, and helps with the actions, whose forms are here: ️
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	 And let them be thick and firm to hold the bone, that it does not escape, but can be held and removed.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	 And then restore it with the appropriate medicine for this purpose. If there is decay in the bone and it is small, use all these tools.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	 When the teeth appear not according to nature, and the shape is ugly, especially in virgin women, then you should know if the tooth is new after a tooth, and is not in the right place, and one cannot file or grind it.
adonques lou raie;	 Then pull it out.
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	 And if it is caught with the tooth, then take this instrument whose shape is like a small beak and is made of iron at the point.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	 And the instrument cuts little by little each day because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others. And if it appears that it can be filed down, then file it with a file like this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	 and it is like the file with which one makes needles;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	 and with a file the tooth is removed bit by bit each day lightly, so that it does not move until it falls out.
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	 then the plain at the end to any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it wounds the tongue, it is necessary to file away the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not wound the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	 When the teeth become dislodged
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	 When the teeth are loose, whether by striking or falling out, and the patient cannot chew on what he eats without them falling out, and you have treated them with astringent medicine, and it does not work;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	 then they must be secured with a gold thread, for the silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	 And let the thread be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, according to the space between the teeth.
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	 And if you want to straighten the teeth, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then pass the ends between the misaligned teeth, whether there is one or more, until you skillfully reach the other healthy tooth.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	 Then repeat the covering from the starting point, and gently and skillfully tighten your hand until it does not move at all.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 And let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	 Then cut the ends of the thread with scissors, and gather them together, and place them between the healthy teeth, so that they do not injure the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	 And then he leaves it so tight for as long as it can stay in place, and if it dislocates again or the string breaks, then he binds it with another string;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 so that it stays in place and serves him thus for his entire life, and this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of two healthy teeth and two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	 And when a tooth falls out, it should be put back in its place, from time to time, as we have said.
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	 and let no one who is not wise and skillful interfere with it, and sometimes a tooth made from cow bone is shaped, and placed where the defect is, and bound as we have said, and stays and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	 of copper to heal the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	 Sometimes there is this ligament which comes under the tongue at birth.
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	 or by accident of a healed wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	 and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and have their head in your lap, and raise their tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	 then cut the nervous ligament wide, so that the tongue is dislocated from its position, and if there is hardness or a knot, and this is due to the suddenness of the wound, then push in the hook and cut widely that ligament;
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	 and be careful that the cleft is not too deep, because of the artery which is underneath;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	 and when you have done this, lift the place with rose water and aloes, or cold water, then place under the tongue a tent of linen;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 And the patient should shave every night, so that the place cannot scab over.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	 And if a bleeding comes out, put ground vitriol on the place;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	 and if the blood spreads, then cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 then treat it again until it is healed,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	 and if you see it turning black or hard, such that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	 and if it is inclined to become white, with moisture present, throw in alum, and open it with a fine spatula, and clean it from both sides.
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	 And if blood rises during your work, apply vitriol until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you remove all the foreign body.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then lift it up with oil and silk, and care for other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	 of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	 Sometimes there are lumps in the throat called "gland," and they are properly called the two almonds. And when you treat them, as we have said in the description, and they are not healed, take care:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 If it is a hard abscess of small size and pale color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also to prevent bleeding;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	 but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will separate it from there, lest it burst on its own;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 and if it is of white color again, and the root is subtle, then prepare the instrument for cutting, but first look whether the hot abscess rests and is appeased.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	 Then have the patient sit before the sun, and his hands be in your hand, and he open his mouth wide and you take the tongue between your hands, and press the tongue down onto the instrument entirely, which is its form;
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 and let it be of silver or fine brass, like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	 When you press the tongue against this instrument and see the abscess, take the onion and fix it in the almond paste, and draw it forcefully over the top as much as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	 And draw out some object from the cloth with it, then cut off the instrument, whose shape seems like a forceps.
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	 And yet the heads are curved, and one against the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of Indian iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if you do not have this instrument at hand, then take the tongs, of which here is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	 And let it be cutting on one side, and named on the other side.
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 And when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and afterwards gargle the patient with hot water, and cold and salted water, and if blood begins to flow, then gargle the patient with water, in which cooked pomegranate rind or myrtle leaves, and similar things are mixed, until the flow is stopped.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then let the cure continue until he is cured;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	 and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two almond-shaped ones, so cut them off in the same way as the two almond-shaped ones.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	 And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born within her throat, that is to say, one small abscess;
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 and had almost completely closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, nor could she eat or drink, and would have died if she remained in this state for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so high that it had forced out two teeth through the two openings of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	 I hurried immediately and inserted one lancet, then drew it out, and with it pulled out a large portion of pus;
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	 then reattach another part in the other hole of the nose, and he opened his mouth and pressed his tongue;
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	 then inserted a lance into these abscesses, and took out some of it, and only a little blood came out;
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	 and thus the woman's throat passage was opened up, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting into that abscess for a long time;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	 and the abscess would always grow back and fill up the place that I had emptied, until it became very large again;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	 then I cauterized it from within the throat;
ensi demora sens croistre;	 thus it remained without growing;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 And let this body be separated from these parts, and let it be as God made it after me.
de l’uve	 of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	 When the pupil descends to the eyelid and is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular";
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 And if it is below, large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	 When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that this abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then you must cauterize it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	 And the one which is round and assembled and is not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 And it is either bloody or of a dark color or black, then you should avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	 It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner I have spoken of, concerning its brightness and length, that you make the patient sit facing the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument we have previously mentioned.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 then insert the needle into the eye, and draw it out from below, and cut it with one of the two instruments I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	 And you must not cut more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	 for if you cut too much, it harms the voice and speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient is afraid of cutting, then you must use ingenuity in the cauterization to remove their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the manner of the cautery is sharp and keen.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	 And it is that the patient places his head in your hand, and then presses the tongue against the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and burns with lively water, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And use the application of this instrument, which has this form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	 And have on the head a tuft where one places the medicine, as with the hairs of a spoon, and place the instrument over all the medicine on the eye.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	 And let the patient lie on his side, so that the saliva and mucus run out of his mouth with the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and wound.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	 then take your hand and apply all the medication and press down on the eye for half an hour, until you see it numbed and the stinging of the medication is soothed;
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	 and if you see this, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and soak the cotton in the medication, and insert the instrument with all the cotton into the eye socket, until the cotton dries on the eye;
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	 and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and it will fall off after four days or five.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	 And if you need to repeat the medication cautery, then do so, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around the medication;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And let it be washed with cold water, and treated with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	 This treatment is safer than the incision or the cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	 if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take calament and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and gather all of them or some of them into one pot, and put in ashes, and make them boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	 And let the pot be well sealed with strong earth, and within the pot there should be an instrument made like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	 And let it be of silver or copper, and one end should protrude into the patient's mouth until the vapors rise to the eye through the nose, until the eye is anesthetized.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	 after which it often returns, until the eye dries up, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the hot appearance of the abscess, because many things happen there;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 and do not do so when the abscess is cooling down.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	 And if this instrument is not present, then take a reed and place inside it the head of an egg, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 because the eggshell does not allow the vapor to irritate the mouth, and this is a good remedy along with the treatment.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	 Often there are bones or fish spines lodged in the throat, or something similar;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	 so it is necessary that you remove what you can see, and press the tongue against the sunlight with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing move; ὴ
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	 And what does not open to you and is stuck in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	 by chance if the harsh thing comes out through vomiting
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	 or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of apple, or a lettuce root, or a crust of dry bread.
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	 and attach to the sponge a thread, and then swallow it
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	 and when it reaches the place, it will swell up, and then you will pull on the thread 》
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	 and if it does not come out through what we have said, take an instrument of lead according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	 And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it may enter the throat more easily, and let the head be raised.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	 And take care not to touch the epiglottis, so that the whole [throat] does not swell up, and do not push the bone inside.
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	 And it is better that the patient himself inserts the instrument, so that he may be moved where the thing is difficult.
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	 if she [the patient] pushes downward, or draws it strongly through all the instrument equally, until it is strong.
de la sansue de la gorge	 of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	 Sometimes bloodletting is used, as I said in the division, by means of medication treatment;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 and when this does not help at all, then look into the patient's throat in the sunlight, after you have pressed the tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see blood, then draw it with a very small hook, or with fine tweezers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if this does not work, then take a reed and put it in the patient's throat, then put hot iron into the tip of the reed, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And if the patient is thirsty all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	 then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in without choking, and move it about in their hand often.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 And as soon as the blood feels the water, it falls.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	 And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument I mentioned for the fumigation of the egg.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 do this many times, because it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	 And the manner of the fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are live coals, and let it be covered with a perforated sieve in the middle, and through that hole place the head of the instrument;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	 then cast your fumigation into it, and have the patient put the head of the cane in his mouth, and close his mouth so that no smoke comes out, but let it go all the way to the blood;
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	 And the bleeding will fall now, and if it does not fall, then begin the fumigation many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	 And let the patient be thirsty, and eat salty things and the like, and do not drink water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 And then he will need to evacuate it through this process.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	 And the shape of the instrument with which one draws blood is, when it can be seen, similar to curved pincers to enter into the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	 and has the likeness of a hawk's beak, and there is roughness like a file, so that what it takes, it cannot leave.
et vez ci la forme:	 and see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	 the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	 Very many similarities to an abscess are, according to what is remembered here after from one and the other in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 And this happens in two ways, one of which is by its very nature, due to moisture it retains.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second type is according to their location on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 car the boils of the head are different from those of the base, and the boils of the fleshy place are different from those that come on joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	 And so are the abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is mature according to its development;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And so are those that should be pierced when they are ripe, and do not mature according to their development, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when boils come near joints, and one lets them until they are suppurated all around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint may become corrupted, which is why this causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	 Or if the abscess is near the main member, and you delay the piercing until it is mature, it will harm the main member;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	 or if it is near the foundation, then pierce it as soon as it is ripe.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	 And it is not appropriate to pierce a ripe abscess without complete digestion, except for those near the foundation, so that it does not rot inside and become elongated, leading to a fistula. xspace
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 And may not heal within a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	 And you must know the hour of the abscess’s perforation that has matured according to its completion, and this is when the pain is calmed, and the separation of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and from the debate and improvement of the abscess’s head, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	 And you must make the perforation sit in the most dependent place of the abscess, and where it opens, move.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	 And let the perforation be long of the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in the joints and at the nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no folding.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that bend, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in the fleshy part, it is better that you leave the opening until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	 Because if you pierce it before this, the body will be elongated by the poison from it, and it is full of much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 And perhaps it will harden the lips and make them deeper.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if there is an abscess that has been opened according to the width of the body, according to how much the limb needs it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	 And you must introduce into small abscesses, small holes;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	 and in large abscesses, large holes, and many incisions according to the size of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	 And if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cover the heart and close them off;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	 when they have become as thin as cloths, and are dead, then you must do as one does with buboes:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	 And if there are such that are split into three corners, and some that you close as the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the groin; ︎
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 and if it has such [dislocations], when making a round cut, and other cuts and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	 Those who do not have a head, such as a soft surface abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it completely;
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	 and if the abscess is large and it has collected a great deal of pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus at once in that hour, but draw out some of it.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	 then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out more again.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	 do this many times over several days, until all the pus comes out;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 likewise if the patient is of weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or an old, feeble man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the spirit sometimes jumps with the exit of the pus, which can kill the patient, and you may not notice it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	 Avoid this chapter with great care, and when you have perceived your abscess, wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	 And if it is a clean incision, then apply linen bandages or old cotton.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	 And if it is a large abscess and there are many holes, then you should insert a bandage into each one so that they touch each other.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	 And if you have cut into the abscess a piece of skin and have pulled it around, then you should fill it with old cotton or shreds of linen without moisture, and bind it until the third day.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal the wound until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs in your work, then bring cold and easy water, and moisten the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	 And if the flow of blood persists, administer treatment and care, and use the powders that I have mentioned earlier in this book. If it is wintertime and the place of the abscess is very sensitive, you must apply hot compresses soaked in wine and oil.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	 And if it is in the summer and the place is fleshy, you must apply cold compresses soaked in water or wine until the third day, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then unbind the abscess and dry it and treat it as needed until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	 And this is necessary to know generally in the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	 As I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	 of swellings
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 Or when small abscesses come on the head, and are of the same kind as those that are in clothes, just like the eyes of a sparrow, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	 There are some that are fat and such where there is moisture as well as pus;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 And there are those that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the surgeon does not act contrary to this.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of cutting is such that you should test with all instruments called "spoon", from which the shape comes afterwards, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 Because if it contains moisture, then cut through from above the long (bone).
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	 And when the moisture is emptied, then scrape away the skin without leaving anything that contains this moisture, for it always returns if something is left behind.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	 Then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	 If not, in water and salt, and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day.
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 and those will run like one who has stayed up all night
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	 And then resume the cotton, as before, on the second day and the third, until you know for sure that it does not stay in place at night;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then treat the wound with ointment suitable for this purpose, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	 And if the abscess contains thick pus, cut it according to this method, lengthwise;
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	 and throw away your fingernails, and scrape it from all sides, and put all your effort into pulling the cloth where it lies; ️
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the cauterization does not work as expected, then do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And do the same for a pustulent abscess, in cutting and cleaning as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And cut on the pustulent and moist abscess, for it is lighter, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	 And if there are some of these abscesses on the head where there is no moisture, such as the abscess that I cut on an old woman's head;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	 And I found the abscess like a hard, rough, and white stone, and it could not be broken.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if one had struck it, it would have caused as much damage as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	 In other abscesses that come to a head, be it those that come to the heads of children or to the roots of the ears, the opening should always be made in the lowest possible place, so that the pus may exit.
et les cure si com il covient.	 And treat them as needed.
des scrophules	 of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Often these boils occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and are many, and intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	 And each scrofula is properly inside its rib, like the knot and the abscess of the head, as we have said.
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And there are many similarities between these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and some that are malicious and do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	 In that which you see well-disposed to touch, and is similar in color to the body, and moves from each side and is not harsh on the nerves of the neck or on the artery or on the passage, and is not deep.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	 then you must cut it from above, and peel it from each part, and extend the two lips of the heart, if necessary, as we have said in head abscesses.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 and draw a little at a time, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and let the spatula be neither too sharp nor cutting, so that the hand does not slip, and do not push too far forward, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	 And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not stop bleeding, then put in the wound vitriol powder, or some powders that stanch blood, and bandage the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And leave it until the abscess is relieved, and the wound becomes soft, and begins to suppurate.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	 And when the blood has been stanched, return to your work until it is completed.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 Then search with your finger if there remain any small scabs, and cut and clean them off.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	 And if at the root of the scab there is a great vein, it is not fitting that you cut that scab at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it fall off by itself, without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 Then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then bandage it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut out all the scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, since there is no longer any excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 so it is necessary that you attend to cutting the root of it, and draw strongly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	 Those scrofula which hold excessiveness, pierce there where it appears dead;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	 and pierce it as mentioned before, in descending order, then apply tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and when the wound is well cleansed, then bandage it with ointment-soaked meat until it heals.
de squinance	 of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	 The ancients spoke and taught about the cutting of the throat;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	 but I have never seen anyone in our land who did it, and this is a transcription of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	 For those with squinting, it is necessary that the slit of the throat called "epiglottis" be cut.
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	 and one should not help with this, because all the veins and the throat of the patient are affected in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	 When the disease is in the channel of the tonsil, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	 It is necessary therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three or four small transverse cuts, between two circles or by the quantity of the cut of the hyoid bone, not in the larynx.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 and those who are suitable for the cutting of the epiglottis are those in whom there is no flesh, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	 And if the master is fearful, then he must stretch the skin of the throat to its full length, then split the heart until it reaches the chin.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	 and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then cut the sponge, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	 and it is proven by the paralysis of the chin which jumps strongly at the place that is broken, and by the loss of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	 And when the time has passed where one fears suffocation, bring together the two lips of the heart wound, and suture it all alone without a needle.
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then administer medicines that promote flesh growth until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	 Albucasis said that this should not be done until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dying, and is unable to breathe.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	 Then one cuts the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	 and therefore the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease had passed, and it passes in three days or four, and then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, until it was healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	 I saw that a young woman took a knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the tendons of the neck;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 and I was called to cure her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	 I discovered the wound, and found that blood had issued from it, although she had not cut a vein or artery except in the throat, and the wind was issuing strongly through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	 I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and cared for it until she was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	 And it happened to the maiden that she was hoarse of voice, and she returned afterwards to her state;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	 Of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	 This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in the color of a coal, and it is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	 and there are two kinds:
naturez, et accidens;	 natural, and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 or the natural kind has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	 And the accidental kind is of two kinds, one of which resembles fat and the other kind resembles an abscess that comes from our artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	 and there should be fear, and one must not operate with fire on those that are large, but only on the small ones, and test and seek throughout the entire intromission.
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	 If you find it like this, as if it were fat, and it does not touch any vein, then cut it off, just as one cuts the nose, and draw out all its hair, if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And bandage it well immediately, and treat it as needed, until it heals perfectly.
des nous	 de
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	 There are many kinds of noses, about which I will tell all their similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 and now it is appropriate for me to describe all the differences that exist between a nose and an ulcer.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	 I say that an ulcer is hot and feverish as long as the inflammation has not passed and the pus has been released.
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	 Then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	 With a nose, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains the pus, which is its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and it begins like a boil, and grows large.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 And they are according to two likenesses, either greasy or moist, and many are of color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	 It is necessary that when you come to the treatment of us, you first examine and inquire with all the instrument that is called "entromissoire", according to what its form will be in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	 And the manner of inquiring about the abscesses of us is that you take the moistest place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has reached the heart, then according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 Then remove the probe, and be careful in this, lest it burst forth.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	 If running moisture has a color, incise it as I have said of other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	 And if after the probe moisture comes forth, know that it is greasy, so incise it in a cross shape, and take it with tweezers, and gently scrape each side and guard the skin where it lies so that you draw it out whole with the knot; ething
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 And if you cannot extract it whole, then remove it piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	 For if anything remains, the pain returns many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if a bit remains and the wound festers, then fill the wound with some corrosive powder, close the wound, place something soothing on it, and continue other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 And if the pain is great, then sew together the two lips of the wound, and treat it as if it were a flesh wound.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	 And if the vein is pulsating against you or another, then hurry and fill the place with ground vitriol, and leave it there for two days or three, until the wound festers and the bleeding subsides.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	 Then return to the cup what remains of the nut.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	 Here are the forms of the interposed instruments, and there are three kinds:
grans et moien et petit;	 great, medium, and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	 and there are three types called "albaret," and one called "breb," and they come in three kinds.
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	 large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	 and they are similar to the needles with which one sews sacks, and they are made of citron wood or iron or silver, and those that are yellow in color are worth more, and they are proven better for black lead to encircle the scabs of fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	 And there are three types:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Great, medium, and small, according to the size of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	 The shapes of the hooks are very similar, as you can see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	 Great, medium, and small.
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	 And there are hooks that have two curves of three types likewise.
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	 And there are hooks that have three curves and are also of three types.
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	 And there are hooks with two curves and hooks with only one curve, all of which are of three types.
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 And all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	 The heads of these are sharp, and there are some that cut from only one side, which are used for skinning the hands, so as not to cut the vein or nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	 And from these intrusions are the amputated limbs returned to their places, so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of abscesses;
et sont de III manieres:	 And there are three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	 great, small, and medium, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	 And one does not use it anywhere except in meaty places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and elbows, and in similar places.
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 And sometimes one makes another small instrument, similar to a scoop for stones, according to this shape, with which one stops bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	 And it is sometimes placed in the location that heals quickly for veins and arteries, and sometimes they return according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	 Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much that they seem like women's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 And they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, must follow this form from this line .b to .g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 Then scrape away the fat, and fill the wound with meat-based medicine, then sew together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	 And if the breast sags downward and is reduced due to its size, as happens with women, then make two incisions on top in two similar cuts.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	 so that one is attached to the other at the end of both, so that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this form, from this line .b until this line .g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary for the treatment, until it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	 And if it is not healed, or the incision is not complete, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with damp cotton in a corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 And let it remain until it dissolves the rest and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	 of the abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	 These abscesses that come under the armpits are hard like scrofula with ribs, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those that contain moisture should be incised according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g.:
