Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been drained, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton, and treat with appropriate ointment until healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, then cut it as we have said in the section on scrofula, and if the wound drains pus, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	 From the disruption of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	 When the artery is severed and the skin above it is closed, often abscesses occur, and the same happens with a swollen vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	 And if one recognizes it thus when it is for the artery, then the abscess is long in depth.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	 And when you feel it with your fingers, then you feel the constriction.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	 And when it is for the vein, then the wound is red and swollen.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 And it is foolish to cut this abscess, and especially when it is under the armpits and in the groin and in the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	 Therefore it is necessary to avoid the use of iron, and one who has an abscess on the head must also avoid it, and in one who has a swelling of the artery, make an incision over the skin lengthwise.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	 Cut the flesh as before, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues until it is exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	 Then push a needle under it and make it pierce through to the other side, and tie off the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	 Then press the area between the two ties with a probe until the pus comes out, and the abscess should be relieved.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	 Then manage the dressing in such a way that it covers well, until the ligatures fall off.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then treat with ointment as before, until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	 And if the abscess is of the size of the vein, then it is necessary that you take hold of as much of the abscess as possible with your hand, then insert the needle under the place that you are holding with your hand, and make it pierce through, and there should be a double thread, so that you pull it out from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	 then tie the abscess, as I have told you, with one of the two ends of the thread to the two heads of the needle;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	 and if you doubt that the thread may come out too soon, then insert another needle with all of the thread underneath all of the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	 Then cut the abscess until the pus comes out, then cut the pus from the heart and leave that which is attached.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then place a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil over it, then administer treatments of linen bandages and onions until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	 of the nerve abscesses
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	 Just as abscesses occur in the artery and vein, abscesses also occur in nerves when they are pierced, or by excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	 And this happens most often in the shoulders and feet, and in all places where there are joints. It is a serious abscess, and its color resembles that of the body, and it is in many forms without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	 And when one presses it strongly, the patient feels pain, and it is not in the depths of the body, but beneath the heart.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	 And moves well in all directions, neither forward nor backward, nor downward nor upward. And that which is in the joints should not be cut with iron: 》
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	 per adventure it would go toward constriction
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 and he who is in the head or in the forehead, makes the skin wrinkle up.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	 If the abscess is small, hold it with pincers and cut it at its root
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and if it is large, suspend it with the hook, and scrape off the skin, then remove and close the wound with stitches, and treat it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	 of hanging boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	 Sometimes it occurs in the stomach and nowhere else, and it is an illness called "fungus" because of its similarity to them, and it has a subtle root and a large head
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	 and there are some small ones and very large ones
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 And I saw a man who had two in his belly which were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had small roots, and were always split open, and moisture constantly flowed from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	 I cut them and found that one weighed eighteen ounces and the other six, and the work in the incision is such that you should consider if the patient is moist, and the color of the artichoke is pale and moist with fine roots.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 If you cut it with a broad spatula, and have in your presence the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	 For when cutting often there is too much bleeding, and if the blood overcomes you, then hurry to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	 And if you see the patient frightened and afraid of the iron incision, take a well-made willow branch, and bind it to the affected area as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	 And then tighten it, and do not stop tightening the willow branch until it cuts into the affected area, and each time through this process;
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	 And if the roots are large, there is fear to cut immediately due to the abdomen, but you can cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return;
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 Then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the tendon which is of red-brown color and poor sensitivity and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	 Car it is an encrusted abscess, and I will come to the cure of the abscess afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	 when the wound is severe
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	 Se the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of wound or slitting of sinus, and it is on the belly and goes to some of the abscesses, as happens in other ulcers, either from blood coursing through veins or arteries as mentioned above, or from flatulence;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 and if it is from the ulcer of sinus and from the discharge of boil, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a slight thing without pain, and opens with various discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	 And if it comes from the exit of the intestine, then it is even more diverse, and when one presses on his two hands so that he vomits, and then it returns, and sometimes it becomes hard, and it increases greatly at the entrance to the bath and through great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a minor thing, and it drains well when you press it with your hand, but do not constrict it.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	 and if it is due to blood, then the abscess opens with these signs: it is large and hard, and it is fixed according to its quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to flatulence, then it is easy to touch, and the work is such that you must look to see whether the appearance is due to blood from an artery or a vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 If it is necessary that you leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 Because there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	 And if the appearance is due to the intestines or the bowel, then you must instruct the patient to raise his leg and lie straight, and then sign around the wound;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	 then command him to lie quietly between your hands, then go around the place that you have marked for all the circumference, and draw out half of the abscess above with the entire great hook;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	 then tie it around with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk tightly, and let the knot of the ligature be firm;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	 Then work on half of the abscess stretched over the ligament, and press your thumb inside, and seek the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	 if you find it caught by the ligament, then free it, and push the intestine back out of the belly;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	 and if you find the abscess, then take it at the base, and cut off the excess;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	 and if the artery or vein is in the way, then go carefully around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads into them, and place the two needles around what you have done in a cross pattern that you make by piercing;
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	 then draw the abscess in four places onto the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the place until it putrefies, and each bit of dead flesh will fall away by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	 Or when you cut it, when it is rotted and corrupted, then treat the wound as needed, and remove the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place as needed, and close the wound.
dou chancre	 of the sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	 We have said in the section on cancers, what they look like and how to treat them with medicines, and how to avoid surgical treatment.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	 And we say that cancer begins in the flesh, and great care is needed in its treatment, and the ancients said that when cancer is in a place where it can be scraped off, like cancer of the breast, thigh, or similar places, it should all be removed at the beginning.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	 And when he is old and ancient, you must not approach him, for I have never been able to cure any.
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	 nor has anyone ever cured one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	 And when the work is in place and can be removed, as we have said, it is that you must sometimes purge the patient of black bile;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	 then make him healthy if he has an obvious fullness, then place the patient in a good spot to do the work.
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	 then cut away your onions or warts, and the hair from all around, and remove it entirely without leaving anything behind;
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 and let the blood flow freely, and press the spot well with your hand or some object, and if the bleeding hinders the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is clotted;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal from one treatment until he is healed.
de ydropisie	 Of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	 We have said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and in what manner the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron:
si est eclites soulement;	 only it is inflamed;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	 and in these two similarities one should not touch with iron:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	 that is to say, tympanites and yposarche, for they are deadly things;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	 therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy that is called «inflammation» with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, then look if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, such as diarrhea and similar things;  />
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	 If you do not touch it with iron, for there is doubt;
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	 and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other disease except only dropsy, and he is not too young nor too old, then thus should you work:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 lift the patient straight up in your hands, and have the assistant press the stomach by pushing the water to the lowest part of the bladder, then take the pointed spatula according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut into two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	 with its point, and nevertheless it should not be so intrusive that when inserted, it can reach the intestines and cannot hurt it;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	 then look if the dropsy is accumulated towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	 If it is necessary, you must cut three fingers' width above the base of the thumb.
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	 and if the hydropsy is due to liver disease, let your cut be three fingers' width to the left of the base.
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	 and if it is due to the spleen, then let it be on the right, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie upon the cut so that the excesses do not flow into that weak place.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	 then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push it through, and lift your hand all the way up to the subcutaneous tissue between the skin and the fascia as if you were scraping, to the thickness of a nail or less around.
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 then pierce the fascia until the subcutaneous tissue comes into view, which is the place of water, then draw the instrument strongly, and push this instrument with which there is the shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	 And it is similar to a fine silver chain, and it is of light brass or copper, and has at its lower part a small hole.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	 and on one side there are three holes.
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	 and two on the other side, and one on the other.
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 and the head is cut like a quill, and this is the shape of the incision which scribes cut into the quill.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	 at the top is the airhole, so that when the instrument comes to the water, they now rise on the instrument.
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	 empty then the half or third part, because if you empty more than is necessary in that hour, it may happen that the patient dies from the loss of his spirit through the arm, where he falls unconscious, or approaches death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	 but in an empty place according to the quantity of its power, and according to what the patient's condition indicates, and their pulse.
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	 then take out the instrument and retain the water, which is now retained by the wax that blocks the hole on the syringe, as I have mentioned, so that you pierce in this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	 then renew the instrument the next day, if you see that the patient can tolerate it, and extract a small amount of water;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 do this every day, and be careful not to overdo it so that only a little water remains.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	 And if you are unsure about the patient and leave a lot of water in them, then treat with a hot poultice or sand, and by much sweating or bathing in the sun, and let them drink wine.
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 and the treatment with drying medicines should be continued until it is healed, and cauterization on the stomach, liver, and spleen after removing the fluid, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	 Of the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes children are born without an opening in the penis, or with a small opening, or one that is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 It must be pierced as soon as possible with a very fine needle according to this method:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	 then insert a thin reed through the hole, and tie it and hold it thus for three days or four. And when he needs to urinate, remove the reed, and let him urinate, and then put it back;
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes forth does not leave a hole open.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 He whose hole is small will be treated with the pine plug as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	 those who do not have the hole in its proper place are harmed, for some are born with the hole at the tip of the penis, so they cannot urinate unless they raise their penis upwards;
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 And cannot heal because the material cannot reach the bone, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	 And the manner of the work is that the patient lies on his back, then stretch the head of the rod and the handle equally as the width of a feather quill, so that the hole falls in the middle, as it should be.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And beware of bleeding that often occurs there; and if it does happen, staunch it with what staunches blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	 of the pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	 Many times these baths are taken in the rod, and this is an ugly appearance of flesh;
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	 And there are malignant and benign ones;
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	 Si you must take them at one time with skill, then cut and clean all of them, then place upon moistened cotton in Egyptian ointment.
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then continue the care with daily application until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the albathe is malignant, of putrid color and stinking, then you must apply cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	 When you have cut it, and if the blister is partly on the vein, with part of it under the skin and part outside, then you must remove the part that is under first.
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 And when it has healed, then treat the rest.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	 For when you treat them together, it is not certain that the head of the vein will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption will occur in the vein and in the joint.
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 So it is necessary to cut away all that is black and corrupted, then place upon it a plaster made of honey and flour from the bark of pomegranates and peas, then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if bleeding occurs, then apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	 The cautery serves two purposes at once:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	 that is to say, for the purging of blood and for the treatment of putrefaction.
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	 and if the head of the penis is putrefied and drawn back, then you must insert a leaden probe into the urethra, and have the patient urinate through it.
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	 and when the skin is inflamed at the tip of the penis, which occurs in those who have not been circumcised, due to a wound or an abscess, then you must scrape it with a hairy instrument until the connection is released, and the head of the penis is freed on all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	 and if it is difficult to treat this condition, then you must scrape with a spoonful of the tip of the penis and the skin.
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 Then quickly place between two [supports], and put one fine linen cloth moistened in cold water, so that it does not dry out again.
de la circoncision	 of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	 Circumcision is not a separation of continuity like other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	 nevertheless when we perform this work by our own will, especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best and lightest cut for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	 I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, because they do not practice it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	 For I have seen many masters and healers performing circumcisions around the foreskin, on the strong parts, and on the entire glans;
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	 so that the cutter might cause injury because there are two layers, and if one cuts through the top layer, the bottom layer remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	 Or there is fever, and the pain is doubled, and at the cleansing which is of the water, the point of the member is not secure.
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	 and at the cleansing of the nail perhaps the iron escapes, and the work is ruined, and many times it happens that there is no need for cleansing, and I wish it to be so.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	 From the amputation done with silk thread I have found the advantage of the experiment, for the silk cuts evenly on top as well as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	 For when you press your hand, cut evenly in one stroke.
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	 but the thread must be well twisted around the leather;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	 and the method of the first work is such that you make the child think, if it understands, that you are not doing anything to it but tying the thread around the rod only, and then let it go in all the ways that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	 Then let it stand straight between your hands, and replenish the powers between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments.
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	 Then place your hand on the staff and blow into its heart, and pull it up until the head of the staff is inside.
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	 Then clean it well of the gathered filth, then bind the place securely with a double thread, then tie it under the armpit to another bond.
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	 And hold it with two fingers of the second ligament at the little finger and the index finger, and cut between the two ligaments, then lift the heart quickly and pull the head of the staff.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	 Then let the blood flow drop by drop, for this is the cure.
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And put powder on it and on the powder a drape stuck with the white of a cooked egg, tempered with rose water, mixed with good and fresh oil of roses, and leave it until the next day, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	 The form of the poultice for this is as follows:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	 Both ends should be sharp and equal in size.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	 The error of the poultice is when the herbs inside are wet from the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	 Therefore, you must spread it with your fingernail, so that the place does not form an abscess.
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	 And cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with tweezers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	 And if they exceed three days, and that which is below the member is swollen, then leave it until the abscess has subsided, and gently scrape off the scab.
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	 If you can move the tip as you please, and be careful of the part of the member, it will not harm him at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	 Then cure the place with sudden powdered wound, as we have said in the treatment of powders, and if the tip goes beyond measure and goes above, it will not harm.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	 Of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	 The retention of urine is due to the formation of stones, or congealed blood, or bone, or dead flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the section on classification.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	 And if the urine is not released, and you see that it is retained due to a stone in the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent over his knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	 And let the feet be placed on the back, and extend his belly from the part above the back, and let the patient hold his breath as long as he can.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	 And then the neck of the bladder is forced to expel the stone above, so that the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	 And if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer an extraction with all the instrument that is called "syringe," of which here is the form.
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	 and let it be of fine silver, lightly hammered, like a bird's feather.
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 and let the rod be one and a half palms long, and let it be fine at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	 And the manner of issuing urine is such that you take a double thread, and tie at its end a bag of wool or cotton, and insert the end of the thread into the syringe;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	 and cut off the excess of the wool and push it up to the end of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and have the patient sit on a chair, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	 Then put the syringe lightly on the penis until it reaches the base of the penis, then fold the penis over towards the foreskin.
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	 Then push the syringe forward until it reaches the bladder, and the patient will feel it reaching the empty space, and this is not done according to this order unless because the duct through which it passes is twisted.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	 Then draw out the thread all the way to the tip of the wool little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then pull it out hard and make the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And repeat with the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	 Of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	 When scabbing or blood comes into the bladder, or there is rot assembled therein, and you wish to distill waters and medicines, then make for the entire instrument that is called a "clepsydra," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	 It is closed, and there are three openings:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	 Of one side, and I of the other side, as you see.
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	 and the leaves chosen so that the medicinal juice is such that it stops the member well without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture, and push when needed.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	 and when you see your medicines fall into the bladder, place the head of the kettle in the moisture, and draw out what is inside.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	 thus you will draw the moisture into the kettle, and then push the contents back forcefully.
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	 so the moisture will enter, and will now come to the bladder, so that the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	 and this is the form of the subtle enema with which one enemas the bladder:
si est ci:	 Si est ci
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	 And it is of silver or steel, and the head is higher;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	 and beneath in the chest where the ligament rests.
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	 Then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture in it to enema the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat the pouch with that moisture over the fire.
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	 Then insert the nozzle of the enema into the penis, then press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has entered, so that the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	 And if you do not have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment and make it into a circle, and pierce it evenly all around.
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	 Then push a strong thread through these holes, then join the circle together like one joins a bucket, and put inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument.
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And do as you have done with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	 of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	 We have already said in the division the methods of stones, and the extraction together with medicine;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	 And I have said the difference between a stone in the kidneys and all the signs, and in which stone one should work by cutting;
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	 And in the bladder, and in the penis.
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	 And I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	 I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder happens more often to children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder like fine water in its subtlety;
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	 and there opens the anus, and the patient grabs his penis, and he ejaculates many times, and then it swells.
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	 and with each of these jumps the foundation shakes.
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	 and the healing is light in children until they are four years old, and it is very severe in the elderly, and it is of moderate difficulty for those who are between youth and old age.
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	 and the treatment is lighter for those with a large stone than for those with a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, first, we must cleanse the patient with an enema, to expel all the feces that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes hinders the search for stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	 Then take the patient by the feet and turn them upwards and move downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and jumps out some time.
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	 then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be under his thighs so that the bladder is completely tilted downwards.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	 Then seek and touch within;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	 And if it does not fall with the touch of all, then moisten your finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adolescent;
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	 and push it into its foundation, and seek the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, then bring it to the neck of the bladder;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 then press with your finger, and push it out from where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	 And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and order him to extend with his right hand the testicles upward, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the testicles in the area where the cut is made;
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	 Then he applies the spatula pressing, from which comes the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	 And he makes an incision between that which is between the thighs and the anus, not in the middle but on the left side of the vein.
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	 and let the cut be straight over the stone, and your two fingers be close to the anus, and let the cut across it be so that it is wide on the outside, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	 by chance, the pressure from the finger in the anus causes it to jump out without work
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	 and know that there are some stones with angles and edges:
si est griés a issir;	 if it is obstructed from coming out
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 and there are others that are below, like a pea, round, whose exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	 To those then who have angles and margins, make the cut larger.
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	 And if it does not jump out, then you must pull with the pincers which are like a file at the top, to pull the stone until it is dislodged.
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	 Or you put under the instrument subtle curved at the top;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	 And if you cannot thus trick it, then widen the pouch where the hole is, and if the flesh tears, then constrict it with vitriol;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 And if there are more than one stone, then first put the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut on top, then draw strongly, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, it must be sawed, and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	 For two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	 either he dies, or urine flows continuously where the wound cannot heal;
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	 yet you should strive to extract it, or break it with pincers, until you remove it in pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	 and when you have completed your work, fill the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, bandage it, and place on top a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to calm the hot abscess.
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 then bandage the patient around his neck, and do not untie the knot until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you untie it, wash the place very well with oil and water, then treat it with ointment of dyafinicon and ointment of basilicon, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	 And if abscesses or corrosion come to the wound, and a clot of blood in the bladder, which retains the urine so that it passes with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	 Stick your finger into the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will run to the bladder, and will cause putrefaction.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then raise the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and help him in all the ways you know, until he is healed.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And it is necessary that every time you treat him, you bind his two thighs together, and apply the medicines to the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	 And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra, and stuck there, and the urine cannot come out;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 then the treatment of what I say is such that you cut it many times, and thus he is freed from cutting through this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already proven this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	 Take iron with a shape like this, and it should be fixed at three corners on one stake:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	 Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	 then insert the punch lightly into the shaft until it reaches the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	 and turn the punch in your hand gently against the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 then the urine will come out, and press your hand against what remains of the stone inside the shaft.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	 Then it is immediately broken, and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is cured;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	 and if you cannot do this because of any obstruction, then tie a thread below the stone and another above it, then make an incision in the shaft toward the stone between the two ties, then draw it out forcefully, and untie the threads, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; )))
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And let the treatment continue until healed.
de la piere des femmes	 of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	 It often happens that stones are lodged in women, and if it does occur, the treatment is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons.
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	 One reason is that perhaps the woman is a virgin.
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	 And the second reason is that one cannot find a woman well-versed who reveals herself to physicians, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	 And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well-versed in this hand-based art.
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	 And the fourth manner is that the stones in women are more deeply embedded than in men, which requires a deeper cut, and there is great fear. And if necessity compels you, then you must find a knowledgeable midwife, but they are rarely found, and if you cannot find one, then seek a subtle chaste physician.
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	 And it presents a wise midwife in the life of women, or a woman who knows some part of the art, and commands her to do what you command her concerning the investigation of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	 and take great care to see if the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	 then she must insert her finger into the vagina and search for the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 and if she finds it, she should press it under her finger, and commands that she insert her finger into the vagina of the patient, and seek out and press her left hand strongly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	 If she finds it, she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder downward until it reaches the base of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	 then cut on the bone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the knee, where it is most prepared, and the patient will feel the bone in that part.
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	 and do not move his finger on top or beneath the bone, and let the cut be small at first;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	 then insert the reed into the cut, if you feel the bone, narrow the wound so that the bone may come out more strongly, and know that there are many kinds of bones:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 these are: small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and those with edges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 If you know the signs, you will know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 And if the blood overcomes you, apply powdered vitriol to the place, and let it sit for an hour until the blood is stanched.
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	 Then return to your work, until the stone is strong, and have the instruments that I have told you for extracting stones in men to help you in your work;
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	 And if the blood overcomes you, and it is from the artery that has been cut, then put the powder on the place and bandage with cloths and bandages, and do not start again, and leave the stone alone and do not pull it out, lest the patient die by chance;
puis cure la plaie.	 Then heal the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	 And when the heat of the blood is calmed and the place healed, return to your work until the stone is passed.
de hernie carnouse	 of flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	 "Ramice" means a kind of cloth used to bind wounds. Therefore, an aquous ramice is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white silk under the skin of the kidneys, which contains the egg;
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	 and it is called "silk," and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one believes that this is another egg.
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	 And this is the skin of the eye between the white part that we have said.
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	 and this would not happen if it were not for pus.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	 And the cause of this collection is due to weakness in the kidneys, which spreads this substance.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	 And sometimes it comes from striking the eyes, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	 or it is a yellowish color, or it is without red, or black, or white like water, and this happens more often;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 and these are the signs to recognize this condition, for if it is in the white part that we have said, then the abscess is thin, the pus long like an egg, and the eye does not open, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	 And if there is moisture in the proper fabric, then the abscess is thin with a part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks that it is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	 And if the moisture is between the skin of the coccyx and the white flesh, then one feels it well.
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 Therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, test the entire intromission area from which the form comes before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	 According to that which follows the instrument, judge what is within it.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	 And when we cure it with fire, it is necessary that the patient be bled according to our ability and the fullness of his body.
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	 Then have him lie on his back, on something a little high, and put many blankets under him;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	 Then sit on his left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs at the base of the coccyx.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	 Then take the spatula, and cut the skin of the coccyx along its length until near the anus, and let your incision be straight, dividing the skin of the coccyx down to the white flesh, and delicately scrape according to your ability.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	 Then pierce the sponge full of water through a large hole, and draw out all the water, and then put your fingers in, and swell the sponge upward;
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	 And do not touch the core of the kidneys, but only the sponge;
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	 Cut all or in pieces evenly the flesh from him subtly, so that if you do not cut well wisely, the water will come back;
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	 And if the egg jumps forward from your work, return it to its place when you have completed the sponge's task;
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then sew together the two leaves of the kidney core with one stitch, then heal it as you would other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	 And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you bind the vessels that are bleeding, suspecting the flow of blood;
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	 Then cut the string with all the suspending parts, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	 And if the vessel is divided into two parts together, know that these are two veins;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	 Then cut the other part in the same way as you did the first, then wipe away the blood, and place a piece of cloth soaked in rose oil on the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And place another piece of cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, and put on the two strings, and put double-layered bandages on top, and bind it all up with all the ligatures according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	 Then take two bandages and stuff them with wool according to this pattern, and sew them together at the crotch of the breeches, and one of the strings should go from the anus up to the back, and the other to the scrotum.
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	 And let the other two heads be on the two ankles, and all the ligaments should be bound together in the elbow loop.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	 And sometimes this ligature is treated with a cautery in place of an iron cut. This means you should take a subtle surgical cautery, and cut the skin of the testicles, and it should be heated as we have said, so that the white part which contains water is uncovered.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that white part at the testicles, and it should be burnt with this hot subtle cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	 And cut in all ways that you can, until you burn everything.
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	 and make sure the fire does not touch the testicle.
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	 and know that this work is more healing;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	 and moving cautions against bleeding, and bandages to prevent the work of incision;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 and if any thing goes contrary, whether it is an abscess or bleeding or anything else, then treat what goes contrary to you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	 And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this work because of its horror, then introduce perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are certain through the signs that we have said that aquous humor is there, then make the patient sit on a high seat; etti.
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	 then pierce the abscess in the lower part as wide as possible, and place the perforation along the length of the body;
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	 And let the holes be wide so that all the water flows freely;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	 Then place cotton on the spot, bind it, and allow the rest of the water to drain, then treat until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	 And if the white cloth does not allow water to exit from the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or an instrument for removing water from hydrocephalic patients, as described above.
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And widen the wound, and know that the water will return and be collected again after six months or a year, and when it is collected as before, then the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	 of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	 Know that in cutting this vein there is fear of many complications, which is why I think it is better to leave it alone.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 And I will tell you the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	 So I say that many abscesses come to the body, especially to the joints;
et c’est par mout de cas.	 and this is very common.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	 This is to say by an excessive acute and sharp humour that spreads to the joints, or from blunt trauma;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	 and the colour of the abscess depends on the colour of the body;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	 and it experiences no pain, yet the abscess is severe;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 and sometimes the abscess is feared and dreadful, with a reddish colour, and occasionally it comes from a nodule of artery, or from swollen veins.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	 When it is from a nodule of artery, it is known by the hot nature of the abscess when you press it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 And it is not necessary for you to touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	 He who is affected by the swelling of a vein is known by his propensity to express at the touch of fingers, and one can well make an incision on this similarity, and on other scars;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 And it is that you cut the heart of the kidneys, then elevate the egg above, and draw the white thread outward, and deliver the suspending parts from all around the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	 If the egg is already hardened with these scars born, then it is necessary that you draw out the egg and the cut;
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 And if it is on the surface or in that which is within the vessels, then you must deliver all this tendon and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	 Et si les racines de la chair sont à l'arrière du lieu, alors il faut que tu coupes toute la chair et extrais le pus, comme nous l'avons dit.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when your work is complete, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then perform other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	 of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	 This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping similar to a bud, with the softening of the cheeks, and if the patient goes away, he becomes very ill.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 And the treatment of this disease is almost as dangerous as the one mentioned before, nevertheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	 You must make the patient sit on a raised seat, then wrap the suspenders of the cheeks down to your thighs, with all the vessels that are near the penis, and pull them strongly.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	 Then cut with a broad, sharp spatula across the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the temples' arteries;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	 then he inserts a needle with two threads, and ties it at the first place where the vein has come, and ties it again at the other end;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	 then he cuts them in half straight down, according to the length of the body, and draws out the putrid moisture;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	 then he treats the wound as with others where one inserts a bone, so that some vessel is filled which nourishes one of the eyes;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	 for by this means no harm comes, and if the eye becomes blind in all vessels, then it is necessary to draw out the eyes from all vessels;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 so that the eye does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	 de la rupture du sinus
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	 The events of this hernia occur through the incision that comes in the groin, or the extension on the stomach in the inguinal region, which causes the intestines to descend from that opening into one of the testicles.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	 And this opening is in the groin, or the extension of it, and these two types occur for many reasons.
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	 from a blow, or a jump, or a sneeze, or lifting a heavy object, and from similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	 And the signs when it is an extension of the groin are that it occurs little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly.
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 And the abscess is equal to the groin, because the groin presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	 And the sign that it is of the section in the sinus is that at first it causes sudden pain, and the abscess has various appearances under the skin nearby, and this is due to the protrusion of the intestine and the body outside of the sinus.
