Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	 The things by which wounds are made are by falling of stone, and cutting with sword and knife, or spear or staff or arrow, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	 where they are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck or the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with the simple head wounds, because their treatment will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	 I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from falling stone or similar things, and the skin is torn open and the wound is large, and you suspect a hot abscess:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	 If there is a little blood from the wound, immediately bandage it from the head itself, and let the bandage be on the opposite side of the injured part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 And let the patient avoid drinking wine and eating heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	 And if he does not wish to bandage it, let his food be reduced, and let him not drink wine, nor eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	 And put on the wound, if there are swellings there, only a little cotton soaked in rose oil or in stiptic wine.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	 And if there is no hot swelling, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood and not moved by the air, a powder which I will mention in a moment.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the fire has moved it, apply some poultices until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	 And if the wound is large like that of a sword or similar, and the lips cannot be joined by stitches, then join them by sewing, as I will explain in the case of stomach wounds, using sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	 If the wound is exposed to the bone, and it hangs loose, and is only attached by a thread, then cut it off;
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as heads and cooked wheat, also like beans, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	 And if you find rottenness in the skin, and it reaches to the bone, then cut away all the rot, throw it out, then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	 and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then tie it off with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if this does not help at all, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	 And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	 And this is that you put in this powder that seals before the fire has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	 And the manner of the powder is:
pren encens une partie;	 take incense one part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	 dragon's blood two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	 quicklime three parts, and powder it finely, and fill the wound, and bind it tightly, until it heals well and adheres to all its flesh.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	 And then bind it well, and leave it unbound if it does not swell;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 For one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	 And sometimes one does this with quicklime alone, when one does not have frankincense or dragon's blood, but that the heat has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	 And if the fire has moved the wound, even in summer, one should not put this powder on it.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	 But apply some cooked ointments or poultices made from barley flour with water and honey, until the wound casts off.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then cure with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	 And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, draw it out with fine tweezers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 and I will tell you about fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	 of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	 If the wound is in the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and one in the head, but if a nerve of the neck or an artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	 If it is a nerve, there is no other remedy than to leave the wound alone and not apply anything that might constrict it, for this harms the nerves and causes them to recede.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	 And do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 but the medicine should be warm, like hot water with sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and wash the cuts in the same way with sweet water, and other small stones according to this manner, and moist compresses.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound is large, stitch it and bind with bandages, then let it heal until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	 And if the wounds are deep and they have festered and are full of pus, then pierce them in a lower place.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	 And if the vein is cut and blood flows out, then expose it, clean it, and cauterize it if necessary.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	 And if the windpipe or the trachea is cut and the passage is kept open so that food can pass, then stitch the trachea onto the skin of the neck, and do not touch the throat but put it back in its natural shape.
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And then he holds it firmly, and leaves it for some days, then treats it with dried onions until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	 And if the wound has made an impression in the bone, seek it out;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	 And if there are bone fragments, draw them all out if you can, and those that you cannot extract, leave until the wound heals over and the openings close.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	 And if there are bones in the wound, and it has an abscess, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	 Of a spear or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	 If it is a stab wound or a cut, and the wound is deep, observe if gas comes out of the wound when the patient inhales:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	 know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	 And if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put the powder in at the first hour, nor bind it for fear that the blood does not flow deeply, and returns to the heart, and kills the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	 but apply an attracting ointment, and bandage it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	 and if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	 thus there will not be any spasm, nor evil shaking of the heart, nor fainting.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 and when you see these good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Heal him then with poultices and other treatments until he is healthy.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	 And if she cannot heal, and it works again, know that there is a fistula.
si la cure si com on doit.	 If the treatment is done as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, either worse or on the back, then treat it as for those in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	 If it is large, with stitching;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	 And if it is small, with powder. And if it is near the bone and has broken into pieces, seek to clean the wound and remove any splinters if they are exposed.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	 And if they are not exposed, then let the wound fester, for this will ease the extraction.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And of other wounds to other limbs is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	 of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	 The rupture of the belly is great and moderate and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	 of the great wound sometimes the intestine, or the nerve of the intestine, because of which the introduction of air;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	 and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because it is more difficult to put the intestines back in unless they are replaced hot on hot.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	 because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, and they return less easily; and therefore the moderate wound is better, because one returns the intestine to its place more than in other [types of wounds]
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	 And know that wounds of the belly are according to IV manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	 the II common sewings happen in the sewing of the belly, and the sewing of other wounds of the body and II other special sewings are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 nevertheless they are more specific with the sewing of the belly, and I will speak of each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	 I say that when the wound is small, and something of the intestine has come out, and it is a good thing to return, this is by one of the II manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen by cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	 And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	 moisten a sponge or a clean cloth in warm water only, or boil in hot water with juniper and clove, and wash the intestines until the swelling is gone;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 and sometimes make this wine restraining, and it is said that only sloe berries are used to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	 And when you see the swelling leave, then moisten the intestines in water where mallows and hollyhocks have been boiled, for by this the entrance is made easier.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	 And if it cannot enter, then make a small opening in the wound with the instrument used for cutting hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	 and the first cure is said to be that it should be cut, which no one should cut unless there is great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	 And this is the instrument to split it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 cut inside on the curve and not outside, and see here the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines leap out, set them back in place according to their natural form in their proper location, if you can, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	 When the wound is wide and it is in the part below the stomach, you must make the patient lie on their back and put their legs higher than their head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	 and if it is in the part below the stomach, put the head and feet higher than the parts below, and likewise if the injury to the stomach is in one of the two parts, set your intention so that the injured part is higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 And thus you must manage as I say for both large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	 In small wounds, apply what you have prepared, then hold between your hands a gentle minister who can touch the entire wound with his hand and bring the lips together;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	 And this is the common manner of sutures, and it is that you take one needle or several, according to the width of the wound, then leave two fingers' width from the head of the wound, and there insert a needle with a good strong thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	 And pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the needle, which is beneath the skin within, so that you make it pierce from this side, and gather the three heads of the needle together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	 Then draw a double thread around the needle on two sides, then gather the two heads of the wound similarly, and leave two fingers' width, and insert another needle there;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	 Then take the thread of the needle as you did for the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you need the needles for, until all the wound is closed.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	 And let the needles be of medium size, between fine and thick, because fine needles pierce all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	 therefore they must be of medium size;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	 and it is not necessary to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and widen the wound before sewing.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	 and then cut the heads of the needles so that they do not wound the patient while sleeping, and put a bandage or cloth over the heads of the needles to keep them still, and leave them until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	 And this manner of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because one or two needles are sufficient for it.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	 The second suture is common, and it is that you join the two heads of the skin and the two heads of the flesh together with one needle that has a strong middle thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	 And when you have pierced these four heads together, then bring the needle back to the part where you began, in the manner that one sews clothes.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	 And put a distance between each suture the thickness of a small finger.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 This suture serves men, and I sutured a wound that a man had in the belly, which was wounded by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and two palms of intestines came out, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I returned the intestines to him after they had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound was closed until fifteen days, and I cared for it, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	 And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	 and did not treat him with ointment, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 and placed on the wound old cotton II times a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	 Now I will tell you the II proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	 take the needle, and push it from the outside part to the inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	 when it has pierced the skin from right to left, leave the end of the thread where you pushed the needle in, and make it come out on the other side from the inside to the outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 And the method of this stitch is such that you should sew as the furrier does with furs, and leave the end of the thread on one side, and pick it up on the other side, until the entire seam is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	 The second method of stitching, which Galen specifically mentions, is done in such a way that some people join the two parts together naturally, and apply one end of the thread to the other end, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	 Insert a needle into the nearer end of the thread and make it pass through that place only, leaving the two ends of the thread;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	 then turn the needle and make it pass from the outer part to the inner one, at the two ends of the thread;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	 Then have one and the other pierced from the outer part to the inner, in two other places of the mirror that are on either side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 And this is the manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	 Galen said these words, and some testify that one should sew the belly with two needles, each with thread.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	 And one must insert one needle from one side and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew belts.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 And know that when the perforation is in the middle of the belly, then the stitching is more difficult than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	 The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	 And it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, before the fire has moved it, then put back the entrails, and the skin.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	 Then place on the wound a powder of healing herbs, and if the fire has moved it, then apply some ointment that is readily available until the wound heals.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	 And stitch up the flesh, and let the skin and membrane be sewn together.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then treat the wound like the others until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 And if you do not have medicine, then apply, as soon as it begins to heal, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	 For in many cases you do not need other medicines when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	 and if you doubt that the wound may infect the main members, then you must soak a light linen cloth in temperate oil, or rose oil, and place it around the joints, and under the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	 and if he feels pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which often happens, then give him a clyster of boiled wine, and do this also if the putrefaction reaches the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 and pierce it from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is due to the thinness of the veins that are there, and due to the subtlety of the entire body, and its proximity in nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	 And if the entrails come out of the wound, then replace them like the intestines, as long as they are fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	 And if the hair is grey or turned black, then you must tie the place that is dark, so that blood does not flow there, for there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 Then cut that which is between the ligament, and place the two hooks hanging from the part below the wound until it is completely healed to facilitate extraction when the bone falls out, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	 of the wound of the eye
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	 When the intestines are cut and the wound is small, then one can restore it in some men, because I saw that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	 and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became infected and turned into a fistula, from which excrement and flatulence came out.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 I cared for him as best as I could, and did not stop refining until he was healed, and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	 And when I saw it close, I feared that the patient might have an illness in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	 and there was no illness there, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	 and some experts said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be bound in such a way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	 take broad-headed clamps, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the clamp has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips so that it tightens its mouth upon them;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	 and then cut off the head of the clamp, and this stays so that it cannot be loosened, then place another clamp after in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely grasped; eben
et cout la plaie.	 And treat the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	 Those heads if they get stuck in the intestines, and no harm comes to the patient, then one can tie off the intestines with a fine thread cut from the intestines of an animal, in such a manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	 take the head of this intestinal thread that is very thin, and then tie a fine twisted linen thread to the head of this thread, then pass the thread through the needle, and sew the intestines with it, and bring it back in the opposite direction;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	 and this manner of suturing is only for when there is hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the internal organs, there is no remedy or cure, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	 Of a fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it is healed, is universally called a "fistula", and also when it bursts open again.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	 Et fistula est selon la verité, une nodule dure et blanche, où l'on ne ressent pas de douleur, et elle est aussi creuse qu'une plume d'oiseau.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	 Et parfois, elle apparaît sous forme de claire-voie, et d'autres fois, elle est épaisse.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	 Parfois, elle se présente comme une poche, et d'autres fois, elle est suffisamment remplie.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	 Et je vous ai déjà parlé dans le chapitre sur les plaies, qu'une plaie qui ne guérit pas, et où il n'y a pas de chair, n'est ouverte que pour l'une des NEUF raisons:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	 C'est-à-dire, à cause de la petitesse du sang ou de la chair.
ou por sa malice;	 Or by its mischief;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	 or because there is hard flesh inside it and on the lips, which does not allow new flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	 or if there is too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	 or if the place is rotten and the matter is of bad quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	 or if the medicine is not good for healing;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	 or because the decay is a kind of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	 or because of the property in the region, digestion and healing are slow, and it is naturally swollen.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	 or if there are veins or bones involved.
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	 And it is necessary for me to make you know the treatment of a fistula made by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	 Know that a fistula can occur in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	 for there are fistulas that come to the great veins, and to the arteries, and to the nerves, or to the liver, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 and if it comes to the property of the main member, and to similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	 And all the fistulas that are of this type are of serious illness, and there is nothing except work and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	 and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have mentioned, and you are confident of the cure, and you recognize it, then take a tent of bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, then seek it; xspace
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	 And if the fistula is twisted, then seek a subtle tent of wood, for the wood bends easily around the twisting;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	 And if the fistula has many openings and you cannot easily seek it with tents, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for moisture courses from one opening to another, and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	 Then seek it wisely to your ability, that you may know if there is bone or nerve, and it is cut deeply, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels at the pressing of your hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	 And when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the foulness and the corrupt flesh that is inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	 And then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is well deep from the right place, you must cut into it deeply, as much as you can, then put moist tents in theriac wine, and push them up to the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And then put on bandages made of clean flesh, until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And if it is not healed by this method, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut into it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	 If a vein or nerve troubles you in the principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackening, then clean it until all the corruption is removed, then treat with things that promote healing until it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	 And if it is not healed and the swelling returns as before, know that you have not reached the source.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	 If you expose and clean until you reach the bottom and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 And if it is healed in this way, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	 If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	 if there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	 And if there is a small piece of bone that has decayed and you can extract it with pincers, then do so with an appropriate instrument, and if there are many pieces of bone, then extract all of them, leaving none behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 And if moisture makes it difficult, and there is no mistake or fear, then cut away the flesh and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	 And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then apply a putrefying substance to the wound and allow it to decay around the bones, so that the bones may be more easily extracted.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	 And if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh bone, then wait for the corruption until all the blackness has been removed, then close the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	 And if there is a great deal of corruption, and it reaches up to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	 then you must clean and cut away everything down to the corruption, and then treat it until it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	 He was a young man about thirty years old who had pain in his leg from an internal cause, so that the matter came to the leg, and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no external cause to open it.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	 But the doctors, through their foolishness, operated so much that they opened the abscess, and there flowed a lot of matter from it, and it became a fistula, and there came a lot of holes that all threw out pus and moisture from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	 And many doctors tried to cure it for about two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine present, until I was called upon it, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what flowed through the holes, a great amount.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 And the body of the youth turned red, and it had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	 I hastened then, and struck in one of the holes until I uncovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupt and pierced, and the corruption reached inside the bone;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	 I believed that what appeared to me of the corrupt bone was all the corruption there was, except for what I removed;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	 and began to restore the wound with soothing medicines over a long time, but it could not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	 and then I began again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and believed it, and then removed it, and took care to heal the place;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	 But I could not do so much that I cut around a palm's width of the bone, and I pulled out the arrow with all its shaft, then I treated it with medicines.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 and he was quickly healed and cured, and there was no need to repeat the work except for the weakness of the patient who could not endure it, and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 Because of the evacuation, he often bled profusely, but he was completely cured, and in place of the bone, a hard flesh grew, which had a good constitution and did not cause any harm or opposition, neither while coming nor going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	 take a bandage and tie it around the end of the protruding bone, and command someone to extend it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	 and put another bandage of thicker cloth than the first one around the flesh above the bone, and stretch out the end so that you pull the corrupted flesh away from below, and uncover the flesh in the place where you wish to tie, so that the thread does not injure the flesh; )))
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	 And place a glowing coal under the bone to better burn the rotten flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And it must be burned until the corruption can be seen and felt, and then it must be burned again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	 And if the bone is corrupt, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then peel away all the flesh;
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	 Then place a coal underneath, and then burn from one part to the other of the corruption, and let the burning be deep as the length of the corruption, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	 And if the corruption is in the joint, then burn the corrupt joint, and burn the bone from the other side where it contains the corruption.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	 And if the corruption is between two joints, there is no other remedy than to burn.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	 and if the corruption is in the palm of the hand or the sole of the foot, then that thing is very strong; nevertheless, you must investigate this corruption, how it opens to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	 and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but let not the vein or nerve hinder you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	 and know that the incisors and saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and delicacy, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	 and therefore it is necessary to prepare for each type of work its tool;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	 and know that the work will show you the tool that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 If you consider the instrument you need according to what is required.
dou feu	 Of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	 The head persists either because of internal causes or external ones;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	 and when you have treated that corruption with the remedies of medicines, and they do not help, then it is necessary to cover that member up to the place where the corruption comes, so that the patient escapes by death or by the greater evil of the loss of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	 and the signs are that the member becomes black, as if it were burnt by fire, and persists after the blackening, then this corruption of the limb spreads from one member to another, and takes over the entire body; xspace
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 if you hasten to cover it, and if it is due to the bite of some venomous creatures, such as scorpions of the sea and vipers and similar ones, if the corruption is at the head of the arm, then cover it, and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	 And if it extends to the hand, then cut it at the joint, so that corruption does not spread to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	 and if it extends to the arm, then cut it with a knife;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	 and if it goes beyond the knife's edge, it is death, and there is no remedy outside of the amount of its power.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	 and do the same when corruption comes to the foot.
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	 if it comes to the first joint, then cut after the next joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	 and if it reaches the foot, then cut off the entire foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	 and if it moves up the leg, then cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	 and if it comes above the knee, there is no other recourse than to leave the patient to die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	 And the way to use the copper or silk member is that you bind it above and below, and have one assistant extend one of the ligatures downwards, and another the other ligature upwards, and you cut away the flesh that is between the two ligatures to a width of one thumb, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 Then take the copper or silk, and place a linen cloth on each side, so that the silk does not touch the healthy area, and another infection or abscess will come to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	 And if bleeding occurs as you work, then cauterize the area immediately, or apply some powder that constricts;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then return to your task until it is complete, then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it heals.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	 And I will tell you that it happened to a man in his feet:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	 It happened to him that a blackness appeared on him as if it were a burn from fire, and this corrosion first came upon his big toe of the foot, so much so that it spread throughout the entire foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	 And when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover the foot, and was healthy.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	 And after a long time the corrosion returned to his thumb of the hand, and he came to me, and I put repercussive things on him after cleansing his body, but the corrosion could not cease.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	 And he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to, for I had hope of expelling the material.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	 And I also feared that if I cut his hand, he would die, for the man's strength was weak;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	 and he became completely hopeless, returned to his land, covered his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And I have only told this account in order that others may do the same if they find it necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	 Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy place and stays so long that it causes a large accumulation of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	 and then it breaks open and bursts, and the pus jumps out, leaving the place empty, like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	 and the skin on top is as thin as fine cloth, and it does not extend to the bone or the nerve. Such an illness is called "sinus" and is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	 If it is so elongated that it reaches to the bone perfectly, then it is called "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	 And the skin is such that you should cut all around this skin, even when it is subtle, just like a piece of cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 and it does not rot due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	 And if you think that the skin will rot and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with a clyster in this manner:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	 check if the breast is large and the pus that comes out of it is foul-smelling, then give a clyster with Egyptian medicine made in this way:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	 take equal parts of asphalt, oil, and litharge (lead oxide), and put them to cook in a vessel over the fire until the medicine becomes red and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	 And then take of this according to your need, and make it into a mixture with water and honey, and use it as an enema on the chest, and constrict the anus.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	 And let the medicine stay in for two hours, then remove it by pressing out.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	 Do this many times until the chest is clean, and the pus is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	 And sometimes use an enema of ashes water, when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes of vine wood, and pour water over them, then strain it, and use it as an enema until you know that the chest is well cleaned.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	 And if the patient cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ashes water, then use an enema of water and honey in which there is a little powdered lead.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	 or you cleanse it with honey and mixed wine, for the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the flesh dry;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	 and when you have done this, and are confident that the breast is well cleansed, then cleanse it with that which causes flesh to grow in it, which is to take a definite plaster, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	 or you cleanse it with some medicinal herbs and onions, of which I have spoken the properties in the treatment of onions;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	 and if the hole in the breast is small and the tube of the enema cannot enter, then widen it a little with an iron, and put inside a tent of Egyptian onion, or Basilicum onion, until it is widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if the wound is too wide, then sew it and leave an opening only where the enema can enter; and if the aperture that the bladder makes is on top, then cut it off or to a lower place than it was.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	 For when the bladder is burst, do not allow any flesh to enter;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	 And if you cannot cut the bladder as you see fit, then arrange it in such a way that the bladder moves to the lowest place possible; for when the bladder is burst, do not allow any flesh to enter. And if you cannot cut the bladder as you see fit, then arrange it in such a manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	 so that the bladder slides gently downwards, and leave nothing of the bladder there;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	 And take consolidative medicines to apply to the wound, and extend on a linen cloth that covers all the wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	 then press as firmly as possible around the hole in the vein with a larger cloth than the first, then apply soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the hole, and place it on the hole in the wound to lighten the weight, and do not remove the large cloth until after several days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	 and the one that is on the hole in the vein, remove often to remove the weight, and know what comes out of the weight, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digestible, or undigestible;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	 and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been applied in this manner and you see what nature rises on the hole in the wound, know that the vein has already closed, and health approaches;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 And then unbind it in the morning, or on the third day; and when you unbind the wound, change the bandage and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	 And if the breast casts out undigested food after many days, know that the breast does not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poisons pass after a long time, do not despair of health, for healing approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	 For there are men in whom the flesh delays to heal in their wounds, and of those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	 And if the undigested food rises from the stomach after many days, know that the stomach is not healthy.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	 And if the stomach delays in healing and is distant, apply drying moist substances with drying power, such as diaphoretic ointment, for it contains a large amount of vitriol, and that is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	 Take diaphoretic ointment and make it with rose oil and wash it with equal parts of old wine.
puis le confit et en use;	 Then crush it and apply it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	 And if the same substance is more swollen when cooked, and onion is not available, you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and powder it on the honey while it is over the fire.
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	 And then in a cloth bandage, and apply it to the breast, and sometimes administer a long cataplasm of lily roots, which is also like pea flour and celery.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	 And make use of simple or compound [remedies].
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	 Grind them, and make into a powder, and put on the honey that I have mentioned, and apply it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	 And if the wound is prolonged and not healed by this treatment, then know that the corruption has gone deep and affects the bone, or the hard parts, or the tendons.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 Si the treatment of the treatment of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	 of the abscess of the fingernail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	 Paronychia is an abscess that forms under the fingernail or toenail of the hand or foot, or occasionally it can form in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	 and when it is neglected, and nothing is done about it, then an abscess like this forms, and it runs and throws pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and sometimes it can even reach all the way to the end.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 and the corruption reaches the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the toe is swollen, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away with an iron all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	 Cautery is very helpful if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	 And if the nail presses into the flesh and begins to prick and wound it, then you must place the reed under the nail that points at the flesh, push it up, cut away that flesh delicately and lightly, and apply burning and corrosive medicines on the rest of the flesh to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then heal with ointments until he is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	 And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it out and draw strongly, for as long as the corrupted bone remains there, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if you see the finger corrupting, cut it off at the first joint as was said before, then heal until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	 And if it is pierced and swollen and there is great pain, then you must heal it first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	 then cut the fingernail of the patient obliquely from above, and ensure that the cutting does not reach the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 and if it happens, place something on it to soothe [the pain].
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	 The pain from the shoulder of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The two bones that sometimes grow in the hands of some men are sometimes entirely fleshy, and sometimes there is bone, and occasionally there is a claw, and sometimes they grow at the root of the joint, or the growth is in some people’s fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	 He who is born under the knuckle of the finger does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the finger, perhaps moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	 The cutting of the one who is fleshy is light in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	 He who is born in the root of the joint is difficult to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	 if you hold back from cutting [it].
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In one who is born or should at the anus, it is necessary that you cut the flesh roundly until the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable size for him, then cure him until he is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	 The union that comes to the two together comes by birth, or by union of a wound, or by cauterization with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	 Therefore, you must cut that suture, so that it may heal according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	 Then place between two tents or cloths soaked in rose oil, lest they stick together.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 or you can place between two thin sheets of lead until the place is soldered, as needed.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	 If suddenly one of his fingers comes with the palm, strike that suture as needed.
des vils	 from worthless
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	 Veins are large wounds filled with superfluous melancholic substances that come in many parts of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	 Therefore, you should administer to him some purging of bile, and then heal it with the holy basilicum.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	 The treatment with iron is according to two methods:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	 one is that they are cut, and then one draws out the black blood with an iron.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 and the other method is that you lift the wound, and draw it all out with an iron.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	 The cut is done in this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	 the first rises with very hot vinegar so strongly that the large vein is made fine, then hold the patient's leg from above the thigh down to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	 then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision, then raise and pull strongly to draw out the black blood into your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient's strength can bear;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	 and then bandage it, and instruct him to eat foods that produce black bile.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 and renew the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full again, and benefit the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	 The elevation of it is according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	 take the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put it in the bath, and wash the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and swell the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	 and if you do not have a bath, then warm it at the fire, and then cut towards the vein along the thigh to the knee, or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	 then peel back the skin, and scrape the vein from each side until it appears when touched;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	 and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems like a white cord; xspace
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	 Then push the hair under, so that it is raised from the skin, and then attach it lightly with a needle, then cut it in another place above three fingers;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	 Then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it with a razor, as you have done, and attach it to another needle, as you did before;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	 Then cut another shape, or several if you need them, then lift it and cut at the finger of the foot, then draw and lift until the second shape;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	 Then draw it from shape to shape until it comes out completely, then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	 And if you cannot draw and lift it, then insert a very strong needle with a double thread, and tie and draw it, and push it under the hair, and turn your hand from one side to another until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	 And be careful that it does not cut, for if it cuts, then one cannot draw or lift it, and it causes harm to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	 And when you have drawn it all out, then place wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And tend to it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	 And if the vein is twisted and wrapped together and is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it carefully, but do not cut it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And draw it out as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	 The shape of the iron used to cut the vein is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not cut the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 And it is of thick curvature, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said. And here is its form.
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	 This vein is engorged in legs, in hot places where no grass or tree grows, and in land where there is no moisture.
