et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 and by chance it appears elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to corruption that comes under the skin, just as snakes and worms appear within the body, engorged between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is such that a very great inflammation comes into the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to emerge like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	 When the shoulder dislocates, you should wrap around it a piece of linen from one and a half to two and a half cubits, and knot it, and let the linen hang on the leg, and every time it comes out due to weakness, wrap it again with the linen and knot.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	 And if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut near the base until all of it has come out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	 because if you cut it, then it enters into the flesh, and brings forth an abscess and pus in that place, and causes a severe illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	 for which reason it must be treated little by little until the end, and nothing should remain in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	 and sometimes this vein when it is treated with five or ten palms in length, and a man came to me whose vein was ten palms long, and when you cut it, then one or two ribs or openings burst forth, and it goes through until the end, so that everything comes out;
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 and let the matter inside be emptied, and apply to the place medicines that prevent pus every day, then treat it as you would with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	 And sometimes at this vein there are fewer waters, and especially when it opens in the foot's joint or in the foot, and there comes much water from it, and because of which it becomes rare;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 then heal it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	 This illness is called in our land "cattle disease," because it often happens to cattle. It is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and goes through the whole body ascending and descending, and one feels it well when moving from member to member, until it tears the skin where it goes, and jumps out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	 And it is infected by the corruption of some humors, like worms and snakes and leeches and roundworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	 And one fears its harmfulness, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps it enters and destroys the eye.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	 And this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	 When you see it being cured and drawn out, one cannot go too far until it has gone away:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	 then you must bind the place above and below with a strong tie very tightly, then cut on top and pull out strongly, and if the pus is deep in the flesh and you cannot find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	 And the greatest harm that it does is to blind the eye, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	 And if you see it coming toward the head near the eye, tightly bind under it the eyelid, then cut on top and pull out strongly.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 and it is necessary to use the patient for body cleansing with soluble medications for bad humors, and avoid foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 from the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	 This disease is called in our land "vakirir," and it is a pain that comes in some members, and then moves from member to member;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 and I saw this happen as I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	 I was called to an ill woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	 and soon after, I saw it rise like a worm on her shoulder, faster than anything else, as if it were alive silver when it runs from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	 the pain left that place and inserted itself in the shoulder, and then a little later it ran throughout the body, until it came to the other arm;  ?> li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 Then she told me that she was always turning around the body, as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	 Je me demande beaucoup comment elle change ainsi d'un membre à l'autre, car je n'avais jamais vu cette maladie se manifester de cette façon auparavant.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	 However, I had seen many who well had wanted to move pain from one place to another, but I did not see it as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	 and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and open veins, and therefore appeared this forced windiness.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 And they did not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate, and have moist bodies and filled veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	 And when you see this disease being treated, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then strike quickly above and below, and then cut until that forced windiness comes out of its place;
et cauterize le leu;	 And cauterize the place;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 and if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat it with those that expel flatulence, such as foul-smelling pills, and mugwort pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	 Et si tu ne vois pas de flèches
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	 Les flèches sont variées, selon leurs apparences et selon les endroits du corps où elles atterrissent.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	 The differences in their kind is that there are those which have large points, and small ones, and hooked, and welded.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	 and of those which have two prongs, and of those which have tongues, and of those where there are parts;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	 and if it falls into any member, it falls in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 or in a principal member, such as brain, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	 When it falls then in any place of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you afterward appear to you.
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	 you must beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death follows in many ways;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then remove it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	 And the signs of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and leaps the sutures that are above the brain, are: scotoma, drowsiness, faintness, redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm, confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	 And perhaps it is without force of the nostrils or the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	 and perhaps he loses his speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	 and from the wound comes white moisture resembling pus, and it leaps out like flesh broth.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And if these signs appear to you, then take care of the cure, and draw out the arrow if it is there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	 The signs of the arrow when it falls into the heart are that it is near the left nipple, and it feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	 And perhaps the arrow moves as if it were pus, and black blood comes out, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 Know then without doubt that death follows.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	 And the sign of the arrowhead that never comes out without foam or bubbles from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	 And if the arrow falls into the cover of the foot, it is near the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	 and it causes great pain and suffering.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	 And it moves all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	 And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps something undigested comes out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	 And if the arrow falls into the belly, and some feces come out through the rectum, then there is no hope for a cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	 And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine leaps out and flows away, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	 know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	 The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulders and arms and spine of the back and chest and hips and legs, and similar members, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	 When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery, and it is not poisoned, as I will tell you happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	 It happened to a man, an arrow fell into the arm in the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 I extracted it and drew it out from another side beneath the fat of the ear, and he was healed without injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	 And he drew an arrow that fell into the fat of the eye beneath the skin, and the arrow was bent, and he could only reach its tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was as large as a Turkish bow, with all the iron very light without ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 The game was completed, and no bad incident happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	 And he drew an arrow from his throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic in nature:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 I shaved my beard, and acted subtly until I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	 And I drew an arrow from a man into whose belly it had fallen, and thought that he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	 and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change at all.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 I cut into the arrow, extracted it with force, and he had no bad incident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	 And then I saw a man onto whom an arrow fell on his back, and the wound was closed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And the arrow remained within him, and did not change its natural disposition in any way, nor was it disturbed in any of its natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	 And he saw another man, into whose face an arrow fell and the wound closed up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	 and he remained thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	 and many other similar ones.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	 And one threw an arrow at a man of the king's nobles, which had fallen into his nose, and was leaning slightly to the right side; abei
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	 and the arrow was completely lodged.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 I was called to treat it after it had fallen for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 Si je trouve la plaie très étroite.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	 I touched it all over with a subtle probe, and felt nothing;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 And he felt a stabbing pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	 I thought it was the tip of an arrow, I applied a poultice that is attractive and digestive on the spot, so that the place would not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 And I saw the place where the arrow had entered.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	 I applied the poultice for several days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained in this state for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his nose;
et il le me dist.	 And he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	 I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was open, and then I probed it, and felt the tip of the arrow which had turned in place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	 Then I inserted into the opening of the wound using that sharp medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared clearly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	 And it exceeded the limit by three months, and then the wound healed so much that when I put the pincers in, I could not pull out [the arrowhead] from either side.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 Then I did not stop trying and contriving various instruments until I got it with well-made pincers, as will be described at the end of this chapter, so that I pulled it out and the wound healed.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	 And physicians judge that the nasal septum cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 I then restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	 Or I have told you the nature of extracting certain arrows, so that you may apply your care to what I do not say, for the book cannot comprehend everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 but the wise master comprehends very little and only what is present and failing; he finds nine works and nine instruments in the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	 I say that arrows should not be removed from the members into which they are inserted except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	 or through the place where they entered, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 and that which should come out from where it entered is an arrow entering fleshy places, and sometimes now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	 And if it does not jump now, let it remain until the flesh is rotten around, and the exit be cleared.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	 And similarly, if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, let it remain thus for several days, and move it each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And then it will jump out, and if it does not, pierce all around with the finest needle until the place is enlarged, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	 And if the arrow is stuck in the skull bone and goes into one of the cavities of the brain, and some of the things I have mentioned happen to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 Do not draw it out, but let it remain until it is equal after some days, for if the arrow reaches the sinus, it means death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not fixed firmly only in the bone, and does not reach up to the surface, and the patient remains for some days without any bad incident, then use the tool of pulling.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	 And if it is very firmly lodged and cannot come out by force, then apply tourniquets around it, as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	 And if the arrowhead has returned to its place in the body and cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the entire area.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	 and if you feel it, then draw it out with some suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	 and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrowhead, and there are no bones, nerves or veins, then widen it until the wound is large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	 and draw out the arrowhead if you can, and if there are barbs on the arrowhead that hold it in place, then cut away the flesh from two sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the barbs of the arrowhead until you can draw it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And handle it carefully so that you do not break the arrow, which would wound more severely.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	 And if you cannot do it all at once, leave it until the place around is rotten, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easy.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	 And if the flow of blood seems contrary to you, then proceed as we have said in the chapter on treatment;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	 And beware of cutting the nerve or vein, and devise a way how you may draw out the arrow safely, whether early or late, strongly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And put the patient in the same position he was in when the arrow struck him, for that is the greatest help there can be; and if you cannot do this, then place him according to the signs that show you how.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	 An arrow that comes from another place, or where it protrudes something from it, or the skin is swollen there so that one sees or feels it clearly: 
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	 Cut it off, so that the pincers can take hold of it, and then extract it.
si saut fuer maintenant.	 If it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	 And if it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand roundly until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	 And if she cannot come out, leave her there and then begin the extraction again until she comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	 And if part of the arrow is still in there, push it all the way to the shaft.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	 And if the shaft has broken off, and you see that a push will be necessary, then use an instrument with a notch, so that the arrowhead fits into the notch of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And then push hard, and if the arrow is splintered, push in an instrument with a pointed end to ease extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is poisoned, you must cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	 And if an arrow falls into the belly or the stomach or the bladder or the side, and it is close to the surface, and you can reach it with a knife, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	 And take care not to cut the vein or the nerve, and then extract it, and then close the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And treat until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	 The shape of the pincers used to remove arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	 And there are many kinds of them:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	 large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the arrowhead tip is like the feather of a bird, to pierce the point of the arrow, as shown here in this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	 The shape of the pincers for pushing and extracting is as follows.
des voinnes dou cors communes	 common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	 There are XXXI wounds from which one can heal, of which there are sixteen in the head, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	 Two hollows located after the ears, called the "two herbaceous".
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	 And the two arteries which are in the two temples of the head.
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	 And two veins that are in the two eyelids, which are called "aspirers".
et li voine que est emmi le front;	 And the vein that is on the forehead.
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	 And the vein that is at the tip of the nose.
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	 And the two windpipes which are in the neck.
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	 And the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augerich".
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 And two veins which are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	 The veins which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	 One is the cephalic, and it is from the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	 And the remedy is called "fennel," and it is composed of celery and basil, and the common people call it "vein of the heart.
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 And the basil is in the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly," and it is on the fascia, and it is that one by which one heals, which clearly appears on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	 And the savatelle is the vein between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	 And in the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	 one is below the crook of the left wrist, and the second sophone is at the ankle of the right side.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	 And the vein which is called "nesse," that is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And in the other leg there are three veins beneath these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	 The opening of the veins which are after the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	 And the quality of the opening is that you raise the head of the patient and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	 Then the patient should squeeze his neck with one hand, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two hanging places from the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	 Cut them then with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, press firmly;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	 Then take the lancet, and push it under the vein until the bone, then lift your hand along with the entire vein, and cut both the skin and the vein well into two parts, and make the blood come out as much as you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 Then hold it tight and bind it until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 And I have already spoken of the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	 The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is good for chronic migraine, and inflammation, and chronic glaucoma, and for acute tears of the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	 And the quality of the bleeding is as I have said:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	 And it is that the patient should hold his neck, so that the two veins appear clearly.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	 And feel your thumb under your toe, then signify so.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	 then lift the curved needle above the vein at your toe's tip, and insert the lancet below, and lift the vein up, and cut it, just as you have done with two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	 then unbind the patient, and place your toe on the vein for an hour, then put cotton over it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 and then bandage it firmly, and leave it until it heals.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 and we have already spoken about their cutting and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	 The bleeding from the vein of the forehead is as valuable as the bleeding from the cephalic for ancient facial diseases, and for migraines, and for redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	 And the quality is such that the patient stretches his neck by twisting it until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 then take the instrument called "fosseur", of which here is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	 And place the tip on the vein, and strike with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you wish.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 then release the patient's neck and bind the vein until it is healed and sometimes work with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	 However, it should not be that the flame is too sharp;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	 and heal obliquely, for the bone is close by, and perhaps breaks the flame when it is delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	 The bleeding of the two veins that are in the two temples helps with the eyes, and with alopecia, and with redness, and with the little vein in the eye, and with diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	 And the quality of their bleeding is such that the patient should tighten his neck by twisting some rope, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 Then let it bleed, and the bleeding should be from a hole, a little long rather than wide, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	 And if the flame is delicate, perhaps it will break.
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	 Then make the blood flow as much as you need, and then tie it with a cotton cloth, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	 The bleeding of the nose vein is good for fever, and for madness, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that occurs in the face, and especially when it is chronic.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	 And the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient strains his neck, then presses his nose against your left hand, and takes the fine long flame, and inserts it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	 And do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your needs, then bind it for one night, because it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 And this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	 The bleeding of the two jugulars helps with the narrowing of the vein, and with the beginning of leprosy, and with many illnesses, and with pustules, and with ulcers, and with shingles.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	 And the quality of the bloodletting is such that the patient should stretch his neck under one and the other, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	 And let the master be standing over the patient's head, and the patient sit on a stool. Then open the vein along its length widely, then draw blood gently or as much as is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	 Then do the same on the other vein, then untie the bandage, and stretch all the veins moderately so that the patient does not choke.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 And leave it until morning, so that the wound may be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	 of liver bleeding
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	 The bleeding from the wounds of the lips above thus helps to heal in the mouth, and causes decay of the gums, and splitting of the lips, and of the nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	 And the quality of bloodletting is to make the patient sit in front of you and stretch his neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	 Then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is in the right lip and the other in the left, and they are recognized by being black, and because around them there are small black veins.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 So cut both of them, and if you do not recognize them or are in doubt, then cut the thicker one from each side, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 Of the wound beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	 The bleeding of the veins that are under the tongue helps after the bleeding of the cephalic (vein), and it is for the constriction of the throat, and for the diseases of the eye, and for the diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	 And the quality of the sick person is such that he lies between your hands in front of the sun, and he raises his tongue, and looks down on each side a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 Heal one and the other, and do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	 The veins of the knife with which one commonly heals are healed in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	 either by piercing with all the flame of a large mirror or an olive-shaped subtle knife, and it is called "anaesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 and they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	 The form of the burning ember is very famous, and it is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	 And it is necessary to open the swollen veins that are full of thick and visible blood, which contain large and turbid blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And this is the form of the olive oil flame
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	 And it is more finely pointed, and is for healing fine veins, where there is fine citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	 The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps against diseases under the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 And it is necessary for the physician to draw wisely, and to guard against the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	 And if he cuts the artery, and blood comes out, then he must cauterize it, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And the flame should not be pricking, but cutting like a lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	 And if the basilica does not open clearly, then you must constrict it and seek another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	 Or where you wish to take some blood from him, or you heal in his place the vein within the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	 it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 and clamp with the flame cautery, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	 And if you wish to know the place of the vein, then first you must stretch the arm so that you touch the place until you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	 then mark the place with a cross, and then tie the arm, and clamp the vein with the flame cautery.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	 and beware not to strike an artery when you see the place swelling, for it is from the artery:
eschui la donques.	 avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	 And if you see it spurt out like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from an artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	 hurry then, and place your finger firmly, then remove your finger if it is stained with blood, for this often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	 if the arm moves, let it be, and do not move it yourself, the patient.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and act cautiously, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	 And if the blood is not stained, and it flows away from you, and the doctor is not present, cut the artery if it is open, for the head of the vein will retract.
et estainche li sans.	 and staunch the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	 And take a piece of fig bark, and split it, and take one half and bind it firmly until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	 if the blood is staunched, that is good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	 If not, then treat it with powders that stop bleeding;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 And the treatment is not suitable in many conditions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	 The bleeding from the middle of the vein is such that it draws blood from above and below, because it is composed of the basilic vein and the cephalic vein, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	 and it is necessary for the bleeder to be careful of the nerve that is below, and if he goes too deep, and finds the nerve, and it swells, and the healing is not suitable, and perhaps it cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	 And this nerve often opens up, and if it does not open in some men due to its subtlety, then you must cauterize it with the instrument called "anesil";
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 And let the nerve slip away as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	 And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	 The vein of the cephalic also helps, as it draws blood from the head, and it helps with the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 and it is necessary to cut deep into the olive vein or the myrtle vein, because that is the safest of all the veins, because there is neither nerve nor artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	 Nevertheless, one should seek the lightest place, and do not worry if one misses the first time, and start again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 and perhaps the spot swells for some men when one misses the first time, but it does not matter.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	 The quality of the bleeding depends on your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	 The first thing you should know about bloodletting is that bloodletting is practiced only to maintain health and to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	 And let the bloodletting be done in one of the three veins that are in the hand:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	 that is to say, cephalic, fast, and basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	 and one should bleed at the beginning of spring, in autumn, and in winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	 The bloodletting that is used for illnesses has no fixed hour, but rather whenever needed during the day or night, at all hours and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 And it is not appropriate to bleed children until fourteen years of age, nor women who are pregnant beyond the fourth month up to the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	 Nor should the old who have passed sixty years be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	 And when someone wants to heal, in whatever manner it may be, he must cleanse the intestines with a light enema if he has retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines the harmful superfluities into the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	 nor does he heal who is too full of food, or drunk, while still inebriated, or who are dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	 and if one attempts to heal after colic, vomiting, diarrhea, multiple miscarriages in women, labor, vigil, fasting, or anything that entirely diminishes the strength of a person by a weapon or disease.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	 then refine the humors if the blood is thick with foods and drinks and medicines if you have the means.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	 then enter into the bath, if nothing prevents you, to make the blood thin, and heal from the wound of the foot around the third part, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	 and guard yourself that day against work, and pain, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	 and be happy and joyful, and let the bandages be higher than those of one being healed, and rub the arm two or three times, then draw the ligature moderately tight, for when it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	 and then rub the area with the hands, so that the veins swell and are felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 then moisten the bandages with a little old oil, then place his left hand’s finger on that vein beneath the area where he wishes to heal, so that the vein does not flee and evade at the time of healing.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	 Car there are veins that bleed like strings for the bowyer, and there are some filled with windiness, so that when one applies fire, it draws back from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus one is in such a state.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 And if he opens the vein, the wound is too tight, therefore it is necessary that the bowyer be knowledgeable in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	 And if the vein opens on the first attempt, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	 If not, then he should try again a little lower or higher in haste, unless the place is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	 And if the place is swollen and the patient is afraid, let him wait for one day or two, and do not tie the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	 by chance such abscesses may occur
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	 do not enter a bath, then resume the bleeding if it pleases him;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	 and if the orifice is small, or the blood flows subtly, and you doubt that not as much blood will come out as you wish, then thrust into this same orifice all the flame straightaway;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	 and perform it a little hastily, before the place swells;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	 If you see the place swollen, do not begin the bleeding again, and put a little bit of oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the oil is better than oil;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	 And thus administer the juice of oil into each wound that you open the veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	 And this same act as a poultice and boil of them, when one places it on the wound.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If it refines the blood and separates when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	 And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, especially when it is not opened strongly except for that time when the opening of the vein is small, then hurry, and place on the wound a sponge moistened in water and in salt a little hot, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	 And you must do this after the discharge of blood from the vein, and if there remains on the wound after some days any blackness or greenness, it will not harm him.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if you see, put on some substance of aloe or myrrh mixed in calamint juice, mustard, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	 And often there is an abscess and appearance at the base of the skull:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	 put your hand on it, and if you find the spot soft to the touch of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	 Therefore do not put on it any substance of what we have said, for perhaps it is bursting from the artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 but make a dry poultice to harden the spot, then heal it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	 And draw out some of the blood according to its quantity and power, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	 For if the blood is black, let it issue until it becomes red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	 And if you see it swollen, let it be until it is drained;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	 And if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	 And he who is full and strong, and needs bloodletting, should have a larger wound made, and the flame should be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	 And for the weak one, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed often and frequently, and he should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And this manner of bleeding is safe from excessive blood loss and nerve damage, and it is better than the long or wide incisions for bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	 And to him whose body lacks strength for bloodletting, it is necessary to give moistened bread in apple juice.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 If he is heated, draw blood three times or four, and if he has a cold constitution, let him chew bread soaked in syrup of muscadine, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if he faints from blood loss, after losing much blood, it is necessary that he drink broth made of meat, and a subtle, fragrant syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the section on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	 And if he wants to drain his arm and bleed another time, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great blood loss, that he bleed little by little, according to the amount of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	 And if he wants to drain his arm after the first blood letting and he has a strong body, then let him bleed seven hours after the first blood letting, or in the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	 And whoever wishes to heal from another place, must be healed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	 For there is much blood within the body which is already heated, and causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	 then one must draw out a large quantity of it, and widen the opening until it reaches as far as possible.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	 after you have observed all the conditions of bloodletting, and place your hand over his pulse when he is bleeding, so that death does not occur in place of healing, and this often happens when the bleeder is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	 And it is not necessary when you see to dislocate the arm and cause blood to flow a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press very hard;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	 or if it is crooked, let him extend the arm quickly, for this would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	 but leave it until it heals a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 or you press at the tip with the flame until the frozen blood that has gathered in the wound flows out, and place on it a little cloth soaked in water and press lightly on top.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	 Et s'il est enfle, laissez-le et ne le serrez pas, jusqu'à ce que l'inflammation soit calmée.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	 And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, then heal it in the same place or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	 The vein in the arm is healed in the place of the head's vein because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	 And the manner of healing is such that the patient plunges his hand into hot water until the flesh is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	 then it should be moderately bound so that the wound appears well, then let it heal now across, not wide or long; xspace
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	 And let the opening be wide, and let it be cauterized close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, then put the hand in hot water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	 And if it is in summer, do not put the hand in hot water, for one puts it more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the cautery of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there are neither artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	 The cautery of the little vein of the right hand is effective against all liver diseases, and this is how it is done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	 Hold the hand firmly and put it in hot water until the vein swells up, if one can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	 And if the wound is at an angle, and you cut it completely through, then it does not matter.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 And do not go too deep, for the nerves are all bare of flesh beneath, and then place the hand in hot water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	 Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile and seil por souder hastanment, and ensi fai de chescun rain.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	 The wound on his left hand is equivalent to the illness of leprosy, and it does all the same as I have told you concerning the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The wound on the shin is equivalent to all the diseases that are beneath the body, such as diseases of the womb, and retention of flowers, and diseases of the kidneys, and of the thighs and ancient legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	 And the quality of his wound is such that the patient should place his foot in hot water, and rub on the wound until it bursts, and bind it above the ankle.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	 And the wound is at the ankle, and there are many veins that run upward from the foot;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 Cut it then in the widest vein, or at the ankle, whatever is best.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	 And if you heal it on the foot, then beware of the nerves that are beneath, and make the incision across like in cupping;
et soit li flaimes anesil.	 and let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	 And if the pus cannot come out, put the foot back in water, and allow the wound to drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	 And if the incision fails the first time, then start again a little higher on the second attempt, for the place is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 nor should you doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the saphena of the other foot likewise.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	 The place of the sciatic wound is on the ankle bone, and its healing is worth against hip pain, when it is for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	 And the characteristic of its incision is that the patient enters the bath, and draws over the ankle four fingers in twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	 and if it opens, then incise it in all the ways that you can, and across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And it is better for you to cut it off, because the place is open, and it is very painful in many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	 And if you cannot find it, then cut off some of the flesh that is open on the back of the foot, towards the small toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	 And make the blood flow as much as you see fit, and then untie the bandage, and put on cotton and bind it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	 She is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 of bleeding cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	 Cupping glasses are made of horn, or bronze, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	 And cupping is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	 Either by drawing blood or without drawing blood.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	 And this cupping which is done without drawing blood is done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	 Or she is all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	 and venesection which is done by cutting and extracting blood is done in fourteen places of the body, one of which is completely on top of the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	 and the other is in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	 and two others in both sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	 and the cupping glass under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	 and the cupping glasses on both shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	 and the cupping glasses on the buttocks;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	 and the cupping glasses in both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	 and the cupping glasses on both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	 and the cupping glasses on both ankles; xspace
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	 and the venesection does not draw blood, except for the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken anyone at all, as is done with bloodletting from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And it is not necessary that she be purged, by any fire or without fire, in any disease that comes from fullness, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	 And if because of illnesses it is necessary to bleed or by custom, then we administer (it) each hour at the beginning of the month, in the middle and in every time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	 for there are some who, when they need to bleed, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	 and there are those who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and on the neck, and darkness to the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	 and there are those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and spit blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And there are some who dream of blood and wounds and death and such things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	 And when we see these signs, especially when it is in the middle of the month, we instruct them to venesect after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	 The sinus of the nose also helps against the coldness of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary for this to be after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	 and this ventilation is in place of the sinus of the head, and it is not necessary for those who are of cold temperament to use it, or who have catarrh, because it does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 And therefore it is not necessary for the elderly to use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	 And those who bleed often from it become foolish, and therefore it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower because of the fear of folly.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	 The ventilation in the neck is in place of the sinus of the head and basilica, and therefore it is useful for the constriction of the bladder, and for the rupture of the urinary canal of the scrotum, and for stone, and for retention;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 And there you should put a little, for if it holds too firmly, it causes obstruction of the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	 The ventosations at the two ribs of the neck are good for headaches, and migraines, and strangulation, and toothache, and it is in the place of the basilica's venesection.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 And you should instruct the bloodletter to press his hand well, so that he does not cut the artery and cause an uncontrollable flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	 The ventosations under the chin are good for mouth diseases, and for rotting of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	 And it is in the place of the venesection of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	 The ventosations of the shoulders are good for illnesses caused by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	 The punctures of the ribs are worth as much as three veins of the arm, because they draw blood from those large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 and instruct the physician not to strike too deeply into the flesh, because the place is bare of meat, and beneath are nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	 The cupping glass that is on the buttocks is worth against hemorrhoids of the anus, and against diseases below, and it must be large, and made of bronze, so that it can draw well.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	 and perhaps, if it were delicate, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	 and it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	 The cupping glasses on the legs heal openly, because they draw blood from the entire body, and are worth against old pains of the kidneys, and of the spleen, and of the bladder, and remove flows.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	 And they are in the place of two spleens and two ankles, however they weaken the body after long use, and bring paralysis in many ways.
