Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	 The manner of placing the cupping glass is to first place it empty, and suck quickly, and put it on hastily, and move it evenly, and do not cease from doing this, until you see the place red and swollen, and appear the redness of the blood;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	 then burn, and put on the cupping glasses again, and take care according to the condition of the body, for there are some who have dark flesh and clear pores;
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	 so it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a deep cut.
et suce legierement.	 And suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	 And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	 The first time to clear the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	 And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	 and when we want to draw the blood little by little, we need only one strike.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	 And if we want a lot of blood, then we must do it often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	 and if the blood is thick, strike deeply, and the end result should be that the heart is pierced suddenly, and those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, must anoint the places of the cups with opening and dissolving oil.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	 If it is inflamed, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if it is swollen, use watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	 And if the superfluidities are thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the one being healed has tender flesh and large pores, oil must not be applied there, but it should be washed afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or mallow water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar water.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	 And the one with much moisture should be treated with ease, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	 And those who have large superfluous fluids should drink old wine, or the water of swine, or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	 and it is not appropriate to use a cupping glass before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And do not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that one wash, both before and after being cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	 And watch out if the patient is choleric, and if his blood is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	 then he should take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce in vinegar, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 and minced partridges, and roasted meat, and moist dishes.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	 And the one who has a cold temperament should take syrup of honey, and wine that is moderately fragrant, between old and new, and minced peas, and minced partridges and small birds and thrushes;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	 and on the day he bleeds himself, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	 and it is necessary to give some men sometimes a tricacle or musk before bleeding, or after, to strengthen the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And let the blood be drained, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	 The cupping glasses that are placed without puncturing are those placed on the liver, and the bladder, and gout, and on the belly and the breast and the kidneys and the hip, for these members do not allow puncturing, and one does this only to attract blood from one member to another, as we do on the breasts when the nipples bleed;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	 To remove the thickness that is in the member, as we place cupping glasses on the belly and the breast to reduce the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	 And removes the pain when there is a swelling or stone, and by its attractive power perhaps removes the swelling, or moves the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	 And so it does when placed on the liver and bladder when there is retained wind, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only that.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 And sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in pleurisy, and in such a manner that one fills the cupping glass only with hot water or water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	 The form of the cupping glass administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	 And it should be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, and on the side around the middle there should be a small hole, like for inserting a needle, and it should be made of bronze, softened beforehand so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	 And let there be in the middle a rod of cross sectional area made of brass or iron, to place a compress there, and they should be both large and small according to the diseases and age of those who use them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 for the cupping glasses of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	 And one should thus place this cupping glass on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	 grasp the compress of wax or linen, and place it inside the cupping glass across the rod that is inside the cupping glass, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	 and then place it on the member, and your two fingers should be on the hole that we have mentioned, so that when one wishes, the steam escapes, and remove the cupping glass.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And use linen as before, and often repeat it if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	 In the cupping glass which is used for pleurisy, there is no rod or hole, and it is only prepared when full of water, and it is placed on the member alone;
et c’est li forme:	 and this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	 Leaches are only prepared when they are to be placed in members where a cupping glass cannot be used because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	 And in fleshless places, such as fingers or noses, and other similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	 And the quality of using them is that when you find leeches that are in clean fresh water without any stench, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	 And he puts them in a vessel of fresh water, until they become accustomed to it, and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	 And then let them be bled by venesection and cupping, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and apply leeches.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 And when they are full and fall off, if it is a place where a cupping glass can be applied, he should apply one, for this is very effective afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	 If not, then raise the place with a poultice of barley and then with water, very well, and then bandage it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	 And if the place bleeds too much after the removal of the leeches, then soak a linen cloth in cold water and apply it until the bleeding stops.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	 And if the blood is increased, then apply ground vitriol or gallnuts and similar things until it is dried out.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	 Or take half of the peeled beans and place them on the spot, leaving them until they dry out in place, this will stop the bleeding now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 And if you need more, then take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	 And if the leeches do not want to attach, then rub the spot with fresh blood, or insert a needle until the blood comes out, and then place them on, and as soon as they sense the blood, they will attach.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And when you see that they are falling off, then sprinkle on a little powder of ground aloe and gum, or ashes, and they will fall off now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	 Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	 This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the treatment of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	 Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	 et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	 et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	 It is necessary therefore that we say in the prologue of this book the sums of the words and the chapters where the wise man places his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	 I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or splintering occurs in someone, then you must hasten to heal the patient from one side and the other, if anything hinders you completely, such as physical weakness, or childhood, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	 Or if the time is not very hot, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	 And avoid cold food, that is to say cold soups, and bird meat and rabbit, and do not drink wine, nor eat fatty foods, and do not fill oneself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess or swelling in the limb.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 If the patient returns to his previous diet.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	 And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to feed the patient with foods that promote thickening, such as wheat cooked in water, rice, heads (of animals), feet, calf's foot, eggs, fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	 For with such nourishment the bones heal more quickly and sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	 And know that broken bones of the old and decayed cannot be well taken or healed according to their nature due to the dryness of the members, nor can those which are too tender, such as the bones of young children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	 but do not worry, reset on top of the broken bone with strong clamps that hold and join the member together, until it is reinforced as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 and do not completely hinder its work, and for this reason it must be fed with coarse foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	 Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses en maintes manieres.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	 Because the fracture of the head is different from that of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	 Because there is a fracture that goes to the bone marrow, and another in slicing, as when cutting a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	 And there is a fracture with wound, and a fracture which is just a small crack all around.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	 And each kind should have its own device and proper tool for the restoration, according to what comes to mind in its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	 and it is known that the break of the bone occurs because the place is twisted, and it swells well on the outside, and resounds when pressed with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	 And when there is no fracture or breakage, and the patient does not feel great pain.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 But he may well have a dislocation, or a split, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	 If you must not move it by hand, but apply the following medications, and then delicately secure it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	 And know that the breaks that go in the direction of length, and the two parts are separated, it is necessary to now set them equally, before an abscess forms there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	 And if an abscess forms there, then leave it alone for some days, until the abscess is reduced.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	 Then align it equally with a screw that you can easily and wisely place, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restoration of those where there are splinters.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 Then he holds it, as will be explained later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	 And if there are broken pieces in the bone, extend it with two parts, if it is hand or foot, or hold it with your hand if it is a small limb, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	 and place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, you reset all the additions in their places as much as you can, and be careful not to cause the patient injury or pain with your work.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	 And feel it well with your hand if you think it is not well enough: ‌
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	 Si tu alignez bien la dresche, et ne la serrez pas trop fort, ni ne pressez pas comme font ceux qui causent par leur travail un abcès chaud et une contraction du membre, comme nous l'avons observé de nombreuses fois.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	 Et lorsque le membre est prêt, instruis bien le patient de ne pas le bouger, ni en éveil, ni en sommeil, ni en tournant ou d'une autre manière.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 Et veille à ce que le membre soit si solidement fixé qu'il ne ressente aucune douleur.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	 Car lorsqu'il ressent de la douleur, ce n'est pas suffisant, et il faut le placer dans une position où il ne ressent aucune douleur.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	 And take care that it is set straight, so that deformity does not occur when it is reset.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 And the quality of the broken member is as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	 Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	 For there are small members, such as arms and fingers and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	 so it is necessary to wrap them with soft and fine linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	 And those that are large, such as hips and legs: ️
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	 So it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and hard bandage, for the wide bandage embraces the entire large member and holds it evenly on all sides, so that there is no gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	 Then place light wadding around it, three or four turns according to the member, and tighten your hand a little all over the bandage, then go above the break and tighten less, so that the break is moved away from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	 And soften the ligament little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy place, then take the other ligament, and turn it back again on the broken place;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	 then return to the part below the break, and hold it moderately, not too strongly nor too gently, as we have said in the first turn above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 then put between the ligaments linen swabs or cloths, until it is all even, then bind everything above with the bandage, and then place your splints well on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	 And if there is swelling or abscess, put on something that eases the abscess and removes the swelling, and leave it so for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 then brace above your shoulders, and let them be half the width of a large cane, made wisely, or from wood used to make clefts, or from palm leaves, and let them be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	 but it is necessary that the brace placed above the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	 and let it also be as long as needed for the member, whether small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	 then brace above the braces as you did at first, then bind on top with a bandage, as in the first ligature over the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	 tighter is underneath, gradually less so.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	 and it is necessary that the bandages be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 because if the threads are thick, as I have seen the work of fools who make their laces from twisted flax cords, and this is a great mistake, for the lace cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not have between each star less than two fingers' width.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	 And if the patient is wounded by the tips of the stars after being drawn into healthy places, put underneath them wool or cloth scraps so that he does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	 When the wound is with a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will describe its treatment next.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	 And know that it is not appropriate to draw out all the stars from broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	 Because when the limb is large, it should not be put in stars larger than five or seven days, or more according to your security of the resulting abscess;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	 and see here the manner of old plasters for the restoration of breaks, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 and it is that you take flour that stays on the mill walls, and mix it with plenty of egg, and put this preparation, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring breaks in many ways, especially for women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold. ︎
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	 Another method of plaster for mending fractures, dislocations, and twists.
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	 Take aloe, ladanum, elecampane, asafoetida, gum arabic, and musk, in the amount of ten.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	 Myrrh and aloes, in the amount of five.
alechil VIIII З.;	 Garlic, seven.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	 Grind them into powder, and mix with egg white.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	 If the man's temperament is hot, then use this plaster, for it has a good composition and quickly mends broken bones, and is valuable to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	 Another method of plaster for twists:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	 Take musk and marshmallow, in the amount of ten.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	 Mirror and aloe, nine parts each.
acaice VI З.;	 Acaice, six parts;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Bolic Armenian, ten parts; and grind well, and mix with water or plenty of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	 Another method for emplaster on dislocated joints and displaced bones, and soothes the resulting pain, and heals bone fractures and breaks:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Take new wool, and moisten it in vinegar and cooked oil, and place on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This emplaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing hot abscesses and properly removes pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	 Another method of emplaster that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	 Take dried fig leaves and wild pansy leaves, and grind them together, and make an emplaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another method of emplaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to soften the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	 Take root of mallow, chamomile, flowers of violets, chickpea flour, one part each.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 And grind them together, and make an infusion with wine, and if the limb is hot, make the infusion with moist coriander water or plain water, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of plaster that is stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to restore the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	 Take roots of mallow, and seeds of flax, borage, melilot, and woodruff, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 And grind them together, and make an infusion with salt water or fresh water or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	 Ypocras says in his book that one should not place anything on a broken member to restore strength except for a salve made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	 And it seems that Galen says one should place on a broken member, to restore it, dry things that are slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and frankincense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	 Another plaster for injury and pain: 																														
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	 Take mallow and clipped men's hair, or bird feathers, and marshmallow, and salt equally, and crush them, and make a poultice and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	 Then, after that, loosen the poultice a bit, and check if the patient feels any pain, or if the bone has moved from its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	 If not, then do not remove it for several days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	 And if pain comes to the area, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry and remove it, and take away the poultice now.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	 And take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and dip it in water, and lift up the area, until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	 Then let the member rest for an hour, then place on a dry cloth, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind onto a knot, until you are certain of a hot abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	 and the inflammation of the member will rest, and the pain will be removed. Then begin again with a subtle binding, and a little poultice, and do not tighten it as much as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and make it subtle until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	 And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen, I have removed it all, and you need a plaster and a bandage, then start it again, as you did first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	 And if nothing happens to the member as we have said, do not unbind it until after three days or four or five or seven.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	 and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what is seen, until the fracture sets, and the connection of the flesh approaches.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	 Then you constrain it more than before, and you increase its flesh, as I have said earlier.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	 And if you see the place becoming drier than necessary, know that nutrition cannot come there;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	 Therefore, apply warm water dressing every time you dislocate it, which should be done every three days, and release the bandage a little;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	 By this work, then, nutrition comes to the limb, and quickly heals like what foolish doctors do, who return the twisted limb.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 This is bad, and it is a fearful work, and I see no other remedy than to leave it alone and to set it right.
des diverses manieres de brisure	 In various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	 There are many types of breaks, and diverse shapes, and the causes are different;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	 for it has breaks that are made by the strike of a sword, and the neck removes all the bone up to the marrow which is below the bone, as an axe or stick does;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 and therefore this manner of break is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	 where the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, and this manner of break is called "absolue";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	 and the wound from these two breaks is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	 And if there is an embedded strike, or a split from the blow of a stone, or from falling on stone, or from other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	 And if there is a breaking wound, which reaches up to the skin beneath the bone or on the bone itself, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	 And there is a wound that is confined within the bone as fine as a hair, and the fracture is small, therefore this break is called "capillary". 》
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	 and there is the wound that is made either by striking with a stone or by falling or something similar, which causes a fragment of bone to enter inside, and the place is swollen as blacksmiths do when they strike on cauldrons; 》
si entre li piere dedens.	 If between the stones inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	 And this happens more to those who have moist bones in the head, as in a child's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	 and it happens with all these types of breaks where small fragments are separated like stars;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	 and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	 And we recognize all kinds of fractures by their retraction on them, and the examination with tensors, and by the corrupt flesh that is upon it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	 The similarity to hair is known because when the bone is exposed and rubbed with it, the black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	 In the treatment of fractures, pay attention to the patient's accidents, and if you see any evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, distension, pallor, fever, and eyes coming out strong and red, and other similar things in many dispositions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	 And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	 And when the wounded person comes first to you, and this is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	 And if this is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh beneath the bone is not corrupted and the complications that we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	 And if the bone break reaches to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the split part like this:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	 and it is that you take the head of the wounded patient, and uncover on the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound as gently as you can, and if blood runs when uncovering the bone or an abscess like this, help him with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with cloths moistened in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	 And make the wound rest until the abscess is calmed, and be assured of the stoppage of blood;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	 Then begin to remove around the bone, and this is done according to two types of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 one manner is that you cut with a narrow incision in front, and it is called the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	 And then he puts another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	 And the second manner is that you have many different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and made of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	 and work lightly, so as not to harm the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	 And if the bone is tough and hard, you must bore around it before you administer incisions with drills, not so deep that they do not pierce through the bone of the skull, and there should be a margin or circle above the point to prevent it from piercing through the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	 And it is necessary for you to have several, so that each comes into its place in the width of the bone, so that you have pincers for all tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	 and this is the shape of the III types of pincers
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	 The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place one pincer on the bone, and turn with your two hands until you know that the bone is pierced.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	 then place the pincer elsewhere a little after, and do this all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw out the bone to your hand, or by some of the instruments that you have such as tongs, pincers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	 And take care that you do not touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	 And when you have pierced the bone and drawn it out, you must remove the splinter that remains of the bone with all similar instruments, resembling an awl, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other awl.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	 And if any small bones or scales remain, remove them lightly with an instrument.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 Then treat the wound with linens and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	 And the other way of working is that which Galen says is safer;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	 And he praises it greatly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	 It is first necessary that you uncover part of the bone where the fracture appears open, so that when you have uncovered this part, you will place under the head of this lenticular incision.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	 And do not cut from one side only, for the parts are sharp on both sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; xspace Et quant tu avras bien leu ce chapistre, et entendu les choses dessus diz, si te covient conoistre que li cervel porroit estre si perciet par II manieres.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	 Then strike with a small mallet from above, so that you lightly tap the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 If it is adherent to the bone, lightly scrape it off, for one can remove it well without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	 And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce through to the skin, and the bone is only cut slightly from above, and there are small pieces, then you must sharpen that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine scraper of which you should have various quantities, in order to administer in each place the most suitable one, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	 If you first use large scrapers, and then more subtle ones afterwards, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	 In each of the other subtle cuts or breaks, you must bring in a reason according to its nature;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	 and this is something that cannot be answered by someone who has studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	 And if the wound is exposed, then you must take a piece of linen according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	 Then take another double-layered cloth, either two or three times, wet it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	 and do this more lightly than you can, so as not to burden the patient, then administer another ligature on top, and do not tighten it too strongly, only enough to touch the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	 and leave it thus for a day or two, until the abscess has subsided, then remove the ligature, and administer medicines such as lily roots, vetch flour, incense powder, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	 and make a paste of these things, and place it on the wound, and continually administer moistening medicines without irritation.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	 and ensure that the wound is always clean, so that you do not leave any ointment on it, nor allow pus to gather, for when pus gathers on the cloth of the head, it will spread and fester, causing great harm to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 because when one applies a sharp object to the wound, it clots over.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	 Take heed therefore, if any bad accident befalls the patient, as we have said, then doubt is certain.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	 And if blackness occurs other than from the medicine that has been applied, and it has such power, then you must take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix them together to make a poultice;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then proceed with the treatment as required until it heals.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	 Know that sometimes both parts of the nose are broken, or only one alone, because these are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	 And below it is cartilage, and does not break; it does not cause any force to bow or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	 And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must insert your little finger or pierce through the nose, and place the breakage inside your index finger, and with your thumb outside, until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	 And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and the finger cannot reach it, then you must place a small amount of fat evenly at the end of a reed.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	 And if the break is in two parts, then do likewise, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when this swelling has subsided, then insert at the end of the nose some linen cloths, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	 When you push one bone against another, if there is a break
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	 and the ligaments are so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And some say that one should soak the bandages in butter, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	 It does not seem good to me, but they must be moistened in the preparation of an ointment made from egg and powdered myrobalan.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 then let the ligament alone until the bone is firm and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	 And sometimes one puts goose feathers in the nose instead of ligaments, and then there is a soft cloth around it, and the fracture holds, and the patient breathes through it.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	 or do whatever you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	 And if abscesses come to the nose while you are working there, put a poultice of oil rose or cotton soaked in aquilon on it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	 And if there are no abscesses there, then put a poultice on the outside, made from sesame flour and frankincense powder, mixed with egg ointment, then put light wadding on top, and do not bandage the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	 and if the fracture of the nose is small, and it is broken into many pieces, then apply suitable instruments to it, then sew up the split, and treat it with things that draw flesh, and bind it, such as suitable plasters and ointments.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat it with tents, and place lead pins in it until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	 From the dislocation of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	 When the jaw is dislocated beneath, and there is no wound outside of it, and the fracture is only outside, and it is not broken in two, then you recognize it easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	 It is necessary that if the fracture is on the right side, you place your index finger in the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	 and if the fracture is in the left jawbone, then place your index finger of the right hand, and push the fracture gently inside, and adjust it with the other hand from without, and make it equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	 And if the jaw fracture is in two pieces, it is necessary that you apply traction of two parts until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	 And if there is movement or loosening of the teeth, hold them in place with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then apply wax on the broken jaw, and put on a double cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	 And put on the cloth a well-made large bandage, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it at the top as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	 And if you see that the appearance changes, then untie it on the third day, and then reset to the place where it has changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	 And apply a plaster made of flour from the mill with plenty of egg or sesame paste, after you have removed the wax.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	 And put on a light wool bandage, and if the bandage tightens, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it heals.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	 Many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	 Et si apostemes se presentent, faictes ce que nous avons dit maintes fois.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	 And if there is a fracture and wound together, check to see if any piece of bone has been removed.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	 If it has been removed, use suitable instruments for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	 And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your needs.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you have removed all these pieces and none remain, then close the wound if it is wide, and apply suitable dressings to promote healing until it heals.
de la forcele	 of the splint
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	 The collarbone has broken several times before, near the shoulder, and the break is according to three types.
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	 Or it may be broken and separated into two pieces, with parts remaining, and this is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	 Or there may be a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	 And the work is so when the fracture is without wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the broken strength.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	 and the other extends the neck towards the part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	 then place the fracture evenly between your fingers, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor protrusion.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	 And if you need to extend more, place under the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, and let it be thick according to your necessity.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 and extend and lift the limb, and hold the sphere with your hand, so that you place the fracture evenly as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	 And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder out of the wound because it is deeply embedded, then it is necessary that the patient lie on their back, and place under the shoulder a small pillow, and let the assistant push the shoulder down until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	 And then bring the fracture to your fingers, and if you find it splintered, then it is necessary that you split open.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	 And draw out the bones lightly, and if the bone cannot join due to any swelling, then cut it with one of the chisels that you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	 but place under the trestle this instrument, to hold the bone in place:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	 and resembles a spoon, and is not pointed, and should be as wide as needed, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	 And it should have two heads, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, like the shape of the wound that you made when you drew out the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And when you are sure that the abscess is hot, then stitch up the wound, and if the opening is small or you doubt that the abscess is hot, then fill the wound with cloths and bandages according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	 And if there are abscesses here, then moisten the cloth with rose oil and asafoetida and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	 The squeezing of the bone, when it is without wounds and without a fracture, is that you place on the bone the poultice made from powdered millstone and egg white, and put light packing on top, and place a sphere under the seat if you need it.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	 then take a very wide bandage of one palm in width, then place two layers of cloth over the packing and the poultice.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	 then take a subtle strap three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the ends of the bandage hang down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	 and place the strap on the break, and turn the bandage up over the shoulder, and under the healthy seat, and under the unhealthy seat.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	 And there you reset each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the splint does not move above the broken bone, then you should check it every day, and when the ligament slackens, then you bind it again.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	 And make the patient lie on his back, and when he sleeps, place a small pillow under the shoulder to raise it up.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	 This will lighten the fracture of the collarbone by straightening the shoulder, where you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless a bad incident occurs, for up to twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	 Then begin the plaster again, if you see that it is necessary, and bind it and leave it so until he is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 And she is restored within twenty-eight days, and within fewer for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	 Of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	 It often happens that the shoulder breaks or tears in a large place and not in the middle, and it should be touched only by hand.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	 if you prepare it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	 then put on the place powder of millet with plenty of egg, and light stuffing, and put on a double cloth.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	 then put on a wide and fine bandage, somewhat wider than the shoulder, and if there are gaps under the bandage in any place of the shoulder, fill those gaps with linen stuffing so that the bandage sits evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	 And then secure it firmly with a large bandage, so that the bone does not move from its place, and examine the knot each day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	 And every time it loosens, secure it again and align the bone if it has shifted from its place, and have the patient lie on his side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	 And the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 And when this number is completed, release it, and be assured, for the bone does not easily dislocate again.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	 And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward, and touches under the heart, it breaks through, and removes it, and does what we have said in the breaking of the fortress to appease the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	 of the break of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	 The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 But it often breaks at the tip.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 And when it is broken in the middle, it shifts downward, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of breath, and fainting, and perhaps vomits blood, and opens the passage in the broken bone, and this can be felt well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	 And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on his back, and place one cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and bring the ribs of the two ribs towards each other with your hands, and use all means you can to align the bone as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	 then place over it plasters and wool on a thin salt sheet, or other light wood, and wrap it in one cloth, and bind it to the broken bone, so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	 and tie the bandage tightly around the back, and bind it properly, and check every hour to see if it is loosening, and if it does, then bind it again.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	 and if it is necessary to untie him, due to inflammation or itching that occurs at the site, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and untie him, and remove the plaster, and apply a treatment suitable for the condition.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then replace the plaster and bind it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	 Of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	 Know that the breaking of ribs occurs only in large places after the back, and inside the head, and they break only because they are slippery;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	 and one feels it well at the inquiry by two (methods).
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the treatment is that you set the fracture equal, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 And then apply a plaster, and bind it with a bandage, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	 And if the breaking of the ribs is directed inward, then the patient feels very great pain and pricking, as in pleurisy, because the bone pierces the flesh.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	 and breathes with difficulty, and soon vomits great plenty of blood, and this is of grave illness, and the ancients have placed great skill in it (i.e., treating it).
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	 And there are those who say that it should be administered food that swells the belly to expel the fracture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	 We do not do this, lest hot abscesses come, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	 And if they have come, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	 And some say that one should apply cupping glasses to the place, in order to suck strongly, and this seems reasonable. 》
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	 Toute voie, doubt has that the cupping glass may attract the superfluous fluids to the place due to the weakness of the dislocation.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	 And some say that the site should be covered with wool soaked in hot oil, and tents are placed between the ribs to make the bandage even all around, then it should be treated according to the treatment of pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	 And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone that punctures the flesh, and there is doubt on the part of the patient, it is necessary to incise upon the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put under an instrument to protect the liver.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then one should saw the bone, and pull gently, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat with poultices until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	 And if such abscesses come, place dampened cloths in rose oil on them, and put on the place.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And treat the place as one would an abscess, and let it lie quietly on the side where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	 of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	 Sometimes there is a break in the bones of the neck, and often it bends;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	 and similarly to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, then observe whether you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that he is mortally wounded in many parts, and if he moves them and feels well when they are strained and pricked, know that the bone joint is saved, and that the patient will be cured, provided that one applies treatment there.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	 And if something similar happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healed or not, take note whether the feet are numb, and if there are accidents in the hands, and on the back a swelling and involuntary urination;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 and when it is laid on its belly, there is involuntary urination.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it is turned onto its back and wants to sit up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	 Know that it is fatal;
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 If he does not work diligently in his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	 And if this accident does not happen to him, then the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	 And the treatment is such that you should apply a hot poultice if there is heat in the abscess, and place on top of it rose oil or egg yolk oil until it is appeased.
