puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	 Then apply one of the comforting and drying poultices, and tie it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And do not sleep on that part where he feels the pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	 And if any bone breaks, it should be covered with wax.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And remove the bone, then join together the two lips of the wound with a stitch if it is large, and treat it with a flesh-forming ointment until he is healed.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	 and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the shoulder head", place your thumb of your left hand into it, and make it equal to the other hand by your power, then put the plaster and bandage on top, if you need it;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 then hold it steady, and if there are any bone splinters, they should be removed, and heal the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	 of the breaking of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	 It happens sometimes that the hip bone may be broken, and if it is, there will only be a little weakening at the top.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	 and it breaks longwise, and declines to one side, and the patient feels pain in that place, and bruising, and swells as if broken. ➤
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	 And the treatment is such that you extend your hand over it, until you are above the break.
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	 and know what the fracture and its appearance are;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	 and if the fracture is only in the head, then set this fracture so that it is of natural appearance.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	 And if the break is lengthwise, or slants towards the inside, then make the patient lie on their stomach, so that you may prepare to restore that break.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	 And when you have set it equal, then apply the plaster, then place a splint of wood or horn over it, and bind the fracture so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	 and support the place under the ribs, until the limb is level.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	 And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	 And if any abscesses appear there, do not touch them until the abscesses are healed, and then apply what we have said before.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	 And then return to the restoration, and hold it as needed, if there is no bad outcome.
et c’est li maniere.	 And this is the way (to do it).
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	 of the shoulder fracture
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	 The shoulder is that which is between the arm and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two ways.
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	 The first way is that you take a stick full of medium thickness, according to this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	 And tie at the two ends two strings, and pull them up, and make the patient sit on a seat.
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	 Then you throw the broken arm over the stick, until it reaches the armpit, and in the middle there is a curve of the stick, then pull up some heavy thing that the attendant extends downward.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	 Then the doctor should place the splint evenly against his hands together, so that the splint returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	 And another way is that one makes the patient lie on his back, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two attendants, one to hold what is above the break in his hands, and the other to hold below all the cord, and each extends at its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you see that the extraction is stronger, then hold the ligament below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the limbs to its side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	 And if the splint is near the shoulder's head, it is necessary that you place one string under the armpit, and another towards the side, under the splint.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	 and thus if the splint is towards the side, it is necessary to place a string lightly, without difficulty, so that the splint is even on the place and on the side.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 Then make the splint even as it should be, and bandage it, if any abscesses come there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	 And if such abscesses come there, do not bandage it until the seventh day, and place a wet cloth on vinegar and rose oil, until those abscesses are calmed.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	 Then he holds it, and the manner of holding is that you place the bandage on the fracture, then assemble the arm onto the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	 And place the cloth and hold onto the shoulder and the arm, so that the arm is in the proper position, unless something prevents it or the bone is not set.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	 And if you doubt that the bone is not set, use splints, and place on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than others, and there should be between each splint two fingers' width, and each splint should be so large that it passes beyond the fracture by three fingers' width on either side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	 Then hold it up to the stars, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on fractures, stronger and less slanted.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	 And if you see the base of the bones and the holding as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, leave it to bind until the seventh day, as we have said;
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 then check the bandage every three days to ensure that itching or swelling does not occur in the area, and that the nursing cannot reach the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If you accept it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	 And if no such incident occurs, do not unbind it before three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	 and place under the shoulder a pillow filled with wool equally, and check each hour of the day or night that the position of the broken limb does not move, nor is the ligament softened;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	 if he receives it by the power of medicine, and give him the food that we have mentioned before, in such a way that the food is first finely prepared;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 and when he begins to recover, let it be thicker.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	 And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be taken for forty days in total;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 and then one must unbind and administer baths and ointments to heal the place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the constriction is ugly and clogged, it takes one day or two months to unclog.
de la brisure du bras	 of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	 The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "dui foscile", one of which is small and follows the elbow;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	 And the other is large, and this one is below, towards the little finger.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	 By chance, only the large tendon breaks, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	 When the small tendon is broken, the restoration is easy, and so is the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 And when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more serious than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is only the small fuscille that is broken, one should extend it lightly and make it equal.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	 And if it is the large tendon, it must be stretched more tightly;  /> Et se c'est li petis, il n'i covient pas tant grant force;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	 And extend it on the pillow, and raise the heel of the hand higher than the others, and the little finger lower than the other fingers, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the pillow in front of him higher, so that the patient does not endure any effort.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 Then extend one of your arms to the lower part under his hand or at the wrist, and another minister above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 Et puis, remets-le en place le chirurgien, selon la meilleure forme possible.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	 Et si, dans une fracture où il y a des fragments, alors remets chaque fragment à sa place; et s'il y en a un qui dépasse et touche le cœur, et que tu ne peux pas le ramener à sa place, fends-le et retire-le, comme nous l'avons dit précédemment.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	 And if there is a fracture with a wound, I have spoken about it in a specific chapter;
si pren la cure.	 then take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	 And if in the beginning of the treatment such abscesses appear, then apply a cloth of plaster made of rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard nor too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 and delicately place the cloth on top until those abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	 And then remove the plaster and apply the poultice of milled powder with plenty of egg, then put on the bandages, and let the bandage on the fracture be always stronger, and a little wider than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	 And know that it must have six stars or ribs on the arm in various positions.
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	 whether the break is in one of the bones, or in two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	 and press more on the break than elsewhere, and always less while pulling, as I said at the beginning of the chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	 and let the rags that are on the break be soft and moist, and not hard or rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 and let the thread, with which it is tied, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And wrap the limb and the tendon after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	 And if any bad thing happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must rinse the limb with hot water until that itching is calmed.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And let the member not rest too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then begin the splinting again, and if the tendon is weakened and the bone dislocated, or similar things, treat it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	 And if you take precaution that the nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it in a pot, and leave it thus for some days until the nourishment can pass through, and then splint it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things happens to the patient, do not release him until 20 days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	 or in which case, he should place his hands around his neck, and let his neck be equal on both sides, and guard against movement and shifting, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 and know that this fracture is healed in thirty or thirty-five days, and perhaps even twenty, according to the composition and complexion of the body's humors.
de la brisure de la main	 Of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	 Know that in the back of the hand and at the fingers there are few breaks, and it only happens that there is often a sprain.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	 And when a plant [i.e., bone] of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient sit cross-legged, and sit straight in front of himself equally;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	 then place his hand on the stretched table, and let the minister straighten the broken bones, and let the doctor set them evenly until they are well joined;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	 And put the poultice and bandages on it, if there are no abscesses, then apply a compress according to the size of the wound.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	 And let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	 And if the break is around the waist near the lower belly, make a sphere of cloths and instruct the patient to tie it to his broken part.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	 And then bind it with a long cloth, and let the compress be made of soft kersey as large as the palm of the hand, and bind it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	 And if the break is in the hand, you must place a bandage on top and another below the hand so that the fingers are open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and make the knot between the two fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	 And if the break occurs in one of the fingers, whether it is sprained or dislocated, set it straight as needed.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	 And hold it with the sole of the foot, and if you see this, place a small straight splint to lift the fracture, and do not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	 And if the break is in another toe, such as in the big toe or one of the others, place it evenly, and bind it with the sound toe that follows.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	 Or tie them all together in a single bandage, whatever works, or place a splint on top, as with the foot.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	 And take care in the restoration and positioning of a hot abscess, and secure it with what comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	 Of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	 The thigh bone is often broken, and this is evident when the leg turns in front or behind;
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	 And its restoration is such that one ligament is tied above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	 And let the patient lie on his back, then each assistant should extend their ligament to its equal part;
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	 and this is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then let one ligament be towards the knee, and the other ligament below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	 And also if it is near the knee, then let the ligament be by the knee, and let the extension be downwards.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 Then let the surgeon align the bone with his two hands so that it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster and bind it, if pus does not come out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	 And if there is hot pus, let it quiet down first before returning to your work and treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	 The ligature is made in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	 It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture I bandage thick and double in II or III, and remove any excess, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the base of the big toe, and pass a long thread between the thigh and the leg, near the knee below, and let the ends of the thread come out above;
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	 then turn the bandage around the leg and the thigh, then place splints on the fracture, and place a splint on the bone of the leg;
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	 then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to make the splint equal in size, then begin to tie firmly III or IV turns on the fracture;
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	 And as one goes higher towards the fracture, it strains less;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	 Then thread two knots in the thread that you have passed between the thigh and the leg, and tie three knots that are above, then return below to the head of the thread, until you come near the foot.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 And it strains so that it does not move from its place; then leave it thus, for if there comes no abscess or swelling or other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	 And if it happens, then unbind it, and address what comes as we have said many times.
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	 And if there are bone fragments that protrude, they must be removed, if possible.
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	 And if it cannot be done, then the site must be split and pulled strongly.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	 And sometimes the thighbone is broken like a splinter, as in the shoulder and arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	 nevertheless, in such restoration, the patient does not become lame.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	 And know that the thigh is restored in five days, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	 from the cavity of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Saiches que en la ruelle du genouil advient peu de fracture, mais elle ploie souvent.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 Et s’elle brise, si n’est que d’une fente, ou une perte, et il advient à toute plaie, et sans plaie, et cela se sent bien.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	 And the restoration is like placing equal that which is round to its two sides, so that it can be joined together.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	 then apply the plaster, and put a round splint in it if needed, and secure it as required, then follow all the arrangements that we have said for other fractures, such as abscess and others.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 treat each injury with what is needed until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	 Of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	 Know that in the leg there are two bones. One is called by its right name "mustelz," and the other is called "foscile.
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 And there is the same break as in the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as for the arm, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	 And if the small bone is broken, it will turn to the front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	 And if the larger bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is clearly visible;
et torne desoz.	 and it turns downwards.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	 Then apply traction, and make it even, and bind the splints equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	 however, if the break is ugly and there are several fragments, then traction should be lesser and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 And align according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	 And when you have completed your work, take two strips of wood shavings that wrap around the leg on both sides, and let them be as long as the leg from the knee downwards.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	 Then wrap the two of them with one bandage on top and another below, and tie it in the middle as well. And at this point the leg will not be able to decline to the right or to the left, and thus it is well.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	 And some apply splints along the length of the leg, and it is made of wood, and one puts the leg in it to prevent movement. Properly done, this is for a fracture where there is a wound.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	 And move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or other incident.
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the cure is such that it may heal.
de la brisure des os dou piet	 Of the breaking of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	 At the ankle there is no breaking, but sometimes the bones of the foot break and the two heels, and in this case it is only splintering in several directions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	 And if there is a break in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones rising above one another, then put the patient's foot on the ground as if he wanted to walk, and then place your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press until they return to their places;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	 Then place the dressing and wool on top, and under the sole of the foot put a small board with two full nails, then fasten it securely to the foot, after which you wrap bandages around, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	 And when three days or four have passed, then unbind the ligament, for you will find the bones equal, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	 And if there are any broken fingers, restore them, just as we have said for the fingers of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	 Then place a splint on the broken finger according to its length, and let it be a little wider, then place beneath the foot the table that I have mentioned, and bind firmly.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	 and if there are two or three, or more, broken fingers, then place a splint on each finger according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and bind the table beneath the foot;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	 and let it stand on top of the table, beyond the foot's belly, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	 And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	 And assist each incident as needed.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	 of the fracture of the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	 When the woman's natural bones are broken, have her sit upright, then lean her towards the back, and let her be held from behind.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	 Then fill the woman's natural cavity with cotton, and put in as much as needed.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	 Then have the woman stand up and lift her back little by little, and then the cotton will jump out until it reaches the entrance of the vagina, and the bone will return with the cotton.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	 And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven days or more.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	 Thus the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and attach a cord to its opening, and insert all of it into the vagina.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	 Then blow into the cannula strongly, until the bladder is inflated inside.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	 the nature will return to the fracture;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then fill it with cotton, and leave it thus for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	 And when the bone of a man's or woman's fist is broken, restore it as we have said for the hip bone;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 and these nearby fractures are not hidden from those who put their effort and skill into it, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	 For the fracture indicates in several situations the correct path to restoration:
enten le donques.	 understand it then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	 In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and insert the penis into it;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	 Then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for three days wrapped thus, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	 of break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	 It is necessary for someone who has a break with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the thigh bone or shoulder bone or similar, to be bled now, just like the bleedings we have mentioned testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the wound is healthy, then seal it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, and then begin to restore the fracture in that same hour or that day, unless an abscess forms there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	 And if an abscess forms there, then wait until the ninth day to resume treatment, until the abscess subsides, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	 And if the broken bone is protruding through the skin, it is necessary that you gently grasp it with your hands and apply slight traction.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	 And if the extensions are not prepared to be equal to your hands, then reset it with this iron instrument which has seven or eight teeth, and its width is according to the size of the wound.
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	 And for this reason it is necessary for the physician to have three or four [of these instruments], according to what he needs in each wound treatment.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	 And let it be round and slightly thick, so that it does not bend at the pressure on the member during your work, and let it be pointed in front, and thick from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	 And it is called "palainche," which is why the curved head must be placed on top of the visible bone.
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 and it should be struck once, so that it returns, and is equal one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot well take the bone, then it is necessary that you cut off the head of the bone, so that the instrument has control over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	 And if you cannot bring back the bone as we have said, then strike it with a suitable instrument for this purpose, either a scalpel or scissors, according to your ability;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	 then remove the bone fragments and small splinters that remain in the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	 Do this until it is in its place, then moisten the bandage in black stiptic wine, and properly if it is summer.
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	 and do not put any ointment or other greasy substance on the wound, as it will cause rotting and corruption.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	 Then administer stitches when you have reset the bone, and leave the wound open, and cut the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and be sure that the wound is not constricted with the fracture;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	 And many times have foolish physicians done this, causing the patient to either die or be crippled.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 And let the constriction be softer and gentler than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that evil occurrences may happen as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it is not necessary to apply stitches there.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 But instead of stitches, bind hard cloths around it and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one day or two that the wound is swelling, remove everything you have put on it at once, and apply a healing ointment to the wound, such as tetrapharmacon or similar ointments.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	 And you must unbind the limb two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	 And it is necessary that the limb be arranged in such a way that the swelling runs downwards lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	 And if many days pass and it cannot heal but rather swells again, know that there are small bone fragments causing the wound to swell and bringing this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula forms at the site, or another type of corruption occurs, you must treat it according to what is said in the previous chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	 And when the bone is broken and protrudes from the limb, such as the thigh or shoulder bones, and other similar large limbs, do not pull it out, for many times this causes death, but leave it until it rots.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	 Perhaps it will fall out by itself after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 and if you cannot, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	 Of the bruises that come upon the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	 We often see good health after the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it is an ugly sight to see the limb's condition;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	 and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	 Take care, therefore, if the bone is fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	 If you administer to him medicines that are styptic, such as aloes, incense, myrrh, sarcocolle, and similar others, in the manner that you take some of these things, or all together, and boil them with styptic wine, or with an abundance of egg, or with oil;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	 And place them on the wound in cloths, and bind it well, and do not unbind it for many days;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	 And then unbind it, and begin again another, until the knotting is removed;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	 Or you bind onto a well-made plate of lead.
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	 For the property of lead is such that it removes all swelling from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	 And if the knotting has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then scrape off its surface, and make the superfluous part evident.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 You shall have it rasped by some rasp until it is removed, and the wound cared for until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	 of the limb that is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	 When the bone fracture is repaired, but afterwards the limb remains weak and delicate, it happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	 one of which is because it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	 or because there were too many bindings, and the nourishment could not reach the limb.
ou por multitude d’arosement;	 or because of excessive bleeding;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	 or because of too great movements, not at the right time.
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	 or because he has little blood in his body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	 And the care is such that you make the patient eat and soften the body until the blood is increased in him.
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	 And give the patient a bath, and bring him joy and happiness;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	 then apply pitch to the limb, so that the pitch draws out much pus, and wash it often with cold water, until the pus flows from the limb;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	 and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	 of the twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	 When the limb is twisted after being set, and the broken bone is visible, and the shape of the limb is unsightly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	 do not believe those fools who say that one should break the limb anew, and many foolish physicians have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	 and these actions are blamed, and great harm comes from it, and perhaps death.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	 Nevertheless, if the swelling and inflammation are recent, it is necessary that they be bathed in hot water, or herbs with a softening effect should be boiled, such as mallow leaves, roots, and melilot, and similar things.
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	 And he makes a softening poultice, such as well-made diquilon, and you take the mucilage of mallow, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and apply the poultice on top.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	 Or you take fatty figs, and grind them with bran of flax, and similar medicines that reduce the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes the dislocation is removed by continually and for a long time rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And let there be gentle movement to the limb each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	 And if the swelling is old and hardened, like stone, and needs to be removed with an iron instrument, then it must be shaved down to the bone with a fine, sharp knife.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	 And put prudence and diligence in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	 Here begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	 Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	 When dislocation happens to someone, it must immediately be reset without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	 For if one delays, the place swells, and perhaps it is only with great difficulty that it can be reset to its place;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	 because it is not fitting that one moves it at the hour when it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	 many times it brings on cramp and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	 nevertheless, when this happens, have the patient bleed, then leave them until the inflammation has subsided;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 then foment the limb with hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each member as it returns to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	 And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	 of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	 Rarely do both jaws become dislocated at the same time, and the dislocation of both is according to two methods:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	 And they are slightly removed from their places, and softened a little.
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	 and they are completely dislocated, hanging down towards the chest, and saliva runs from his mouth so that he cannot hold it back or close his mouth, and his tongue is tangled with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	 When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself through many positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	 And if it [the dislocation] is complete and accomplished, then you must reset it immediately, without delaying at all;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	 and in such a way that the attendant holds the patient's head, and the practitioner places his little finger of one hand into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	 and the other two fingers are placed evenly.
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And instruct the patient to soften them, his jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	 And the physician should set it right, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	 And if the relocation is difficult, especially if it involves both jaws together, soak them in hot water and oil until they can be easily reset.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	 Do not hesitate to reset them, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	 And when they are reset equally and the patient's mouth closes well without swelling, place moistened cloths in a plaster made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bands.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	 And let the patient sleep on their back with their head between two pillows so that they do not move to the right or left, nor should they try to speak, but rather eat light food until the pain has passed and the jaws have healed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And then he chews what he wants lightly, and does not exert himself to open his mouth for eating or drinking, as long as the jaw is well tied and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	 And if the two mandibles cannot be set right within an hour, and are not returned to their places, then fever and sudden illness may follow, and perhaps intestinal discharge, and possibly pure bile will be vomited.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	 And when you see this, then know that it is a loss;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	 and many times he dies who experiences this, within nine days.
de la forcelle	 of the jawbone
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	 The jawbone cannot dislocate from the inside or from the foot, and sometimes it dislocates downward, which is easily felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	 And the restoration is such that the patient often lies on his back and stretches out his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	 and then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	 then apply the plaster and bandage, and bind it tightly.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	 and the joint that is towards the knife cannot dislocate;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	 if not, and if it dislocates any time, then reset it to its place, as we have said.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then put on the plaster and bandage it, and bind it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And thus the same thing happens with the dislocated shoulder when it is removed from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	 Of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	 Know that the shoulder can be dislocated in only three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	 one of which is when it dislocates toward the lower part of the armpit;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	 and the second is toward the side of the chest;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	 and perhaps it dislocates toward the upper part, which happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	 and it does not dislocate backward behind the shoulder, nor inward toward the nerves;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	 and often it dislocates downward toward the armpit, especially for those who have little flesh, because then it moves quickly. xspace
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 to those who have enough flesh, barely, and it enters barely.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	 And sometimes it happens to some men that they experience bruising or fracturing, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated for this reason.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	 Therefore, you must examine it until you are certain.
et adonques encomence la cure.	 And then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	 The dislocation is known when it falls towards the shoulder blade, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	 And you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the scapula at the armpit the top of the shoulder, as if it were an egg.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	 And the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move in any way.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	 And also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you can clearly see it in the armpit.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 et cette manière de dislocation n'est pas facile à remettre en place lorsqu'elle est nouvelle, ou si l'enfant est malade.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	 And the manner is that the servant takes the patient's hand up high, then places his fingers underneath the axilla, and lifts the joint with force up to its place.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	 And the servant lifts the hand and extends it upward, then places it below.
si venra hastanment.	 Then it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	 And if it does not come as we have said in the hand within several days afterward, then the patient must be bathed in hot water.
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	 And let the servant make a softening and soothing mixture, such as a decoction of hollyhock, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and apply it.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	 then the patient should be placed on his back, and under the armpit a pad of wool should be put, not too soft nor too hard, then the physician should place his heel on the pad, and lift the shoulder head skillfully, and pull the patient's hand;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	 and another assistant should hold the patient's head so that it does not move downward;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	 then the shoulder returns immediately, and if you see this, you should reset it in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	 and it is necessary that a man be present who is larger than the patient;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	 and he should stand straight towards the patient's side, and place his shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit up high, so that the patient hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And another minister draws the patient's hand down towards the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too light, then have him hold something heavy with him, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	 And it is reset in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	 and it is done by driving a long stick into the ground, so that the head is as round as a fist, neither too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	 then it should be placed under the patient, but let there be soft cloths on top, and the patient should stand along the length of the stick; xspace
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	 then his hand should be stretched down on the other side, and the joint will quickly return to its place.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	 And if it does not want to return through all these things that we have said, then perform this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 Take a stick of two arms' length and four finger-breadths wide, which has a round head to enter deeply under the shoulder blade, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	 then place the pole on top of the patient's head, under a drape, so that the pole does not hurt the patient, then put it underneath the patient's backside;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	 and extend the other arm along the length of the pole, and place the shoulder on the pole, and the arm at the top of the hand, then put the arm on the rung of a wide ladder, and let the hands hang down, and let the body hang freely from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	 now the joint returns to its place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	 And when it is inside, in whatever manner it may be, you must place under the seat an equal sphere of wool, then apply the prepared plaster of powdered millstone, with incense and egg white, over the entire shoulder and around it, then tie it securely under the seat, and wrap the bandage over the plaster, and hold the hand to its neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	 And it is necessary that he rests a little, until the member is comforted, for it will heal more quickly;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	 and then rests more afterwards for five or seven days, and moves it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	 And if it is closed and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, it is necessary that you apply three cauteries, as it is explained in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	 And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not hold and cannot raise its arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened;
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	 and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	 The dislocation that is towards the foot, and the hips, or the back, is done by pushing, and stretching of hands, and another remedy is applied there;
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and it is treated until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	 And if after healing there is stiffness in the limb and slowness of movement, then the patient should take a bath many times until that stiffness is alleviated, and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	 of the dislocation of the rib
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	 Know that the dislocation of the elbow is dislocated by points, and returns by points;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	 And if it has dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, the dislocation is not repaired, because one can see and feel it well.
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	 And dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 Et when you join the sick coute with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is cut, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	 And you must reset it before any abscess forms there, for if an abscess forms, it would be difficult to set back.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	 And perhaps it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is at the rear;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	 It is worse than other dislocations and causes greater pain, and death may occur.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	 And the restoration is such that when it can be set back, you should extend its hand with both your hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	 and his arms should be spread, and the hands of the surgeon according to the bone around, above and below, and press the joint together with his thumbs or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	 Et si the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes with the root of the palm where it is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	 And if it does not wish to return to its place, administer a strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	 and let two assistants extend the arm, and hold it still with two assistants, so that it does not move during the extension.
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	 then turn the arm in all directions, after you have wrapped a long and wide double cloth around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	 and when the surgeon has brought the joint together with his hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then press the joint strongly until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 and when it is in place, put on a dry bandage with some egg, and hold it firmly, and tie the arm to the patient's neck, and leave it for some days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	 And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage and leave it;
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	 And if you see that the joint does not hold well, then begin again with the bandage and the band, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set.
puis le deslie.	 Then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	 And if the patient feels stiffness after the joint has been set and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is eased.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	 or you place on the joint a greasy piece of sheep's wool, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make it enter the bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	 and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the wool back on, and then enter the bath;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and do this two or three times, until it is healed.
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	 and if you see, then put on moistened cow dung heated with butter, and bandage it up;
si revenra a sa disposition.	 it will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	 The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	 The joints of the hand are dislocated, and their relocation is light, more than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	 However, it must be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour that it is dislocated, so that the place does not swell, or a hot abscess develops. 》
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	 And the restoration is that you place the afflicted hand on a table, and the minister extends his hand, and the physician places it equally, so that he places his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	 However, you must check if it is properly in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 Then the patient should place the back of his hand on a table for extension and restoration.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and the physician should place his hand on that part of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	 If it returns now, that is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If not, then apply soothing plasters for such abscesses, and leave it thus without repeating the process.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	 And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then the joint remains dislocated; ️
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	 And do not cause any harm to the patient further than the hand is wet, and cannot grasp anything at all:
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	 then know that the nerve has been cut or the artery.
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 if there is no other means than to grasp by cautery near the wound, and perhaps it serves no other purpose.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	 And when the hand is in place, apply the poultice we mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then unbind and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he cannot move it well and there is stiffness, then moisten it with hot water and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	 of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the wrist.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	 then extend the fingers and push the dislocation back towards you until it returns, then support the head of the finger and turn it towards the part where it is dislocated.
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	 and leave it for two days, and then set it straight on the third day;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	 And of night the ligament, as we have said, and unbinds by day, and makes it move, and binds it again at night;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated at the wrist of the hand, and act as you have done before, until it is healed.
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 And do the same when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	 Of the dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	 When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, if there are several dislocations, there is no treatment, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	 And the sign is that the excretion jumps out without willpower, and one cannot hold it in, and often some member becomes soft, whether the two thighs or the two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	 And often the spine moves in four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	 that which moves at the back is called "scoliosis":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	 The remedy is such that you treat if the curvature has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 there is no cure or healing for the whole of it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	 And those that come from falling or striking or similar things, the ancients speak of cures in great words where there is not always great benefit;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have made instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	 I say that in the curvature that comes in the chest, there is no skill or healthiness;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	 and also that which comes straight into two ribs, and one cannot cure except for the one that comes directly to the back, as I say.
