et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	 and is such that the patient should be stretched out on his back in one equal place, and have support under him, so that he does not injure himself.
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	 then drive a stake firmly into the ground at the head, and another at the feet, and tie one rope under the patient's ankles, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	 and two assistants should hold the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 and ensure that the stakes are securely in place, as we have said, and let the physician place his palms firmly on the spine until it returns [to its original position].
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	 And if it does not return to its original position with this treatment, then take a board three arms long, and place it under the patient's back, and let the patient be on their side, and push the end of the board under the back, then put the middle of the board on the spine; pgfqpoint
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	 And let the physician place his feet on the other end of the table, and press firmly until it returns to its place.
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if you see it happen, do the same at the shoulder that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	 And it is that you place two faggots at the head of the patient, one on each side of the body, and between each faggot, above and below, there should be a hand's breadth of space.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	 And let there be in each faggot a hole, where the shoulder fits, and let the faggots be firmly in the ground, so that they do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	 And between each of the two faggots, there should be a rotating faggot, on which the rope turns, and for the two turnings, there should be two small faggots the length of a hand, to turn the shoulder.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And then have the patient lie down with a ligature between their legs at the tourniquet towards the head, and the other ligature towards the feet at the other tourniquet, and each of the assistants turn their tourniquet for the entire ligature, and the master should place the spindle evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And when it is even, place a desiccating poultice with plenty of egg, and then the bandages, and then a strip from a board three fingers long, which should cover the area of the swelling and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a ligature, as we have said, and let the patient use delicate nursing until they are healed;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	 And if something happens at the end of the treatment, then it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, along with the poultice that we have mentioned before;
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	 And sometimes one administers a piece of lead, and sometimes it appears at the back of the spine, and one thinks that this is a dislocation;
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	 and it is the bone that has broken through, which is why one should not have any presumption about it:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 by chance it could bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	 of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	 Know that at the hips and shoulders, only dislocation occurs, not like in other joints;
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	 and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	 Inside and outside, front and back;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	 And more inside than elsewhere, hardly dislocates in front or behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	 And the sign of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer and more open is the patient's knee than the healthy one, and the patient cannot double his knee to the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the place that is nearby is swollen with abscess is hot, because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	 And the sign of that which comes to pass, so it is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	 And the sign of the one in front is that he stretches his leg according to its length;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	 yet he does not double his knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot go forward, and holds his urine, and the ankle swells, and when walking, he walks on his heels.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	 And the sign of that which comes to pass behind, so it is that they cannot spread their knee, nor double it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the hip bone is in the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	 The remedies for this type of dislocation are such that you should consider if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its position, then there is no treatment.
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	 And it is not necessary for him to have any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	 And in that where the dislocation is fresh, and this occurs in four ways of dislocation, then you must hurry to return the joint, and push it inside and outside, and move it to the right and left.
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	 Perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is necessary.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	 And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare a strong assistant, and strongly support the leg with two hands, or with one hand that is tied above the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	 And another assistant extends his hand over it in such a manner that he places his hands under the cushions, then binds with a soft bandage on the thigh;
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	 and another holds the end of the bandage.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And they pull upwards and downwards all at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground all at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	 This method of extension is common in four ways; if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	 If not, then it is necessary to take care of its appearance.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	 When the dislocation is at the shoulder, it is necessary that you place the patient on his healthy side, then put the bandage at the root of the thigh, and the place that is under the armpit, then pull the bandage up towards the armpit, and towards the chest;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	 Then let another assistant take his arms, and embrace the thick part of the sick thigh, and stretch it firmly.
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	 now it will return to its place;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 and this manner of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	 And if you cannot secure it in this manner as we have said, then you must bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong, soft band around both ankles and both knees, and let the sick leg be extended two fingers' width more than the other.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	 then let it be hung over the top of a beam, and let it be two arms' length above the ground;
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 then instruct one assistant to embrace the top of the thigh, and let another assistant hang with the patient, who should embrace the thigh firmly, because the joint returns quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	 Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides,
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	 Et li maistres le retaigne par dessus sus le col, et en ceste maniere deveint li malaides sanz aucune dolor.
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 Et quant il est a point, si le ramoine en ceste maniere: il tient l’olle par dessus, et les cuixes entre ses bras, si les distent tant qu’il voit que li malaides ad son membre tout reteigne; puis le fait asseoir sus sa lite, et lui met II coussins sous la teste, et II autres sur la jambe, puis un autel sous les piez, et l’olle et les cuixes il li enlace, et ainsi le tient une heure ou II au plus.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place him on the table and press it as we have said in the case of dislocation, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	 And when the dislocation is forward, then it is necessary to extend the injured leg quickly, as I have said.
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	 And let the doctor apply his strength to be on the injured shoulder, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	 And if the dislocation is backward, then it is not necessary to extend the injured one downwards or lift it off the ground, but rather it should be as if the hip were dislocated backward, as we have said about lying on two hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	 And let him be on his back, and the strap extended as we have said before, and one should press on the joint at the table.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	 And it will be perfect when the patient extends his legs, and they will be equal.
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	 then draw together the thighs, and apply a poultice, and hold it in place with a bandage, so that the hip does not move.
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	 and let him rest for three or four days, then unbind him, and apply another poultice on top;
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	 and if you see that they are equal, then bind as before, and leave it for three days.
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 then unbind him, and let him walk gently, until the limb is healed.
de la dislocation dou genoil	 of the knee dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	 The knee is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	 that is to say, inward and outward, and backward. ‌
et ne desalue point devant.	 And do not dislocate beforehand.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	 And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it does not adhere to his thigh, know that he is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	 And the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his face, and put his foot on top of your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	 then take his knee in your palms, and pull it between your thighs, then strongly bend the two sides of the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	 and another assistant extends his foot, so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he adheres his leg to his thigh lightly.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	 And put the poultice on, and make the leg adhere to the thigh, and bind them together strongly for three days or four, then unbind.
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And let the patient not exert himself in walking, until the limb is healed.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not at all, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	 of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	 The ankles are sometimes swollen and sometimes completely dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	 And the sign is that the ankle is swollen and protrudes forward towards the dislocated part:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 The resetting should be gentle, and it should be gently extended at its hands when only slightly moved.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	 And when it is fully dislocated, you should make the patient sit up straight and have one assistant hold the leg by the foot, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	 Then pull the foot towards yourself with your right hand, then with the left two times, then extend it upwards and nicely push the foot up;
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	 And do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot.
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	 If it returns, that is good;
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	 if not, then begin the work again, for it will return.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	 and if it cannot return thus, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and drive one strong stake firmly into the ground between his thighs, and tie cloths around [it], so that it does not hurt the patient.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	 then let one servant take hold of the thigh, and another servant extend the foot to his hands or with one band, which he ties above the ankle;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	 then let each servant pull equally, and let the stake be always between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when [he] is stretched.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 Then let the physician set the dislocation evenly with his hands, and another assistant hold the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	 And when it is perfectly set, apply the bandage and padding on top, bind it very tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and protect the nerves that are above the ankle in the back, so that the binding is not too tight;
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	 then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandage softens, bind it again.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	 Then unbind on the third or fourth day, and advise the patient not to walk for four days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And if he goes before that time, it is not certain that he will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if abscesses come here, you must soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	 of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	 When the fingers are dislocated, they must be stretched nicely without effort, and this is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	 And if the dislocation is in any node of the back or foot, you must make the patient sit on a plain place or on a table completely straight, and put your foot on what opens from these joints, then press with your foot strongly until it returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	 And when it is level and nothing opens, place under the foot a board with two legs, then press strongly, and leave it for three days, then release.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	 Of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	 When a wound comes with the dislocation and one wants to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	 If you are not learned in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and patient, do not be bold. xspace
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	 And use at first things that calm a hot abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands if you see no hope of health.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	 And when you see hope, reset the limb to its place immediately before the hot abscess grows there;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	 And when the limb is in place, administer things that calm hot abscesses and treat the wound as needed with dried onions.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	 And if there is also a fracture with the dislocation and small bones are shattered, remove them and do what we have said in simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 And guard yourself from entering into fear, as I have said, for this will move you according to your Creator and for the safety of your weapon and body.
